Hanafi Distance Measures for Travel Concessions
Defines units of distance relevant to travel concessions (qasr, tayammum, etc.)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hierarchy of Hanafi distance units from the smallest (barleycorn) to the largest (barid) and apply the conversion factors to determine travel distances for sharia concessions.

Core Idea
Sharia distance measures are precisely defined from barleycorn to barid — knowing them is essential for travel rulings.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the exact measurements used in Hanafi fiqh to define travel. Understanding the hierarchy from the smallest unit (shu'ayrah) to the largest (barid) ensures that rulings on qasr, iftar, and tayammum are applied correctly. The versified lines provide a memorable framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the largest unit and its subdivisions
The passage begins by defining the barid as 4 parasangs, the parasang as 3 miles, the mile as 1000 bā', and the bā' as 4 cubits. This gives the upper part of the hierarchy.
Barid is the key unit for travel threshold.
2
Break down the cubit into fingers and barleycorns
The cubit (dhirā') is defined as 24 finger-widths, each finger (isba') is 6 barleycorns (sha'īrat), and each barleycorn is 6 horsehairs (sha'r). This details the lower part.
The barleycorn is the smallest standard unit.
3
Understand the versified mnemonics
The poem encodes the conversion ratios: 'A barid is four parasangs, a parasang three miles, a mile a thousand bā', a bā' four cubits, a cubit twenty-four fingers, a finger six barleycorns, a barleycorn six hairs.'
Poetry helps memorization.
4
Recognize the authoritative source
Al-Ramli's commentary confirms that these definitions are taken from al-Zayla'i and are the relied-upon (mu'tamad) standard in the Hanafi school.
Knowing the source adds confidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا شعيرات مرصوصة بالعرض والشعير ست شعرات بشعر البرذون ا هـ . كلامه وهو موا موافق لما في الزيلعي وقد نظم ذلك بعضهم فقال : إن البريد مـن الـفـراسـخ أربع ولفرسخ فثلاث أميال ضـعـوا والميل ألف أي مـن الـبـاعـات قـل والباع أربع أذرع تتتبع ثم الذراع من الأصـابـع أربــع في بعدها العشرون ثم الأصبع ست شعيرات فظهر شعيرة منها إلى بطن لأخرى توضع ثم الشعيرة ست شعرات فقـل من شعر بغل ليس فيها مدفع أقول : فتحصل من هذا كله أن ما نقله الزيلعي هو المعول فتأمل ا هـ. كلام الرملي ملخصاً،
No barleycorns arranged widthwise, and a barleycorn is six hairs of a pony's hair. His speech is in agreement with what is in al-Zayla'i. Some versified it: Indeed, a barid is four parasangs, and a parasang is three miles, they placed. A mile is a thousand cubits, say from bā' measures. A bā' is four cubits to follow. Then the cubit is four fingers in its length is twenty. Then the finger is six barleycorns, so a barleycorn from it to the belly of another is placed. Then the barleycorn is six hairs, so say from hair of a mule which has no defect. I say: From all this, it is obtained that what al-Zayla'i transmitted is the relied-upon, so reflect. The speech of al-Ramli summarized.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling providing the precise units of distance used in Hanafi fiqh for travel concessions such as qasr, iftar, and tayammum. The author begins by clarifying the measurement of a cubit (dhira'): it is defined as 24 finger-widths (isba'), and each finger-width is 6 barleycorns (sha'irat). A bā' (fathom) is 4 cubits. A mile (mil) is 1000 bā' (or 4000 cubits). A parasang (farsakh) is 3 miles, and a barīd is 4 parasangs (12 miles). This system is taken from al-Zayla'i and is relied upon in the Hanafi school. The versified lines help memorize the hierarchy: barid (4 farsakh) → farsakh (3 miles) → mile (1000 bā') → bā' (4 cubits) → cubit (24 fingers) → finger (6 barleycorns) → barleycorn (6 horsehairs). The commentary by al-Ramli confirms that al-Zayla'i's definitions are the standard.

Key Terms
بريد (barīd): A unit of distance equal to 4 parasangs (approximately 12 miles or 48,000 cubits). Used in defining travel distance for sharia concessions.
فرسخ (farsakh): A unit equal to 3 miles (approximately 12,000 cubits or 7-9 km).
ميل (mīl): A unit equal to 1000 bā' (or 4000 cubits). Approximately 1.6 km in modern terms.
ذراع (dhirā'): A cubit, equal to 24 finger-widths (isba') or about 30-36 cm in modern terms.
أصبع (isba'): A finger-width, equal to 6 barleycorns. Used as a sub-unit of the cubit.
شعيرة (shu'ayrah): A barleycorn, the smallest standard unit of length, approximately 0.5 cm. 6 barleycorns = 1 finger-width.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many barleycorns (sha'irat) make one finger-width (isba') according to the definitions in this passage?
A) 4
B) 6
C) 20
D) 24

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distance hierarchy is precise: 1 barīd = 4 farsakh = 12 miles = 48,000 cubits = 1,152,000 barleycorns, with each unit defined by natural measures (finger, barleycorn, horsehair).

Tayammum for Illness and the Dispute on Capacity via a Helper
Intra-Hanafi dispute on capacity via helper

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for tayammum due to illness and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether finding a helper invalidates tayammum, identifying the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
If help is available, tayammum is invalid — the capacity of another is considered one's own according to the relied-upon view.

This lesson dives into an important intra-Hanafi dispute: when a sick person cannot perform wudu themselves but can find someone to help them, does tayammum remain valid? The answer hinges on the concept of capacity (qudra). We'll explore the positions of Abu Hanifa and his two companions, and see how the later school settled the matter. By the end, you'll be able to apply this ruling and understand the underlying legal principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition for Tayammum Due to Illness
The passage first restricts the general permission for tayammum: it is only valid if the illness would be exacerbated or prolonged by using water. Minor illness does not justify it. Make sure you understand this threshold.
This condition is common to all schools, but the Hanafi school emphasizes fear of harm.
2
Recognize the Two Scenarios of Help
Next, the passage distinguishes between finding a servant (slave, child, hired worker) and finding a non-servant helper (e.g., a stranger or spouse). In the first case, all agree tayammum is invalid. In the second, a dispute arises.
The dispute is about 'non-servant' helpers.
3
State the Views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa, according to some narrations, allows tayammum even if a non-servant helper is available, because he does not consider the person capable via another's capacity. The Sahibayn say tayammum is invalid because the helper's assistance makes the person capable.
The 'zahir al-madhhab' (apparent school) is that there is no dispute, but al-Tanqih records it.
4
Understand the Legal Principle: Qudra bi-Alat al-Ghayr
The Sahibayn's view is based on the principle that capacity can be established through another's instrument (alat al-ghayr). Abu Hanifa's view is that a person is only capable if the action is directly in their power. This principle also applies to other issues like hajj, kaffarah, and qibla direction.
Later authorities like Husam al-Din preferred the Sahibayn's view.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi (Relied-Upon) Position
The passage indicates that the mufta bihi is that tayammum is not valid when any helper is available, as this is the view of the Sahibayn and the preference of later Hanafi masters. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
Even if the helper is a stranger or spouse, tayammum is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (أو لمرض) يعني يجوز التيمم للمرض وأطلقه وهو مقيد بما ذكره في الكافي من قوله بأن يخاف اشتداد مرضه لو استعمل الماء، فعلم أن اليسير منه لا يبيح التيمم وهو قول العلماء إلا ما حكاه النووي عن بعض المالكية وهو مردود بأنه رخصة أبيحت للضرورة جمهور پشتد ودفع الحرج وهو إنما يتحقق عند خوف الاشتداد والامتداد، ولا فرق عندنا أن بين بالتحرك كالمبطون أو بالاستعمال كالجدري، أو كان لا يجد من يوضئه ولا يقدر بنفسه اتفاقاً. وإن وجد خادماً كعبده وولده وأجيره لا يجزيه التيمم اتفاقاً كما نقله في المحيط، وإن وجد غير خادمه من لو استعان به أعانه ولو زوجته فظاهر المذهب أنه لا يتيمم من غير خلاف بين أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه كما يفيده كلام المبسوط والبدائع وغيرهما. ونقل في التنجيس بين أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه على قوله يجزئه التيمم، وعلى قولهما لا. قال: عن شيخه خلافاً وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا كان مريضاً لا يقدر على الاستقبال أو كان في فراشه نجاسة ولا يقدر على التحول منه ووجد من يحوله ويوجهه لا يفترض عليه ذلك عنده، وعلى هذا الأعمى إذا وجد قائداً لا تلزمه الجمعة والحج والخلاف فيهما معروف. فالحاصل أن عنده المكلف قادراً بقدرة غيره لأن الإنسان إنما يعد قادراً إذا اختص بحالة يتهيأ له الفعل متى أراد، وهذا لا يتحقق بقدرة غيره ولهذا قلنا: إذا بذل الابن المال والطاعة لأبيه لا يلزمه الحج، وكذا من وجبت عليه الكفارة وهو معدوم فبذل له انسان المال لما قلنا. وعندهما تثبت القدرة بآلة الغير لأن آلة الغير صارت كالته بالإعانة وكان حسام الدين رحمه الله يختار قولهما. والفرق على ظاهر المذهب بين مسألة التيمم وبين المريض إذا لم يقدر على الصلاة لا يعتبر. وفي الشرنبلالية قال بعد نقله ما ذكره الزيلعي عن البرهان عن ابن شجاع قلت : يمكن أن يقال لا خلاف لحمل كلام ابن شجاع على أن مراده بالذراع ما فيه أصبع قائمة عند كل قبضة فيبلغ ذراعاً ونصفاً بذراع العامة، ويؤيده ما قاله الزيلعي مقتصراً عليه وهو أي الميل ثلث الفرسخ أربعة آلاف ذراع بذراع ست حبات شعیر محمد بن فرج ابن الشاشي، طولها أربعة وعشرون أصبعاً، وعرض كل أصبع قلت : لكن ما ادعاه من تأييد عبارة الزيلعي لما قاله من التوفيق غير ظاهر بعد ظهر البطن ا هـ . تحديده الذراع وكذا ما مرّ عن ابن الهائم تأمل قوله : (ومن كان في كلة) قال في القاموس: هي ملصقة الستر الرقيق وغشاء رقيق يتوفى به من البعوض قوله : (كما نقله في المحيط) عبارته على ما في يوضئه فهذا على وجهين الأول أن يكون الذي يوضئه حراً في هذا التتارخانية، وأما إذا وجد أحداً الوجه. قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله : يجزئه التيمم وقالا لا يجزئه الثاني إذا كان الذي يوضئه مملوكاً له بأن كان عبداً أو أمة لا شك أن على قولهما لا يجوز له التيمم، وإما على قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله فقد اختلف المشايخ والصحيح أنه لا يجوز له التيمم. وذكر في الوجه الأول عن فتاوى الحجة سأل أبو حنيفة رحمه الله عمن عجز بنفسه عن الوضوء قال : يجوز له التيمم وإن كان يجد من يوضئه . ثم قال
His statement (or for illness) means tayammum is permissible for illness, and he made it absolute, but it is restricted by what was mentioned in al-Kafi: that he fears exacerbation of his illness if he uses water. So it is known that a minor illness does not permit tayammum. This is the statement of the scholars except what al-Nawawi related from some Malikis, and it is rejected because it is a concession allowed for necessity and removal of hardship, which is only realized when there is fear of exacerbation and prolongation. According to us, there is no difference whether it is by movement (like a person with diarrhea) or by use (like smallpox), or if he cannot find one to perform wudu for him and cannot do it himself by agreement. But if he finds a servant like his slave, child, or hired worker, tayammum is not sufficient for him by agreement, as related in al-Muhit. If he finds one who is not his servant, and if he sought help he would help him, even if it is his wife, the apparent madhhab is that he does not perform tayammum, without dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions, as indicated by the words of al-Mabsut, al-Bada'i', and others. It was related in al-Tanqih that there is a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions: according to him, tayammum suffices him; according to them, no. He said: from his shaykh there is disagreement. Upon this disagreement branches: if he is sick and unable to face the qibla, or if there is najasa in his bed and he cannot move from it, and he finds someone who can move him and direct him, it is not obligatory upon him according to him (Abu Hanifa). Similarly, a blind person, if he finds a guide, Friday prayer and hajj are not obligatory upon him; the disagreement on these points is well-known. The conclusion is that according to him, the accountable person is capable through the capacity of another, because a person is considered capable only if he is in a state such that the action becomes possible for him whenever he wants, and this is not realized through another's capacity. For this reason we said: if a son offers money and obedience to his father, hajj is not obligatory on him; similarly, one who owes kaffarah and is poor, if someone offers him money, it is not obligatory. According to them (the two), capacity is established through another's instrument because the other's instrument becomes like his own instrument through assistance. Husam al-Din (may Allah have mercy on him) used to prefer their view. The difference according to the apparent madhhab between the issue of tayammum and a patient who cannot pray is that it is not considered. In al-Shurnubulaliyya, he said after transmitting what al-Zayla'i related from al-Burhan from Ibn Shuja': I say it can be said there is no disagreement, because Ibn Shuja's words should be understood as meaning by 'cubit' the one in which there is a standing finger at every handful, so it reaches one and a half cubits by the common cubit. This is supported by what al-Zayla'i said restrictively: that a mile is one-third of a parasang, four thousand cubits by the cubit of six barleycorns, according to Muhammad ibn Faraj ibn al-Shashi, its length is twenty-four fingers, and the width of each finger... I say: but his claim of supporting al-Zayla'i's expression for the reconciliation he mentioned is not apparent after 'zahr al-batn'. The definition of the cubit, and similarly what was mentioned about Ibn al-Ha'im, reflect. His statement: 'Whoever is in a mosquito net' - in al-Qamus: it is a thin veil and thin membrane by which one protects from mosquitoes. His statement: 'As he transmitted in al-Muhit' - his expression according to what is in... He said: this is two aspects: first, the one who performs wudu for him is free; in this Tatarkhaniyya... As for if he finds someone... aspect. Abu Hanifa said: tayammum suffices him; they said: it does not suffice him. Second: if the one who performs wudu for him is his property, such as if he is a slave or slave girl, there is no doubt that according to them tayammum is not permissible for him; as for according to Abu Hanifa, the mashayikh differed, and the correct view is that tayammum is not permissible for him. He mentioned in the first aspect from Fatawa al-Hujjah: Abu Hanifa was asked about one who is unable to perform wudu by himself; he said: tayammum is permissible for him even if he finds someone to perform wudu for him. Then he said.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, known as the Sahibayn) regarding the validity of tayammum for a sick person who cannot perform wudu himself but can find someone to help him. The passage begins by clarifying the condition for tayammum due to illness: it must be a genuine fear of exacerbation or prolongation of illness if water is used. Minor illness does not permit it. Then the discussion moves to the scenario where a person cannot do wudu himself (due to illness or disability) but can find another person to assist. The relied-upon view (zahir al-madhhab) is that if he finds a helper (even a stranger willing to help, or his wife), he is considered capable of using water and tayammum is not allowed. This is the unanimous view of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn according to the apparent sources (Mabsut, Bada'i'). However, there is a narration (in al-Tanqih) that Abu Hanifa differed, permitting tayammum in such a case. The passage explores the underlying legal theory: Abu Hanifa's position is that a person is only 'capable' (qadir) if they have direct control over the action; the capacity of another does not transfer to him. The Sahibayn argue that assistance from others establishes capacity vicariously (bi-alat al-ghayr), so the person should use that help rather than resort to tayammum. Husam al-Din (a later Hanafi authority) favored the view of the two companions. The text also relates this principle to other issues: a blind person is not obligated to perform hajj if he finds a guide (according to Abu Hanifa), and offering money to a poor person does not make hajj or kaffarah obligatory. The latter part of the passage digresses into a discussion on the definition of the cubit (dhira') from al-Shurunbulali, clarifying a potential contradiction in earlier sources, and then returns to the tayammum issue, noting a difference of opinion when the helper is a slave owned by the person. The correct view is that tayammum is not allowed even for Abu Hanifa in that case.

Key Terms
مرض (marad): Illness that justifies tayammum when using water would cause exacerbation or prolongation. Minor illness does not suffice.
قدرة (qudra): Capacity to perform an act. In this context, a person is considered capable if they can use water with the help of another, according to the Sahibayn.
آلة الغير (ālat al-ghayr): Instrument or agency of another person. Used in the argument that if someone can help, it becomes like their own instrument.
خادم (khādim): A servant, including slave, child, or hired worker. Finding such a helper makes tayammum invalid by agreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in this passage, what is the ruling if a sick person cannot do wudu but finds a stranger willing to help?
A) Tayammum is valid
B) Tayammum is not valid; he must seek help for wudu
C) He may choose between tayammum and wudu with help
D) It depends on whether the helper is free or slave

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, if a sick person can find any helper for wudu, tayammum is invalid; the helper must be used.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Tayammum Due to Illness: Condition and Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Capability Through Another
Commentary on tayammum due to illness and cold, with an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the condition of illness that permits tayammum and identify the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two companions on whether a free helper negates tayammum, and state the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires genuine harm from water; a free helper makes wudu accessible according to the relied-upon view.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the scope of tayammum due to illness. It first establishes that only serious illness—fear of worsening or prolonging—justifies tayammum, not slight indisposition. The commentator then delves into a key intra-Hanafi dispute: if a patient cannot perform wudu alone but a free person is willing to help, does that negate tayammum? Abu Hanifa says no; the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say yes. The relied-upon fatwa follows the companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for tayammum due to illness
The passage states that tayammum is permitted only when one fears that using water would intensify his illness or delay recovery. Slight illness does not suffice. This is the agreed view among the schools, rejecting a deviant Maliki opinion.
The condition applies whether the illness is aggravated by movement (e.g., stomach ailment) or by contact with water (e.g., smallpox).
2
Recognize the condition for tayammum due to cold
Similarly, if a junub or one in hadath fears death or severe harm from using cold water, tayammum is permitted. This is also a legitimate necessity.
The proof is the same general principle of removing hardship.
3
State the scenario of the intra-Hanafi dispute
A patient cannot perform wudu by himself but finds a free person—neighbor, wife, etc.—who would help him. Does that make him capable of using water, thus invalidating tayammum?
This scenario does not apply to servants (slave, employee), where tayammum is invalid by agreement.
4
Contrast the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two companions
Abu Hanifa holds that tayammum suffices because a person is only capable if the action is possible whenever he wants, independently. Dependence on another's will does not constitute capability. The two companions hold that the helper's ability becomes like the person's own through assistance, so tayammum is invalid.
The difference extends to analogous cases: facing qibla, removing impurity from bed, and obligation of Hajj for a blind person with a guide.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi scholars, including Husam al-Din, prefer the view of the two companions. Therefore, if a free helper is available, tayammum is not permissible and wudu is required.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (أو لمرض) يعني يجوز التيمم للمرض وأطلقه وهو مقيد بما ذكره في الكافي من قوله بأن يخاف اشتداد مرضه لو استعمل الماء، فعلم أن اليسير منه لا يبيح التيمم وهو قول العلماء إلا ما حكاه النووي عن بعض المالكية وهو مردود بأنه رخصة أبيحت للضرورة ودفع الحرج وإنما يتحقق عند خوف الاشتداد والامتداد، ولا فرق عندنا أن بين بالتحرك كالمبطون أو بالاستعمال كالجدري، أو كان لا يجد من يوضئه ولا يقدر بنفسه اتفاقاً. وإن وجد خادماً كعبده وولده وأجيره لا يجزيه التيمم اتفاقاً كما نقله في المحيط، وإن وجد غير خادمه من لو استعان به أعانه ولو زوجته فظاهر المذهب أنه لا يتيمم من غير خلاف بين أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه كما يفيده كلام المبسوط والبدائع وغيرهما. ونقل في التنجيس بين أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه على قوله يجزئه التيمم، وعلى قولهما لا. قال: عن شيخه خلافاً وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا كان مريضاً لا يقدر على الاستقبال أو كان في فراشه نجاسة ولا يقدر على التحول منه ووجد من يحوله ويوجهه لا يفترض عليه ذلك عنده، وعلى هذا الأعمى إذا وجد قائداً لا تلزمه الجمعة والحج والخلاف فيهما معروف. فالحاصل أن المكلف قادراً بقدرة غيره لأن الإنسان إنما يعد قادراً إذا اختص بحالة يتهيأ له الفعل متى أراد، وهذا لا يتحقق بقدرة غيره ولهذا قلنا: إذا بذل الابن المال والطاعة لأبيه لا يلزمه الحج، وكذا من وجبت عليه الكفارة وهو معدوم فبذل له إنسان المال لما قلنا. وعندهما تثبت القدرة بآلة الغير لأن آلة الغير صارت كالته بالإعانة وكان حسام الدين رحمه الله يختار قولهما. والفرق على ظاهر المذهب بين مسألة التيمم وبين المريض إذا لم يقدر على الصلاة لا يعتبر قادراً بقدرة غيره وفي الشرنبلالية قال بعد نقله ما ذكره الزيلعي عن البرهان عن ابن شجاع قلت : يمكن أن يقال لا خلاف لحمل كلام ابن شجاع على أن مراده بالذراع ما فيه أصبع قائمة عند كل قبضة فيبلغ ذراعاً ونصفاً بذراع العامة، ويؤيده ما قاله الزيلعي مقتصراً عليه وهو أي الميل ثلث الفرسخ أربعة آلاف ذراع بذراع ست حبات شعیر محمد بن فرج ابن الشاشي، طولها أربعة وعشرون أصبعاً، وعرض كل أصبع قلت : لكن ما ادعاه من تأييد عبارة الزيلعي لما قاله من التوفيق غير ظاهر بعد ظهر البطن ا هـ . تحديده الذراع وكذا ما مرّ عن ابن الهائم تأمل قوله : (ومن كان في كلة) قال في القاموس: هي الستر الرقيق وغشاء رقيق يتوفى به من البعوض قوله : (كما نقله في المحيط) عبارته على ما في يوضئه فهذا على وجهين الأول أن يكون الذي يوضئه حراً في هذا التتارخانية، وأما إذا وجد أحداً الوجه. قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله : يجزئه التيمم وقالا لا يجزئه الثاني إذا كان الذي يوضئه مملوكاً له بأن كان عبداً أو أمة لا شك أن على قولهما لا يجوز له التيمم، وإما على قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله فقد اختلف المشايخ والصحيح أنه لا يجوز له التيمم. وذكر في الوجه الأول عن فتاوى الحجة سأل أبو حنيفة رحمه الله عمن عجز بنفسه عن الوضوء قال : يجوز له التيمم وإن كان يجد من يوضئه . ثم قال يتيمم إذا كان ومعه قوم لو استعان بهم في الإقامة والثبات جاز له الصلاة قاعداً أنه يخاف على المريض زيادة الوجع في قيامه ولا يلحقه زيادة الوجع في الوضوء ا هـ ما في التنجيس. وظاهره أنه لو لم يكن له أجير لكن معه ما يستأجر به أجيراً لا يجزئه التيمم، قل الآجر أو كثر، فإنه قال : أو عنده من المال مقدار ما يستأجر به أجيراً والفرق بين الزوجة والمملوك أن المنكوحة إذا مرضت لا يجب عليه أن يوضئها وأن يتعاهدها، وفي العبد والجارية يجب عليه إذا لم يستطع الوضوء، كذا في الخلاصة . يعني أن السيد لما كان عليه تعاهد العبد في مرضه كان على عبده أن يتعاهده في مرضه والزوجة لما لم يكن عليه أن يتعاهدها في مرضها فيما يتعلق بالصلاة لا يجب عليها ذلك، إذا مرض فلا يعد قادراً بفعلها. وفي المبتغى: مريض إذا لم يكن عنده أحد يوضئه إلا بأجر جاز له التيمم عند أبي حنيفة قلّ الأجر أو كثر. وقالا : لا الأجر ربع درهم ا هـ. والظاهر عدم الجواز إذا كان قليلاً لا إذا كان كثيراً لما عرف من شراء الماء إذا وجده بثمن المثل على ما نبينه إن شاء الله تعالى وبقولنا قال مالك وأحمد والشافعي في الأصح كما نقله النووي لإطلاق قوله تعالى وإن كنتم مرضى) [النساء: ٤٣] والمراد من الوجود في الآية القدرة. قال العلامة الكردري : الفاء في قوله تعالى «فلم تجد واللعطف على الشرط، وفي فتيمموا الجواب الشرط ، وفي فامسحوا» لتفسير التيمم. وهذا إذا قدر المريض على التيمم، أما إذا لم يقدر عليه أيضاً ولا عنده من يستعين به فإنه لا يصلي عندهما . قال الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر : رأيت في الجامع الصغير للكرخي أن مقطوع اليدين والرجلين إذا كان بوجهه جراحة يصلي بغير طهارة ولا يتيمم ولا يعيد وهذا هو الأصح . كذا في فتاوى الظهيرية ذكره مسكين وسيأتي بقية الكلام عليه إن شاء الله تعالى . قوله (أو برد) أي أن خاف الجنب أو المحدث إن اغتسل أو توضأ أن يقتله البرد أو يخاف على المريض زيادة الوجع في قيامه ولا يلحقه زيادة الوجع في الوضوء ا هـ ما في التنجيس. وظاهره أنه لو لم يكن له أجير لكن معه ما يستأجر به أجيراً لا يجزئه التيمم، قل الآجر أو كثر، فإنه قال : أو عنده من المال مقدار ما يستأجر به أجيراً والفرق بين الزوجة والمملوك أن المنكوحة إذا مرضت لا يجب عليه أن يوضئها وأن يتعاهدها، وفي العبد والجارية يجب عليه إذا لم يستطع الوضوء، كذا في الخلاصة . يعني أن السيد لما كان عليه تعاهد العبد في مرضه كان على عبده أن يتعاهده في مرضه والزوجة لما لم يكن عليه أن يتعاهدها في مرضها فيما يتعلق بالصلاة لا يجب عليها ذلك، إذا مرض فلا يعد قادراً بفعلها. وفي المبتغى: مريض إذا لم يكن عنده أحد يوضئه إلا بأجر جاز له التيمم عند أبي حنيفة قلّ الأجر أو كثر. وقالا : لا الأجر ربع درهم ا هـ. والظاهر عدم الجواز إذا كان قليلاً لا إذا كان كثيراً لما عرف من شراء الماء إذا وجده بثمن المثل على ما نبينه إن شاء الله تعالى وبقولنا قال مالك وأحمد والشافعي في الأصح كما نقله النووي لإطلاق قوله تعالى وإن كنتم مرضى) [النساء: ٤٣] والمراد من الوجود في الآية القدرة. قال العلامة الكردري : الفاء في قوله تعالى «فلم تجد واللعطف على الشرط، وفي فتيمموا الجواب الشرط ، وفي فامسحوا» لتفسير التيمم. وهذا إذا قدر المريض على التيمم، أما إذا لم يقدر عليه أيضاً ولا عنده من يستعين به فإنه لا يصلي عندهما . قال الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر : رأيت في الجامع الصغير للكرخي أن مقطوع اليدين والرجلين إذا كان بوجهه جراحة يصلي بغير طهارة ولا يتيمم ولا يعيد وهذا هو الأصح . كذا في فتاوى الظهيرية ذكره مسكين وسيأتي بقية الكلام عليه إن شاء الله تعالى . قوله (أو برد) أي أن خاف الجنب أو المحدث إن اغتسل أو توضأ أن يقتله البرد أو
His statement (or due to illness) means that tayammum is permitted for illness, and it is unrestricted but restricted by what he mentioned in al-Kafi: that he fears the intensification of his illness if he uses water. So it is known that a slight [illness] does not permit tayammum. This is the statement of the scholars except what al-Nawawi reported from some Malikis, which is rejected because it is a concession permitted for necessity and removal of hardship, and that is only realized when fearing intensification and prolongation. There is no difference in our school whether it manifests through movement like a stomach ailment or through use like smallpox, or if he cannot find someone to perform wudu for him and cannot do it himself by agreement. And if he finds a servant like his slave, son, or hired worker, tayammum is not permissible for him by agreement as transmitted in al-Muhit. And if he finds someone other than his servant, such that if he sought help he would help him, even his wife, then the apparent madhhab is that he does not perform tayammum with no disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions as is indicated by the words of al-Mabsut, al-Bada'i' and others. It is transmitted in al-Tanjis that there is disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions: according to him, tayammum suffices; according to them, no. He said: from his shaykh there is disagreement. Based on this disagreement, if a patient cannot face the qibla or has impurity on his bed and cannot move from it, and he finds someone to move him and orient him, he is not obligated to do that according to him. Similarly, if a blind person finds a guide, Friday prayer and Hajj are not obligatory upon him, and the disagreement in these two is well-known. The conclusion is that the responsible person is not considered capable through another's ability, because a person is only considered capable if he has a state that makes the action possible whenever he wants, and this is not realized through another's ability. For this reason we said: if a son offers wealth and obedience to his father, Hajj is not obligatory upon him; similarly, one who owes expiation and is destitute, if someone offers him wealth, [it is not binding]. According to them, ability is established through another's means because another's means becomes like his own through assistance. Husam al-Din (may Allah have mercy on him) used to prefer their view. The difference according to the apparent madhhab between the issue of tayammum and the patient who cannot perform prayer: he is not considered capable through another's ability. And in al-Shurunbulaliyya, he said after transmitting what al-Zayla'i mentioned from al-Burhan from Ibn Shuja': I say: It can be said that there is no disagreement, by interpreting Ibn Shuja's words to mean that by 'cubit' he means one where there is an upright finger at each fist, so it reaches one and a half cubits by the common cubit, supported by what al-Zayla'i restricted to: that a mile is one-third of a parasang, four thousand cubits by the cubit of six barley grains of Muhammad ibn Faraj ibn al-Shashi, its length twenty-four fingers, and the width of each finger... I say: but his claim of support from al-Zayla'i's statement for his reconciliation is not apparent after the emergence of the abdomen. So his definition of the cubit, and likewise what was mentioned from Ibn al-Ha'im. Consider his statement: (And whoever is in a kallah). In al-Qamus: it is a thin curtain and a thin covering used to protect from mosquitoes. His statement: (as transmitted in al-Muhit). Its wording according to what is in [al-Tatar Khaniyya]: 'He performs wudu for him. This is on two aspects: first, that the one who performs wudu for him is free.' In this al-Tatar Khaniyya: 'And if he finds someone' the aspect. Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Tayammum suffices him. They both said: It does not suffice. Second: if the one who performs wudu for him is his property, being a male or female slave, there is no doubt that according to them tayammum is not permissible for him. As for the view of Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), the mashayikh differed, and the correct view is that tayammum is not permissible for him. And he mentioned in the first aspect from Fatawa al-Hujja: Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) was asked about one who is unable to perform wudu by himself. He said: Tayammum is permissible for him even if he finds someone to perform wudu for him. Then he said: He performs tayammum if he is with people who, if he sought their help in standing and stability, it would be permissible for him to pray sitting, because it is feared that the patient's pain would increase if he stands, but no increased pain would affect him in wudu. End of what is in al-Tanjis. Its apparent meaning is that if he does not have a hired worker but has money with which to hire one, tayammum is not permissible for him, whether the wage is little or much. For he said: 'or he has wealth with which to hire a worker.' The difference between the wife and the slave is that if the wife falls ill, it is not obligatory for him to perform wudu for her or to care for her; while for the slave and slave girl, it is obligatory for him when he cannot perform wudu. Thus in al-Khulasa. Meaning that since the master is obligated to care for the slave during his illness, the slave is obligated to care for him during his illness. As for the wife, since he is not obligated to care for her during her illness regarding prayer matters, she is not obligated for that. So if he falls ill, he is not considered capable through her action. In al-Muntagha: A patient who has no one to perform wudu for him except for a fee, tayammum is permissible for him according to Abu Hanifa, whether the fee is little or much. They both said: No, if the fee is a quarter dirham. End. And the apparent view is non-permissibility if it is little, not if it is much, based on what is known about buying water if he finds it at the market price, as we will explain if Allah wills. And our view is held by Malik, Ahmad, and al-Shafi'i according to the most sound opinion as transmitted by al-Nawawi, due to the generality of Allah's statement: {And if you are ill} [4:43]. The intended meaning of 'finding' in the verse is ability. Al-Allama al-Kardari said: The 'fa' in Allah's statement 'falam tajidu' is for conjunction on the condition, and in 'fatayammamu' is the answer of the condition, and in 'famsahu' is for interpretation of tayammum. This applies if the patient is able to perform tayammum. But if he is also unable to do it and has no one to assist him, then according to them he does not pray. Shaykh al-Imam Abu Bakr said: I saw in al-Jami' al-Saghir of al-Karkhi that one whose hands and feet are cut off, if he has a wound on his face, he prays without purification and does not perform tayammum and does not repeat, and this is the most correct. Thus in Fatawa al-Zahiriyya, mentioned by Miskin, and the rest of the discussion will come if Allah wills. His statement (or due to cold): meaning that if a junub or hadath person fears that the cold will kill him if he performs ghusl or wudu, or he fears increased pain for the patient when standing but no increased pain in wudu...
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the phrase 'или из-за болезни' из текста (tayammum). It begins by stating that tayammum is permitted for illness, but this permission is restricted: the illness must be such that using water would worsen it or prolong it. Slight illness does not permit tayammum. This is the view of all scholars except some Malikis as reported by al-Nawawi, but their view is rejected because the concession is for necessity and hardship. The passage then clarifies that it makes no difference whether the illness manifests through movement (like diarrhea) or through contact with water (like smallpox). If the person cannot find someone to perform wudu for him and cannot do it himself, all agree tayammum is permitted. However, if he finds a servant (slave, son, hired worker) to help, tayammum is not permitted by agreement. If he finds someone who is not his servant (like a free person who would help if asked), the apparent madhhab is that tayammum is not permitted, and this is agreed upon by Abu Hanifa and his two companions. But al-Tanjis reports a difference: Abu Hanifa said tayammum suffices, while the two companions said no. This difference extends to other cases: if a patient cannot face the qibla or has impurity on his bed and finds someone to move him, according to Abu Hanifa that person is not obligated to accept help; according to the companions he is. Similarly, a blind person who finds a guide is not obligated to attend Friday prayer or Hajj according to Abu Hanifa. The core legal principle is that Imam Abu Hanifa defines 'capability' (qudra) as personal capacity, not capacity through another. A person is only considered capable if the action is possible whenever he wishes, which is not realized by another's ability. Therefore, if a son offers wealth and obedience to his father, Hajj is not obligatory on the son because he is not personally capable. Similarly, expiation is not required if someone offers money. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider capability established through another's instrumentality because that instrument becomes like one's own through assistance. Husam al-Din preferred their view. The passage then digresses into a discussion about the definition of a cubit (dhira') and a mile, which appears to be a marginal note about the distance that permits tayammum during travel, but this may be a separate topic. Returning to the main issue, the text discusses the case where the helper is a free person versus a slave. If the helper is free, Abu Hanifa says tayammum suffices; the companions say no. If the helper is a slave, the mashayikh differed on Abu Hanifa's view, but the correct position is that tayammum is not permitted. The passage then explains the difference between a wife and a slave: a wife is not obligated to help her husband with wudu during illness because he is not obligated to care for her in that way; a slave is obligated because the master must care for the slave. Thus, the patient is not considered capable through his wife's action. If the patient has money to hire someone, tayammum is not permitted according to the apparent view if the wage is little (like quarter dirham) but permitted if the wage is much. This is analogous to buying water at market price. The verse {And if you are ill} (4:43) is cited as proof for tayammum, with the term 'finding' interpreted as 'capability'. Al-Kardari explains the grammatical structure of the verse. Then follows a special case: if the patient cannot even perform tayammum and has no helper, he does not pray according to the two companions. But the more correct view from al-Karkhi is that a person with amputated limbs and facial wounds prays without purification and does not repeat. Finally, the passage addresses tayammum due to cold: if a junub or hadath person fears death or illness from using cold water, tayammum is permitted.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution using clean earth (or any pure substitute) as a replacement for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
قادر بقدرة غيره (qādir bi-qudrat ghayrihi): A person considered capable of an action through another person's capacity or assistance, such as having someone else perform wudu for him.
مرض (marad): Illness that makes using water harmful, either by causing fear of worsening the disease or delaying recovery.
أجير (ajīr): A hired worker; in this context, someone paid to assist with wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), if a patient cannot perform wudu but has a free neighbor willing to help him with wudu, what is the ruling regarding tayammum?
A) Tayammum is permissible because the patient is not capable through another.
B) Tayammum is not permissible because the patient has access to water through the helper.
C) Tayammum is permissible only if the neighbor demands payment.
D) The patient must wait until the neighbor becomes unavailable.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum for illness is conditional on genuine harm from water; if a free helper is available, the mufta bihi view requires wudu, not tayammum.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Tayammum with a Helper: The Dispute on Hiring Wages
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum with helpers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum for a sick person who can hire a helper, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the wage limit.

Core Idea
Having means to hire a helper at a fair wage makes you able to use water; tayammum is not allowed.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq examines when a sick person may resort to tayammum if he has companions or can afford to hire a helper. The author presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa allows tayammum regardless of the wage, while the Sahibayn restrict it to a quarter dirham or less. The commentary also distinguishes between a wife and a slave, and ends with an exceptional case for the severely disabled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine the act (tayammum) and the condition (sickness preventing wudu). Recognize that the dispute revolves around whether having money to hire a helper constitutes ability (qudra) to use water.
The source text frames the problem: if a sick person has money to hire, can he still perform tayammum?
2
State the Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa: Tayammum is allowed regardless of the wage because even a small wage is a burden. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): Tayammum is not allowed unless the wage is a quarter dirham or less (i.e., nominal).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with practical consequences.
3
Consider the wife vs. slave distinction
If the sick person has a wife, she is not obliged to help him with wudu, so his inability remains. If he has a slave, the master must tend to the slave's illness, so the slave's availability makes the master able to use water.
This shows how obligation (wujub) affects the determination of ability.
4
Review the exceptional case
A person with amputated limbs and facial wounds prays without purification (no wudu, no tayammum) and does not repeat, according to the soundest view cited from al-Karkhi.
This is a separate case of extreme inability.

يتيمم إذا كان ومعه قوم لو استعان بهم في الإقامة والثبات جاز له الصلاة قاعداً أنه يخاف على المريض زيادة الوجع في قيامه ولا يلحقه زيادة الوجع في الوضوء ا هـ ما في التنجيس. وظاهره أنه لو لم يكن له أجير لكن معه ما يستأجر به أجيراً لا يجزئه التيمم، قل الآجر أو كثر، فإنه قال : أو عنده من المال مقدار ما يستأجر به أجيراً والفرق بين الزوجة والمملوك أن المنكوحة إذا مرضت لا يجب عليه أن يوضئها وأن يتعاهدها، وفي العبد والجارية يجب عليه إذا لم يستطع الوضوء، كذا في الخلاصة . يعني أن السيد لما كان عليه تعاهد العبد في مرضه كان على عبده أن يتعاهده في مرضه والزوجة لما لم يكن عليه أن يتعاهدها في مرضها فيما يتعلق بالصلاة لا يجب عليها ذلك، إذا مرض فلا يعد قادراً بفعلها. وفي المبتغى: مريض إذا لم يكن عنده أحد يوضئه إلا بأجر جاز له التيمم عند أبي حنيفة قلّ الأجر أو كثر. وقالا : لا الأجر ربع درهم ا هـ. والظاهر عدم الجواز إذا كان قليلاً لا إذا كان كثيراً لما عرف من شراء الماء إذا وجده بثمن المثل على ما نبينه إن شاء الله تعالى وبقولنا قال مالك وأحمد والشافعي في الأصح كما نقله النووي لإطلاق قوله تعالى وإن كنتم مرضى) [النساء: ٤٣] والمراد من الوجود في الآية القدرة. قال العلامة الكردري : الفاء في قوله تعالى «فلم تجد واللعطف على الشرط، وفي فتيمموا الجواب الشرط ، وفي فامسحوا» لتفسير التيمم. وهذا إذا قدر المريض على التيمم، أما إذا لم يقدر عليه أيضاً ولا عنده من يستعين به فإنه لا يصلي عندهما . قال الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر : رأيت في الجامع الصغير للكرخي أن مقطوع اليدين والرجلين إذا كان بوجهه جراحة يصلي بغير طهارة ولا يتيمم ولا يعيد وهذا هو الأصح . كذا في فتاوى الظهيرية ذكره مسكين وسيأتي بقية الكلام عليه إن شاء الله تعالى .
He performs tayammum if he has people with him; if he seeks their help in standing and stability, it is permissible for him to pray sitting, because it is feared for the sick person that his pain might increase in standing, but he is not subject to increased pain in wudu. End of what is in al-Tanjis. And its apparent meaning is that if he does not have a hired helper but has with him money to hire a helper, tayammum is not sufficient for him, whether the wage is little or much, for he said: 'Or he has with him money in the amount to hire a helper.' And the difference between the wife and the slave: that if the married woman falls ill, it is not obligatory on him to perform wudu for her nor to tend to her; while for the male slave and female slave, it is obligatory on him if she cannot perform wudu. Thus in al-Khulasa. Meaning that since the master is required to tend to the slave in his illness, the slave is required to tend to him in his illness; and since the husband is not required to tend to his wife in her illness regarding matters of prayer, she is not required to do that for him, so when he falls ill, he is not considered able by her action. And in al-Mubtagha: A sick person who has no one to perform wudu for him except for a wage: tayammum is permissible for him according to Abu Hanifa, whether the wage is little or much. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: No, unless the wage is a quarter dirham or less. End. And the apparent view is that it is not permissible if it is little, not if it is much, based on what is known about purchasing water if he finds it at the fair price, as we will explain if Allah wills. And by our saying Malik, Ahmad, and al-Shafi'i in the soundest view also hold, as al-Nawawi transmitted, due to the generality of His statement: 'And if you are ill' (4:43), and the intended meaning of 'existence' in the verse is ability. Al-Kardari said: The fa in His statement 'then you did not find' is conjunctive to the condition, and 'then perform tayammum' is the answer of the condition, and 'then wipe' is to interpret tayammum. This is if the sick person is able to perform tayammum; but if he is not able to do that either and has no one to help him, then he does not pray according to the two. Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr said: I saw in al-Jami' al-Saghir of al-Karkhi that a person with amputated hands and feet, if he has a wound on his face, prays without purification and does not perform tayammum and does not repeat, and this is the most correct. Thus in Fatawa al-Zahiriyya, mentioned by Miskin, and the rest of the discussion on it will come, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage addresses the conditions under which a sick person may resort to tayammum when he cannot perform wudu due to illness, focusing on the availability of helpers. The text first mentions that if the sick person has people who can assist him in standing or maintaining stability, he should pray sitting, because the fear of increased pain in standing is greater than in wudu. However, if he lacks a helper but has money to hire one, tayammum is not permitted, because he is considered able to obtain water through hiring. The ruling is the same whether the wage is small or large according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two) differ, restricting permissibility only if the wage does not exceed a quarter dirham. The commentary notes that the apparent view favors non-permissibility when the wage is small (i.e., fair market price), drawing an analogy with the purchase of water at market price. The text then distinguishes between a wife and a slave: a husband is not obliged to perform wudu for his ill wife, so if she is available to help him, he is still considered unable because she is not obligated to assist; but a master must tend to his slave's needs, including wudu, so the availability of a slave makes the master able to use water. Finally, an exceptional case is cited from al-Karkhi: a person with no hands or feet and a facial wound prays without any purification and does not repeat, as the most correct position.

Key Terms
أجير (ajir): A hired helper (paid worker) who can assist in performing wudu.
ثمن المثل (thaman al-mithl): The fair market price or standard wage for a service.
قدرة (qudra): Legal ability; in this context, the ability to perform wudu without undue hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), under what condition can a sick person who can hire a helper perform tayammum?
A) Only if the wage is exactly a quarter dirham.
B) Only if the wage is a quarter dirham or less.
C) Only if the wage is a quarter dirham or more.
D) Never, because hiring is always possible.

Key Takeaway
The availability of a hired helper at a fair wage generally prevents tayammum, but the Sahibayn set a nominal threshold of a quarter dirham, while Abu Hanifa considers any wage that is not extortionate.

Tayammum for Junub Due to Cold: Ruling, Proof, and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling and proof for tayammum due to cold for a junub, with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum due to cold for a junub, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding location, and apply the conditions that limit the permissibility.

Core Idea
A junub may perform tayammum due to cold only if he cannot heat water, afford a bathhouse, find warmth, or shelter.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on tayammum for a junub in extreme cold. The key issue is whether the concession applies inside a town or only outside. Abu Hanifa's view, supported by a hadith, allows it anywhere given genuine inability, while his two companions restrict it to outside the town. We will explore the proof, the conditions, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tayammum (dry ablution) for a person in a state of janabah (major impurity) due to extreme cold. The ruling is a permissible concession (rukhsah) when using water would cause harm.
The concession is conditional, not unconditional.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of 'Amr ibn al-'As, who performed tayammum on a cold night and led prayer. The Prophet approved his action without inquiring about the location.
Hadith narrated by Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's general approval and lack of location inquiry indicate that the ruling is general (ta'mim) – it applies wherever the fear of harm is genuine.
The Prophet gave a general reason: 'fear of destruction'.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa permits tayammum inside the town; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) restrict it to outside the town, reasoning that inside a town one can usually find means to warm water or use a bathhouse.
This ikhtilaf is limited to the location; both agree on the conditions.
5
Apply the conditions
The permissibility requires: (1) genuine fear of death or illness, (2) inability to heat water, (3) inability to afford a bathhouse, (4) no warm clothing, (5) no shelter. If any means exist, tayammum is impermissible by consensus.
The Sahibayn's view inside the town is further restricted: one must have attempted to obtain hot water from all residents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (أو برد) أي أن خاف الجنب أو المحدث إن اغتسل أو توضأ أن يقتله البرد أو يمرضه تيمم، سواء كان خارج المصر أو فيه. وعندهما لا يتيمم فيه. كذا في الكافي . وجوازه للمحدث قول بعض المشايخ والصحيح أنه لا يجوز له التيمم كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان والخلاصة وغيرهما. وذكر المصنف في المستصفى أنه بالإجماع على الأصح. قال في فتح القدير : وكأنه والله أعلم لعدم اعتبار ذلك الخوف بناء على أنه مجرد وهم إذ لا يتحقق ذلك في الوضوء عادة ا هـ . ثم أعلم أن جوازه للجنب عند أبي حنيفة مشروط بأن لا يقدر على تسخين الماء ولا على أجرة الحمام في المصر ولا يجد ثوباً يتدفأ فيه ولا مكاناً يأويه كما أفاده في البدائع وشرح الجامع الصغير لقاضيخان، فصار الأصل أنه متی قدر على الاغتسال بوجه من الوجوه لا يباح له التيمم إجماعاً. وقالا : لا يجوز التيمم للبرد في المصر. وقد اختلف هذه نشأ المشايخ فمنهم من جعل الخلاف بينهم في اختلاف زمان لا برهان بناء على أن عن أجر الحمام في زمانهما يؤخذ بعد الدخول فإذا عجز عن الثمن دخل ثم تعلل بالعسرة وفي زمانه قبله فيعذر، ومنهم من جعله برهانياً بناه على الخلاف في جواز التيمم لغير الواجد قبل الطلب من رفيقه إذا كان له رفيق. فعلى هذا يقيد منعهما بأن يترك طلب الماء الحار من جميع أهل المصر، أما إذا طلب فمنع فإنه يجوز عندهما، والظاهر قوله لأنه لا يكلف الطهارة بالماء إلا إذا قدر عليه بالملك أو الشراء وعند انتفاء هذه القدرة يتحقق العجز، ولهذا لم يفصل المنية العلامة ابن أمير حاج أخذاً مما اتفقت عليه كلمتهم في ماء الوضوء إذا كان يباع ولا يوجد مجاناً. قوله: (تيمم سواء كان الخ) لأبي حنيفة ما روي عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بعث سرية وأمر عليهم عمرو بن العاص وكان ذلك في غزوة ذات السلاسل فلما رجعوا شكوا منه أشياء من جملتها أنهم قالوا: صلى بنا وهو جنب فذكر للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال : يا رسول الله أجنبت في ليلة باردة فخفت على نفسي الهلاك لو اغتسلت فذكرت ما قال الله تعالى ولا تقتلوا أنفسكم إن الله كان بكم رحيماً [النساء : ٢٩] فتيممت وصليت بهم فقال لهم رسول الله : ألا ترون صاحبكم كيف نظر لنفسه ولكم ولم يأمره بالإعادة ولم يستفسر أنه كان في مفازة أو مصر وعلل بعلة عامة وهو خوف الهلاك، ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم استصوب رأيه والحكم يتعمم بعموم العلة اهـ حلية.
His saying (or cold): that is, if a junub or one with minor hadath fears that if he performs ghusl or wudu, the cold will kill him or make him ill, he performs tayammum, whether he is outside the town or inside. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he does not perform tayammum inside the town. Thus in al-Kafi. Its permissibility for one with minor hadath is the saying of some shaykhs, and the correct view is that tayammum is not permissible for him. Thus in Fatawa Qadikhan, al-Khulasa, and others. The author mentioned in al-Mustasfa that it is by consensus according to the most correct. He said in Fath al-Qadir: And it is as if, and Allah knows best, because that fear is not considered, based on it being mere illusion, since it is not usually realized in wudu. End. Then know that its permissibility for the junub according to Abu Hanifa is conditional upon him not being able to heat the water, nor on the fare for the bathhouse in the town, nor finding a garment to warm himself in, nor a place to shelter, as conveyed in al-Bada'i' and Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir of Qadikhan. So the principle is that whenever he is able to perform ghusl in any way, tayammum is not permitted for him by consensus. And the two said: Tayammum for cold is not permissible in the town. And the shaykhs differed regarding this difference: some considered the disagreement temporal without evidence, based on the fact that the fare for the bathhouse in their time was taken after entry, so if he was unable to pay, he would enter and then excuse himself with hardship, while in his time it was taken before entry, so he would be excused. Others considered it evidential, building it on the disagreement about the permissibility of tayammum for one who does not find water before asking his companion, if he has a companion. According to this, their prohibition is restricted to leaving off requesting hot water from all the residents of the town; but if he requests and is refused, then it is permissible according to both. And the apparent view is his saying, because he is only required to perform purification with water if he is able to do so by ownership or purchase, and when this ability is absent, inability is realized, and for this reason the author of al-Munya, al-Allama Ibn Amir Hajj, did not differentiate, taking from what they all agreed upon regarding water for wudu if it is sold and not available for free. His saying: (He performs tayammum whether etc.) For Abu Hanifa, there is what was narrated from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him: He sent a raiding party and appointed Amr ibn al-'As over them, and that was in the Ghazwa of Dhat al-Salasil. When they returned, they complained about him for various things, including that they said: He led us in prayer while he was junub. So it was mentioned to the Prophet, peace be upon him. He said: O Messenger of Allah, I became junub on a cold night and feared destruction for myself if I performed ghusl. So I remembered what Allah said: 'And do not kill yourselves, indeed Allah is merciful to you' (4:29). So I performed tayammum and led them in prayer. So the Messenger of Allah said to them: 'Don't you see how your companion considered for himself and for you?' And he did not command him to repeat, nor did he ask whether he was in a wilderness or a town, and he gave a general reason: fear of destruction. And the Messenger of Allah approved his opinion, and the ruling is generalized by the generality of the reason. End from al-Hilya.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on tayammum due to extreme cold, particularly for a junub. The core ruling: if a person in a state of janabah or minor impurity fears that using water (ghusl or wudu) will cause death or severe illness due to cold, he may perform tayammum. Abu Hanifa permits this regardless of whether one is inside or outside a town, while his two companions restrict the permission to outside the town only. The text notes that for a person with minor hadath (muhdith), some scholars allowed tayammum, but the relied-upon view prohibits it, citing the general principle that fear of cold in wudu is usually imaginary. The ruling for the junub is conditional: he must be unable to heat the water, afford a bathhouse, find warm clothing, or shelter. If any of these are available, tayammum becomes impermissible by consensus. The two companions argue that within a town, one can typically find hot water or a bathhouse, so tayammum is not allowed. Some later scholars reconciled the disagreement by noting a change in the timing of payment for bathhouses, while others based it on a more fundamental dispute about seeking water from companions. The proof for Abu Hanifa's position is the hadith of Amr ibn al-'As, who was junub on a cold night, feared death, performed tayammum, and led the prayer. The Prophet approved his action without asking if he was in a town or wilderness, and did not order him to repeat the prayer, indicating that the general reason (fear of harm) permits tayammum universally.

Key Terms
برد (bard): Extreme cold that poses a threat to life or health if water touches the body.
مصر (misr): A town or city where amenities like bathhouses and heating might be available.
سرية (sariyya): A military detachment sent by the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition must be met for a junub to perform tayammum due to cold according to Abu Hanifa?
A) He must be outside the town only.
B) He must not be able to heat the water, afford a bathhouse, find warm clothing, or shelter.
C) He must have no money at all.
D) He must have a minor hadath, not janabah.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum due to cold for a junub is permitted only when there is genuine fear of harm and no means to obtain warmth; Abu Hanifa's view, supported by the hadith of Amr ibn al-'As, applies inside towns, but the Sahibayn restrict it to outside; the mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa with strict conditions.

Tayammum for the Muhdith Due to Cold: The Dispute
Refinement of the ruling on tayammum for cold

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum for a muhdith fearing cold and explain the exception when fear of limb loss is certain.

Core Idea
Tayammum for cold is generally prohibited, but certain fear of losing a limb may allow it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq navigates a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: whether a person in a state of minor hadath (muhdith) may perform tayammum out of fear of harm from cold. The default position is prohibition, but some later shaykhs allowed it. The author refines the discussion by highlighting an exception when the fear is for a specific limb—a case that tests the general rule.

Guided Path
1
State the general Hanafi position
Recall that the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) prohibits tayammum for a muhdith due to cold. This is the starting point of the dispute.
The harm from cold is usually not considered severe enough to justify tayammum.
2
Identify the conflicting view
Some shaykhs (e.g., as cited in al-Asrar) permit tayammum for cold. Note that this is a minority position within the madhhab.
This view is later subjected to criticism.
3
Analyze the refinement: the case of limb loss
Examine the specific scenario where a person fears his leg may fall off due to cold. Shaykh Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam and al-Halabi allow tayammum here, arguing that this is essentially the same as the earlier dispute but with concrete harm.
This challenges the blanket prohibition.
4
Apply the legal principle of harm
The Quranic verse 'Do not kill yourselves' (4:29) supports allowing tayammum when harm is certain. If the fear is verified or strongly conjectured, tayammum is permissible by consensus.
The key is certainty: ghalaba al-zann (strong conjecture) suffices.
5
Note the author's caution
The author (Ibn Nujaym) signals that later in the text he will weaken this permissive view, arguing that the correct action is wiping (mash) over khuffs, not tayammum.
This anticipates a further refinement based on available alternatives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وجوازه للمحدث قول بعض المشايخ) قال الرملي : أي جواز التيمم عند خوف البرد له قول بعض المشايخ واختاره في الأسرار كما نص عليه في النهر وأقول : يشكل على تصحيح عدم الجواز مسألة المسح الآتية في بابه وهي جواز التيمم بعد مضي المدة إذا خاف سقوط رجله من البرد كما حققه الشيخ كمال الدين بن الهمام واختاره الحلبي في شرح المنية وليس هو إلا تيمم المحدث لخوفه على عضوه فحينئذ يتجه اختيار قول بعض المشايخ وقد ظهر بقوله كأنه» والله تعالى أعلم لعدم اعتبار ذلك الخ» أنه لو تحقق أو غلب على الظن يجوز اتفاقاً وذلك لأن مثله مدفوع عنا بالنص الشريف تأمل اهـ. ولكن سيأتي منه في محله تضعيف هذا التصحيح الذي نقله عن ابن الهمام وأن ظاهر المتون أن الواجب عند خوف سقوط رجله من البرد هو المسح لا التيمم وستطلع إن شاء الله تعالى على تأييدنا له بالنقول الصريحة.
His saying: (And its permissibility for one with minor hadath is the saying of some shaykhs.) Al-Ramli said: That is, the permissibility of tayammum when fearing cold has a saying of some shaykhs, and he chose it in al-Asrar, as stated in al-Nahr. And I say: This corrects the non-permissibility with the issue of wiping (mash) that will come in its chapter, which is the permissibility of tayammum after the period passes if he fears that his leg will fall off due to cold, as investigated by Shaykh Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam, and chosen by al-Halabi in Sharh al-Munya. And it is nothing but tayammum of a muhdith due to fear for his limb. Therefore, choosing the saying of some shaykhs is appropriate. And it has appeared by his saying 'as if' and Allah knows best regarding the non-consideration of that fear, that if it is confirmed or strongly conjectured, it is permissible by agreement, because the like of it is repelled from us by the noble text. Ponder. End. But later in its proper place, the author will weaken this correction that he transmitted from Ibn al-Humam, and that the apparent meaning of the texts is that when fearing the falling of his leg due to cold, the obliged action is wiping (mash), not tayammum. And you will see, if Allah wills, our support for that with explicit quotations.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage addresses a subtle point: whether a person in a state of minor hadath (muhdith) can perform tayammum due to fear of cold. The text initially states that some shaykhs permit it, but the correct (sahih) view is that it is not permitted. However, a later discussion complicates this: Al-Ramli notes that in the chapter of wiping (mash), there is a ruling that if a person fears that his leg might fall off due to cold after the period of wiping has passed (i.e., for a person who has made masah on khuffs and the period ends), he may perform tayammum. That is essentially a tayammum for a muhdith fearing for a limb. This suggests that the absolute prohibition for muhdith is not watertight. If the fear is certain (haqqaqa) or highly probable (ghalaba al-zann), tayammum is permissible by agreement, because the shari'a does not require one to risk losing a limb. However, the author (Ibn Nujaym?) is preparing to weaken this view later, arguing that the correct opinion is that the required action in such a case is wiping (mash), not tayammum, and the student will see explicit support for that. This shows the dynamic nature of fiqh deliberations.

Key Terms
مسح (mash): Wiping over khuffs (leather socks) as a substitute for washing feet in wudu; here, it is an alternative to tayammum when the fear is for the foot.
غلب على الظن (ghalaba al-zann): Strong conjecture; a level of certainty less than absolute but sufficient to justify a legal concession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does tayammum become permissible for a muhdith fearing cold?
A) Whenever the temperature is below freezing.
B) Only if the fear is verified or strongly conjectured and no alternative like mash exists.
C) Never, even if the limb is at risk.
D) Only for a person who is already in the state of janabah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi default prohibits tayammum for cold, but certain fear of severe harm creates an exception—though alternatives like mash are preferred.

Tayammum for Junub Due to Cold: Conditions and Proof
Ruling with proof on tayammum for junub due to cold

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a junub may perform tayammum due to cold according to Abu Hanifa, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement with the Sahibayn using the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Tayammum due to cold is wajib only when unable to heat water, pay for a bathhouse, find warmth or shelter—and the Prophet's approval of Amr's action proves generality.

This lesson examines a key ruling in taharah: the permissibility of tayammum for a person in major impurity (junub) when extreme cold makes ghusl harmful. We will unpack the conditions set by Imam Abu Hanifa, the objection of his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and the primary proof from the hadith of Amr ibn al-As. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply usul principles to a concrete fiqh case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act under discussion is tayammum as a substitute for ghusl due to cold. According to Abu Hanifa, it is permissible (and in fact wajib when ghusl is obligatory) both inside and outside a town, subject to conditions.
The Sahibayn restrict this to outside the town only.
2
List the conditions for permissibility
Note the four conditions from Abu Hanifa: inability to heat water, inability to pay the bathhouse fee, lack of a garment to warm oneself, and lack of a shelter. These establish that tayammum is only allowed when ghusl is genuinely impossible.
These conditions are mentioned in al-Bada'i' and Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's objection
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that tayammum due to cold is not permissible inside a town (misr), reasoning that in a town one can typically find means to heat water or afford a bathhouse.
The mashayikh differed on whether this is a time-based or substantive disagreement.
4
Examine the hadith proof
Analyze the hadith of Amr ibn al-As: he led prayer while junub, having performed tayammum due to cold. The Prophet approved his action without asking about location, indicating the excuse is general (whether desert or town).
The hadith is found in Ghazwat Dhat al-Salasil; it is ahad but its dalalah is qat'i according to the Hanafis.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's, as supported by the hadith. The generality of the cause ('illah) means the ruling applies in all places where the conditions are met.
This is the position adopted by al-Marghinani and later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يمرضه تيمم، سواء كان خارج المصر أو فيه. وعندهما لا يتيمم فيه. كذا في الكافي . ثم أعلم أن جوازه للجنب عند أبي حنيفة مشروط بأن لا يقدر على تسخين الماء ولا على أجرة الحمام في المصر ولا يجد ثوباً يتدفأ فيه ولا مكاناً يأويه كما أفاده في البدائع وشرح الجامع الصغير لقاضيخان، فصار الأصل أنه متی قدر على الاغتسال بوجه من الوجوه لا يباح له التيمم إجماعاً. وقالا : لا يجوز التيمم للبرد في المصر. وقد اختلف هذه نشأ المشايخ فمنهم من جعل الخلاف بينهم في اختلاف زمان لا برهان بناء على أن عن أجر الحمام في زمانهما يؤخذ بعد الدخول فإذا عجز عن الثمن دخل ثم تعلل بالعسرة وفي زمانه قبله فيعذر، ومنهم من جعله برهانياً بناه على الخلاف في جواز التيمم لغير الواجد قبل الطلب من رفيقه إذا كان له رفيق. فعلى هذا يقيد منعهما بأن يترك طلب الماء الحار من جميع أهل المصر، أما إذا طلب فمنع فإنه يجوز عندهما، والظاهر قوله لأنه لا يكلف الطهارة بالماء إلا إذا قدر عليه بالملك أو الشراء وعند انتفاء هذه القدرة يتحقق العجز، ولهذا لم يفصل المنية العلامة ابن أمير حاج أخذاً مما اتفقت عليه كلمتهم في ماء الوضوء إذا كان يباع ولا يوجد مجاناً. قوله: (تيمم سواء كان الخ) لأبي حنيفة ما روي عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بعث سرية وأمر عليهم عمرو بن العاص وكان ذلك في غزوة ذات السلاسل فلما رجعوا شكوا منه أشياء من جملتها أنهم قالوا: صلى بنا وهو جنب فذكر للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال : يا رسول الله أجنبت في ليلة باردة فخفت على نفسي الهلاك لو اغتسلت فذكرت ما قال الله تعالى ولا تقتلوا أنفسكم إن الله كان بكم رحيماً [النساء : ٢٩] فتيممت وصليت بهم فقال لهم رسول الله : ألا ترون صاحبكم كيف نظر لنفسه ولكم ولم يأمره بالإعادة ولم يستفسر أنه كان في مفازة أو مصر وعلل بعلة عامة وهو خوف الهلاك، ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم استصوب رأيه والحكم يتعمم بعموم العلة اهـ حلية.
Tayammum makes him ill, whether he is outside the town or in it. And according to them (Sahibayn) he does not perform tayammum in it. As in al-Kafi. Then know that its permissibility for the junub according to Abu Hanifa is conditional on his not being able to heat water, nor pay the bathhouse fee in the town, nor find a garment to warm himself in, nor a place to shelter, as stated in al-Bada'i' and Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir of Qadikhan. So the principle is that whenever he can perform ghusl in any way, tayammum is not permissible for him by consensus. And the two said: Tayammum due to cold is not permissible in the town. The mashayikh differed about the nature of this disagreement: some considered it a difference of time, not argument, because the bathhouse fee in their time was taken after entry, so if he lacked the price, he would enter and then plead hardship, while in his time it is taken before, so he is excused. Others considered it argument-based, founded on the difference regarding tayammum for one who does not have water before asking his companion if he has a companion. Accordingly, their prohibition is restricted to his abandoning the request for hot water from all the people of the town. But if he asks and is refused, then it is permissible according to them. And the apparent is his statement (Abu Hanifa's) because he is not obligated to purify with water unless he is able to do so by ownership or purchase. When this ability is absent, inability is realized. That is why the commentator of al-Munyah, Ibn Amir Hajj, did not differentiate, taking from what their words agreed upon concerning water for wudu if it is sold and not available free. His statement: (Tayammum, whether he is, etc.) For Abu Hanifa, what is narrated from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, that he sent a detachment and appointed Amr ibn al-As over them, and that was in the expedition of Dhat al-Salasil. When they returned, they complained about him, among which they said: He led us in prayer while in a state of janabah. So it was mentioned to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and he said: O Messenger of Allah, I became junub on a cold night and feared destruction if I performed ghusl, so I remembered the saying of Allah Almighty: 'Do not kill yourselves, indeed Allah is Merciful to you' (4:29). So I performed tayammum and led them in prayer. The Messenger of Allah said to them: Do you not see your companion how he considered for himself and for you? And he did not order him to repeat, nor did he ask whether he was in a desert or a town. He gave a general cause, namely fear of destruction. And the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, approved his opinion, and the ruling is generalized by the generality of the cause. End quote from al-Hilya.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It discusses the permissibility of tayammum (dry ablution) for a person in a state of major impurity (junub) due to extreme cold. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, tayammum is permissible both inside and outside a town (misr) if the person cannot heat water, cannot afford the bathhouse fee, and cannot find a garment to warm himself or a place to shelter. This is based on the hadith of Amr ibn al-As, who performed tayammum on a cold night and led the prayer, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) approved of his action without inquiring about the location. The hadith proves that the excuse of fear of harm is general. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that tayammum is not permissible within the town. The mashayikh differed on the nature of this disagreement: some saw it as a difference of time (whether the bathhouse fee is paid before or after entry), while others saw it as a substantive disagreement based on whether one must ask his companion for water before resorting to tayammum. According to Abu Hanifa, the person is only obligated to perform wudu or ghusl if he has ownership or the ability to purchase water; otherwise, inability is established. The hadith of Amr ibn al-As is cited as the primary evidence, showing that the Prophet deemed his action correct and did not order repetition, indicating that the ruling is general for any place.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
جنب (junub): Person in major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
مصر (misr): Town or city with established civilization.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for Abu Hanifa's ruling that tayammum due to cold is permissible for a junub even inside a town?
A) The hadith of Amr ibn al-As where the Prophet approved his tayammum without asking location.
B) The Quranic verse on not killing oneself.
C) Analogy (qiyas) with the case of missing water.
D) Consensus (ijma') of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum due to cold for a junub is valid both in and outside a town when genuine inability to perform ghusl exists, as confirmed by the general 'illah in the hadith of Amr ibn al-As.
