Tayammum for the Muhdith Due to Cold: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Resolution
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum for muhdith due to cold

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct Hanafi position on tayammum for a muhdith fearing cold, explain the reasoning, and evaluate the opposing view.

Core Idea
Tayammum for minor impurity due to cold is generally not allowed; the fear is a delusion, not a valid excuse.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a dispute among later Hanafi scholars regarding tayammum for a person in minor ritual impurity (muhdith) who fears harm from cold during wudu. The correct view, supported by major authorities, is that tayammum is not permitted because the fear is usually baseless. However, some scholars allowed it by analogy with a case where tayammum is permitted after time for fear of losing a limb. We will analyze the arguments and see why the majority position is stronger.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its authority
Identify the correct Hanafi position from Fatawa Qadikhan and Khulasa: tayammum for a muhdith due to cold is not permissible.
Note that the author of al-Mustasfa claims consensus on the correct view.
2
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
From Fath al-Qadir, the fear is considered a delusion (wahm) because wudu does not typically cause such harm.
This reasoning is key to understanding why the fear is not a valid excuse.
3
Identify the opposing view and its evidence
Some mashayikh allowed tayammum, citing the case of a person who fears his foot falling off due to cold after the time expires, where tayammum is permitted.
Al-Ramli and others transmitted this view.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opposition
The Hanafi response is that the analogy is flawed: in the cited case, the obligation is actually masah (wiping), not tayammum. The texts indicate masah, not tayammum.
The author later weakens the opposing correction.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: the muhdith must still perform wudu (possibly with warm water); if fear is confirmed, he may perform masah over socks, not tayammum.
This clarifies the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوازه للمحدث قول بعض المشايخ والصحيح أنه لا يجوز له التيمم كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان والخلاصة وغيرهما. وذكر المصنف في المستصفى أنه بالإجماع على الأصح. قال في فتح القدير : وكأنه والله أعلم لعدم اعتبار ذلك الخوف بناء على أنه مجرد وهم إذ لا يتحقق ذلك في الوضوء عادة ا هـ . قوله : (وجوازه للمحدث قول بعض المشايخ قال الرملي : أي جواز التيمم عند خوف البرد له قول بعض المشايخ واختاره في الأسرار كما نص عليه في النهر وأقول : يشكل على تصحيح عدم الجواز مسألة المسح الآتية في بابه وهي جواز التيمم بعد مضي المدة إذا خاف سقوط رجله من البرد كما حققه الشيخ كمال الدين بن الهمام واختاره الحلبي في شرح المنية وليس هو إلا تيمم المحدث لخوفه على عضوه فحينئذ يتجه اختيار قول بعض المشايخ وقد ظهر بقوله كأنه» والله تعالى أعلم لعدم اعتبار ذلك الخ» أنه لو تحقق أو غلب على الظن يجوز اتفاقاً وذلك لأن مثله مدفوع عنا بالنص الشريف تأمل اهـ. ولكن سيأتي منه في محله تضعيف هذا التصحيح الذي نقله عن ابن الهمام وأن ظاهر المتون أن الواجب عند خوف سقوط رجله من البرد هو المسح لا التيمم وستطلع إن شاء الله تعالى على تأييدنا له بالنقول الصريحة. قوله :
And its permissibility for the muhdith is the saying of some mashayikh, and the correct view is that tayammum is not permissible for him, as in Fatawa Qadikhan, al-Khulasa, and others. The author mentioned in al-Mustasfa that it is by consensus according to the most correct. He said in Fath al-Qadir: It is as if — and Allah knows best — because that fear is not considered, based on it being mere delusion since it is not realized in wudu usually. His statement: (And its permissibility for the muhdith is the saying of some mashayikh) al-Ramli said: Meaning the permissibility of tayammum when fearing cold is a saying of some mashayikh, and he chose it in al-Asrar as stated in al-Nahr. And I say: There is a problem with correcting the non-permissibility by the issue of wiping (masah) coming in its chapter, which is the permissibility of tayammum after the time has passed when he fears his foot falling off due to cold, as verified by Shaykh Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam and chosen by al-Halabi in Sharh al-Munyah. And it is nothing but the tayammum of a muhdith due to fear for his limb. So then the opinion of some mashayikh is justified. And it has appeared by his saying 'as if' — Allah knows best — that if it is certain or dominant in his opinion, it is permissible by agreement, because the like of it is repelled from us by the noble text. Reflect. But there will come from him in its place a weakening of this correction that he transmitted from Ibn al-Humam, and that the apparent from the texts is that the obligatory when fearing the falling of his foot from cold is wiping (masah), not tayammum. And you will see, Allah willing, our confirmation of that with explicit quotations. His statement:
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of tayammum for a person in a state of minor impurity (hadath) due to extreme cold. The general position of the Hanafi school, as recorded in Fatawa Qadikhan and al-Khulasa, is that it is not permissible. The author of al-Mustasfa even claims consensus on this. The reasoning, given in Fath al-Qadir, is that the fear of harm from cold during wudu is usually negligible; it is a mere delusion because wudu does not typically cause such harm. However, al-Ramli raises a challenge based on the issue of masah (wiping over socks) after the time has passed: if a person fears that his foot may fall off due to extreme cold, he is permitted to perform tayammum after the time elapses. This is a case of tayammum for a muhdith due to fear for a limb. By analogy, if the fear is real or overwhelming, tayammum for the muhdith due to cold should also be permitted. The author then notes that this correction by Ibn al-Humam will be critiqued later, and the correct view is that wiping (masah) is the required action, not tayammum. Thus, the ruling remains that tayammum for the muhdith due to cold is not allowed, except in cases of confirmed fear.

Key Terms
محدث (muhdith): Person in a state of minor ritual impurity (hadath) that requires wudu.
وهم (wahm): Unfounded fear or delusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a person with minor impurity (muhdith) who fears cold during wudu?
A) He may perform tayammum.
B) He must perform wudu; tayammum is not allowed.
C) He may wipe over his socks (masah) only.
D) He is excused and can pray without purification.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum for a person in minor impurity due to cold is not permitted; the person must perform wudu, and only in cases of confirmed fear may he turn to wiping over socks.

Tayammum When Unable to Purchase Water on Credit
Refines the ruling on tayammum based on financial ability to buy water on credit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum when one lacks cash but has absent wealth, and apply the condition that absent wealth triggers an obligation to purchase water on credit.

Core Idea
Tayammum is not permitted if water can be obtained on credit and one has the ability to pay later.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the author addresses a nuanced issue: when a person has no cash on hand but could obtain water on credit. Some earlier scholars loosely permitted tayammum in such cases, while others restricted it due to potential deception. The author resolves the matter by distinguishing between having absent wealth and having no wealth at all. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of tayammum in contemporary scenarios involving credit and remote assets.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
Determine that the act under discussion is tayammum (dry ablution) and its general permissibility when water is not available. Recognize that the default ruling is permission (ibaha) for tayammum when one cannot obtain water.
This is the starting point from the Hanafi school: tayammum is a valid substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is inaccessible.
2
Examine the contested view
Some mashayikh argued that tayammum is not allowed in contemporary times because of deceptive practices, such as entering a bathhouse (where the fee is charged after service) and then claiming inability to pay. This view would restrict tayammum even when one lacks cash.
This is a critical refinement: the author is rejecting this broad restriction as unfounded.
3
Analyze the refinement from Fath al-Qadir
The author of Fath al-Qadir clarifies that the decisive factor is the presence of absent wealth. If one has no money at hand and no absent wealth, tayammum is allowed. If one has absent wealth (e.g., money at home or in a bank account), then purchasing water on credit is obligatory, and tayammum is not permitted.
This refinement prevents tayammum from being used when one is actually able to secure water through credit.
4
Apply the rule to the hired worker example
A hired worker who knows water is within half a mile must go and fetch it; he is not excused for tayammum. If his employer prevents him, he may perform tayammum but must repeat the prayer later, and if he prays another prayer while remembering the situation, that prayer is invalid.
This example illustrates that physical access to water also matters, and the rule about credit applies to financial access.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العلماء فيما إذا لم يكن معه ثمن الماء بين إمكان أخذه بثمن مؤجل بالحيلة على ذلك أو لا، بل أطلقوا جواز التيمم إذ ذاك فما أطلقه بعض المشايخ من عدم جواز التيمم في هذا الزمان بناء على أن أجر الحمام يؤخذ بعد الدخول فيتعلل بالعسرة بعده فيه نظر. كذا في فتح القدير. ولا شك في هذا فيما يظهر لأنه تغرير لم يأذن الشرع فيه، ومن ادعى إباحته فضلاً عن تعيينه فعليه البيان ولا يخفى أن مراد المحقق في فتح القدير من قوله «ليس لا مال له غائب أيضاً فحينئذ لا يلزمه الشراء بالنسيئة، أما إذا لم يكن معه مال وله مال غائب فإنه يلزمه الشراء بالنسيئة كما أشار إليه شارح منية المصلي تلميذ المحقق وفي المبتغى الغين المعجمة : أجير لا يجد الماء إن علم أنه يجده في نصف ميل لا يعذر في التيمم، وإن لم يأذن له المستأجر يتيمم ويصلي ثم يعيد ولو صلى صلاة أخرى وهو يذكر هذه تفسد ا هـ.
The scholars regarding when he does not have the price of water, whether it is possible to take it with a deferred price by trick or not. Rather, they generally allow tayammum then. So what some mashayikh said about the impermissibility of tayammum in this time based on the bathhouse fee being taken after entry, so he claims difficulty after entry, is problematic. As in Fath al-Qadir. There is no doubt about this apparently, because it is deception not permitted by the sharia. Whoever claims its permissibility, let alone its obligation, must provide proof. It is not hidden that the intention of al-Muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir from his statement 'he has no absent wealth also' is that then he is not obliged to purchase on credit. As for when he has no money but has absent wealth, then he is obliged to purchase on credit, as indicated by the commentator of Munyat al-Musalli, the student of al-Muhaqqiq. And in al-Mughni: a hired worker who does not find water, if he knows that he will find it within half a mile, he is not excused for tayammum. If the employer does not allow him, he performs tayammum and prays, then repeats, and if he prays another prayer while remembering this, it becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage deals with the issue of performing tayammum when one does not have the cash to purchase water but could obtain it on credit. The general ruling is that if a person has no money at all, he is permitted to perform tayammum. However, some mashayikh argued that in contemporary times (of the author), tayammum is not allowed because the bathhouse fee is only charged after entry; one could enter and then claim inability, which is deceptive. The author of Fath al-Qadir criticizes this view, calling it unjustified deception. He clarifies that the ruling depends on whether the person has absent wealth (e.g., money back at home). If he has no money and no absent wealth, he is not required to purchase on credit. But if he has absent wealth, he must purchase water on credit, and thus cannot perform tayammum. An example is given: a hired worker who knows he can find water within half a mile must go and fetch it; if the employer prevents him, he may perform tayammum but must repeat the prayer later.

Key Terms
نسيئة (nasi'ah): Sale on credit; purchasing with deferred payment.
تغرير (taghrir): Deception or fraud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Fath al-Qadir, if a person has no cash but possesses absent wealth (e.g., money at home), what is his obligation regarding water?
A) He may perform tayammum because he has no cash.
B) He must purchase water on credit.
C) He must heat snow for water.
D) He is excused from all purification.

Key Takeaway
The key factor for tayammum is not just lack of cash, but also lack of ability to obtain water via credit or absent wealth.

Tayammum: Excuses and the Rule of Repetition
Lists excuses for tayammum and discusses repetition of prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the excuses that permit tayammum, apply the principle distinguishing obstacles from Allah vs. from humans, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on repetition.

Core Idea
If the obstacle to wudu is from humans, prayer must be repeated; if from Allah, no repetition.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the excuses that permit tayammum, particularly fear of an enemy, wild animal, thirst, or lack of tools. The commentator extracts a key principle: the source of the obstacle determines whether the prayer must be repeated. This leads to a debate within the Hanafi school regarding whether an enemy is a human or divine obstacle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the excuses
List the four excuses mentioned: fear of enemy, wild animal, thirst, lack of tools. Understand why each makes water inaccessible.
2
Understand the principle of harm
The passage states that if going to water leads to prohibited harm (like self-destruction), inability is established. This is based on the Quranic prohibition of throwing oneself into destruction.
Quran 2:195
3
Analyze the examples
Review the examples: trust property, woman fearing fasiq, debtor, captive, slave threatened by master. Note how each relates to the excuse.
4
Distinguish the source of the obstacle
The passage explicitly states: if the excuse is from Allah, no repetition; if from humans, repetition obligatory. This is the key legal principle.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Two views are presented: Miraj al-Diraya (no repetition for enemy, as enemy is creation of Allah) vs. al-Nihaya (repetition required, as enemy's action is human choice). The commentator prefers al-Nihaya, analogizing with the slave example.
This dispute affects practical fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (أو خوف عدوّ أو سبع أو عطش أو فقد آلة يعني يجوز التيمم لهذه الأعذار لأن لا الماء معدوم معنى صورة، أما إذا كان بينه وبين الماء عدوّ آدمياً أو غيره يخاف على نفسه إذا أتاه فلأن إلقاء النفس في التهلكة حرام فيتحقق العجز عن استعمال الماء، وسواء خاف على نفسه أو ماله. كذا في العناية وفي المبتغى ولو كان عنده أمانة يخاف عليها إن ذهب إلى يتيمم. وفي التوشيح : إذا خافت المرأة على نفسها بأن كان الماء عند فاسق أو خاف المديون المفلس من الحبس بأن كان صاحب الدين عند الماء. وفي الخلاصة وفتاوى قاضيخان وغيرهما : الأسير في يد العدوّ إذا منعه الكافر عن الوضوء والصلاة يتيمم ويصلي بالإيماء ثم يعيد إذا خرج، وكذا لو قال لعبده إن توضأت حبستك أو قتلتك فإنه يصلي بالتيمم ثم يعيد كالمحبوس لأن طهارة التيمم لم تظهر في منع وجوب الإعادة وفي التنجيس: رجل أراد أن يتوضأ فمنعه إنسان عن أن يتوضأ بوعيد ؛ قيل ينبغي أن يتيمم ويصلي ثم يعيد الصلاة بعد ما زال عنه لأن هذا عذر جاء من قبل العباد فلا يسقط فرض الوضوء عنه ا هـ. فعلم منه أن العذر إن كان من قبل الله تعالى لا تجب الإعادة وإن كان من قبل العبد وجبت الإعادة. ثم الاختلاف في الخوف من العدوّ هل هو من الله فلا تجب الإعادة. أو هو بسبب العبد فتجب الإعادة؟ ذهب صاحب معراج الدراية إلى الأول، وذهب صاحب النهاية إلى الثاني، والذي يظهر ترجيح ما في النهاية لما نقلناه مسألة من منع السيد عبده بوعيد من الحبس أو وقع (يتيمم ويصلي بالإيماء) أقول : إن كان المنع من الوضوء فقط كما هو ظاهر كلام الدرر يتيمم ويصلي بالركوع والسجود وإن كان من الوضوء والصلاة معاً يتيمم ويصلي بالإيماء ثم يعيد الصلاة في الصورتين إذا زال المانع. كذا في حاشية الدرر للعلامة نوح قوله فلا تجب الإعادة) وبه جزم الشرنبلالي في شرح نور الإيضاح قوله : (معراج الدراية إلى (الأول) أي إلى كونه من قبل الله تعالى . قوله : (صاحب النهاية إلى الثاني أي إلى كونه من قبل العباد قوله : (وتحرر إن المراد بالخوف من
His statement: (or fear of enemy or wild animal or thirst or lack of tools) means that tayammum is permissible for these excuses because water is nonexistent in meaning and form. As for when between him and water there is an enemy, human or otherwise, he fears for himself if he goes to it, then because throwing oneself into destruction is forbidden, so inability to use water is realized. And it is the same whether he fears for himself or his wealth. As in al-Inayah and al-Mughni. And if he has a trust (amanah) he fears for if he goes, he performs tayammum. In al-Tawshih: if a woman fears for herself, as when the water is with a corrupt person (fasiq), or a bankrupt debtor fears imprisonment because the creditor is at the water source. In al-Khulasa and Fatawa Qadikhan and others: a captive in the hands of the enemy, if the disbeliever prevents him from wudu and prayer, he performs tayammum and prays with gestures (ima'), then repeats when he gets out. Similarly, if an owner says to his slave: if you perform wudu, I will imprison or kill you, then he prays with tayammum and then repeats, like a prisoner, because the purity of tayammum does not prevent the obligation of repetition. In al-Tanjiis: a man wanted to perform wudu, but a person prevented him with threats; it is said that he should perform tayammum and pray, then repeat the prayer after the prevention is removed, because this excuse is from the side of the servants (humans), so the obligation of wudu is not dropped. So it is understood from this that if the excuse is from Allah (e.g., natural causes), repetition is not obligatory; if it is from the servant (human), repetition is obligatory. Then there is a difference of opinion regarding fear of an enemy: is it from Allah so no repetition? Or is it due to the servant so repetition is required? The author of Miraj al-Diraya went to the first, and the author of al-Nihaya went to the second. What appears is the preference of al-Nihaya, based on the case we narrated of the master preventing his slave with threats of imprisonment or... (the text continues:) (He performs tayammum and prays with gestures) I say: if the prevention is only from wudu, as appears from the words of al-Durar, he performs tayammum and prays with ruku and sujud. If the prevention is from both wudu and prayer, he performs tayammum and prays with gestures, then repeats the prayer in both cases when the obstacle is removed. As in Hashiyat al-Durar by Allamah Nuh. His statement: so repetition is not obligatory) and al-Shurunbulali asserted this in Sharh Nur al-Idah. His statement: (Miraj al-Diraya to the first) i.e., to it being from Allah. His statement: (the author of al-Nihaya to the second) i.e., to it being from the servants. His statement: (and it is determined that what is meant by fear of...
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage lists additional excuses that permit tayammum: fear of an enemy (human or non-human), fear of a wild animal, fear of thirst (if going to water would cause excessive thirst), and lack of tools (such as a rope to draw water). The rationale is that if accessing water would lead to harm that is prohibited (like throwing oneself into destruction), the inability is established. The examples include a person protecting an entrusted item, a woman fearing a corrupt person, a prisoner of war prevented by disbelievers, a slave threatened by his master, and a person threatened by another. The key principle derived is: if the obstacle is from Allah (natural causes like extreme cold), the prayer performed with tayammum does not need to be repeated. If the obstacle is from other humans (like a tyrant preventing wudu), then the prayer must be repeated later. This leads to a dispute: is an enemy considered an obstacle from Allah (since the enemy is a creation) or from humans? The author of Miraj al-Diraya considers it from Allah (no repetition), while the author of al-Nihaya considers it from humans (repetition required). The commentator favors al-Nihaya, citing the case of the slave threatened by his master, which is clearly a human obstacle. The passage also clarifies that if the prevention is only from wudu, the person can still pray with normal movements; if both wudu and prayer are prevented, he prays with gestures and repeats later.

Key Terms
إيماء (ima'): Gestures; performing prayer movements by nodding or moving the head when unable to bow and prostrate.
عذر (udhr): Legal excuse that permits dispensation such as tayammum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, if a person performs tayammum due to fear of an enemy soldier, what is the ruling regarding repetition of the prayer?
A) The prayer is valid and does not need to be repeated.
B) The prayer must be repeated when the enemy is gone.
C) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated immediately.
D) The person should make up the prayer with qada.

Key Takeaway
The prayer performed with tayammum due to a human-caused obstacle must be repeated; if due to a natural cause, it does not need repetition.

Obligation to Purchase Water on Credit When You Have Hidden Wealth
Discussing conditions under which tayammum is not permissible because water can be obtained via credit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum for a person with hidden wealth and apply the principle that hidden wealth obligates purchasing water on credit.

Core Idea
Hidden wealth (mal gha'ib) makes a person capable – tayammum is invalid; purchase on credit is wajib.

A common assumption is that if you have no cash in hand, you can perform tayammum. But the Hanafi school looks at your overall financial ability. If you possess hidden wealth – such as a debt owed to you – you are considered able to obtain water on credit. This lesson unpacks that ruling and the reasoning behind it, showing that tayammum is a concession only for genuine inability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Person and Their Situation
The text describes a traveler who has no money (cash) but does have hidden wealth (e.g., a debt). Identify that this person is not immediately insolvent.
Hidden wealth here means property not physically present, like a loan receivable.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling
According to the verified view (mufta bihi), such a person is obligated to purchase water on credit. Tayammum is not permitted.
3
Understand the Reasoning (dalil)
The proof is logical: since he can obtain water by using his hidden wealth as security for credit, he is capable. Claiming hardship after entering a bathhouse is a deceptive excuse not sanctioned by Sharia.
This is an example of istihsan based on maslahah.
4
Recognise the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Earlier mashayikh absolutely permitted tayammum in such cases. The later muhaqqiqun (Ibn al-Humam, commentator of Munyat al-Musalli) refined this to require purchase if hidden wealth exists.
The later position is relied upon for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العلماء فيما إذا لم يكن معه ثمن الماء بين إمكان أخذه بثمن مؤجل بالحيلة على ذلك أو لا، بل أطلقوا جواز التيمم إذ ذاك فما أطلقه بعض المشايخ من عدم جواز التيمم في هذا الزمان بناء على أن أجر الحمام يؤخذ بعد الدخول فيتعلل بالعسرة بعده فيه نظر. كذا في فتح القدير. ولا شك في هذا فيما يظهر لأنه تغرير لم يأذن الشرع فيه، ومن ادعى إباحته فضلاً عن تعيينه فعليه البيان ولا يخفى أن مراد المحقق في فتح القدير من قوله «ليس لا مال له غائب أيضاً فحينئذ لا يلزمه الشراء بالنسيئة، أما إذا لم يكن معه مال وله مال غائب فإنه يلزمه الشراء بالنسيئة كما أشار إليه شارح منية المصلي تلميذ المحقق وفي المبتغى الغين المعجمة : أجير لا يجد الماء إن علم أنه يجده في نصف ميل لا يعذر في التيمم، وإن لم يأذن له المستأجر يتيمم ويصلي ثم يعيد ولو صلى صلاة أخرى وهو يذكر هذه تفسد ا هـ.
The scholars [discussed] regarding the case when one does not have the price of water: whether it is possible to take it on credit through a legal stratagem or not. Rather, they absolutely permitted tayammum in that case. So what some mashayikh have stated that tayammum is not permissible in this time, based on the fact that the fee for the bathhouse is taken after entering, and thus one excuses himself with hardship after it, is subject to scrutiny. This is stated in Fath al-Qadir. There is no doubt about this, as it appears, because it is a deception that the Law has not permitted. Whoever claims its permissibility, let alone its requirement, must provide evidence. It is not hidden that al-Muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir intended by his statement: 'He who has no money also does not have hidden wealth; then he is not obligated to purchase on credit. But if he has no money but has hidden wealth, then he is obligated to purchase on credit, as indicated by the commentator of Munyat al-Musalli, the student of al-Muhaqqiq. And in al-Mubtagha (with the letter ghain): An employee who does not find water, if he knows that he will find it within half a mile, he is not excused for tayammum. If the employer did not permit him, he performs tayammum and prays, then repeats. And if he prays another prayer while remembering this, it is corrupt. End quote.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the conditions under which a person is not excused from using water and must avoid tayammum. The discussion centers on two scenarios. First, a traveler who has no liquid cash but possesses hidden wealth (e.g., a debt owed to him). The earlier Hanafi scholars generally permitted tayammum in such a case, but later authorities like Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir clarified that if he has hidden wealth, he is obligated to purchase water on credit (al-nasi'ah). This is because the hidden wealth makes him capable of obtaining water, and claiming hardship after entering a bathhouse is a deceptive excuse not sanctioned by the Shari'ah. Second, the case of a hired worker (ajir) who knows that water is available within half a mile. Even if his employer forbids him from going, he is not excused from performing wudu; he must still use water. If he cannot obtain permission, he performs tayammum and prays, but must repeat the prayer later. This shows that the Shari'ah does not consider mere inconvenience or employer restrictions as valid excuses for tayammum when water is realistically accessible.

Key Terms
ثمن الماء (thaman al-ma'): The price or cost of water to be paid for its acquisition.
نسيئة (nasi'ah): Deferred payment; credit sale where water is paid for later.
مال غائب (mal gha'ib): Hidden wealth; property that is not physically present or immediately accessible, such as a debt owed to the person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a person who has no cash but has hidden wealth (مال غائب)?
A) He may perform tayammum without purchasing water.
B) He is obligated to purchase water on credit.
C) He must wait until he receives his hidden wealth.
D) He must borrow money without paying back.

Key Takeaway
Hidden wealth (مال غائب) creates a legal ability to obtain water on credit, making tayammum invalid and purchase on credit obligatory.

Obligation of a Hired Worker to Seek Water Within Half a Mile
Discussing condition of a hired worker when water is within half a mile

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that a hired worker (ajir) must seek water within half a mile, even if his employer forbids him.

Core Idea
Half a mile is the threshold – if water is within reach, a hired worker must use it, employer's permission irrelevant.

The second part of the passage addresses a hired worker who is in a situation where water is scarce. If he knows that water is available within half a mile, he is not excused from performing wudu. If his employer prevents him from going, he must still perform tayammum and later repeat the prayer. This lesson clarifies the duty of a worker and the consequences of ignoring it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Person and His Knowledge
The person is an ajir (hired worker). He does not have water at hand but knows it is available within half a mile.
Knowledge of water's location within that distance is key.
2
State the Ruling
He is not excused for tayammum. He must go and use water for wudu.
3
Consider the Employer's Permission
If the employer does not permit him to go, the worker performs tayammum and prays, but must repeat the prayer. He cannot continue with tayammum knowingly.
Importance: repeating the prayer is required.
4
Understand the Consequence of Ignorance
If he prays another prayer while still remembering that he should have used water, that prayer is corrupt (fasid) and must be repeated.
Knowledge of the obligation matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Fear of Enemy and Obligation to Repeat Prayer after Tayammum
Explaining excuses for tayammum and intra-Hanafi dispute on i'ada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that i'ada is required when the excuse for tayammum arises from a human threat, and distinguish it from excuses from Allah where no i'ada is required.

Core Idea
The obligation to repeat prayer after tayammum depends on the source of the excuse: human threat requires i'ada; natural fear does not.

The Hanafi school permits tayammum when fear of an enemy or wild beast prevents access to water. But after the fear is removed, must the prayer be repeated? This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq reveals a key dispute within the school: some say the fear is from Allah, so no repetition; others say it is from human action, so repetition is wajib. The preferred view reconciles both by distinguishing between a direct threat from a person and general fear without a threat. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rulings of tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tayammum due to fear of an enemy. The ruling is that tayammum is permitted (rukhsah) because going to water would endanger life.
2
State the general principle regarding i'ada
From the cases cited (captive, slave, person threatened), the principle emerges: if the excuse is from Allah (e.g., natural fear without human agency), no i'ada; if the excuse is from human action (e.g., a threat), i'ada is required.
3
Present the two opposing views
Sahib al-Mi'raj al-Diraya held that fear from an enemy is from Allah (no i'ada). Sahib al-Nihayah held it is from people (i'ada required).
4
Examine the reconciliation
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq reconciles: if an explicit threat (wa'id) from a human caused the fear, it is from people and i'ada is required. If there is no threat but only general fear (like from a wild beast), it is from Allah and no i'ada.
Supported by Ibn Amir Hajj and a case from al-Muhit.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The preferred view is that when the fear arises from a human threat, i'ada is wajib. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (أو خوف عدوّ أو سبع أو عطش أو فقد آلة يعني يجوز التيمم لهذه الأعذار لأن لا الماء معدوم معنى صورة، أما إذا كان بينه وبين الماء عدوّ آدمياً أو غيره يخاف على نفسه إذا أتاه فلأن إلقاء النفس في التهلكة حرام فيتحقق العجز عن استعمال الماء، وسواء خاف على نفسه أو ماله. كذا في العناية وفي المبتغى ولو كان عنده أمانة يخاف عليها إن ذهب إلى يتيمم. وفي التوشيح : إذا خافت المرأة على نفسها بأن كان الماء عند فاسق أو خاف المديون المفلس من الحبس بأن كان صاحب الدين عند الماء. وفي الخلاصة وفتاوى قاضيخان وغيرهما : الأسير في يد العدوّ إذا منعه الكافر عن الوضوء والصلاة يتيمم ويصلي بالإيماء ثم يعيد إذا خرج، وكذا لو قال لعبده إن توضأت حبستك أو قتلتك فإنه يصلي بالتيمم ثم يعيد كالمحبوس لأن طهارة التيمم لم تظهر في منع وجوب الإعادة وفي التنجيس: رجل أراد أن يتوضأ فمنعه إنسان عن أن يتوضأ بوعيد ; قيل ينبغي أن يتيمم ويصلي ثم يعيد الصلاة بعد ما زال عنه لأن هذا عذر جاء من قبل العباد فلا يسقط فرض الوضوء عنه ا هـ. فعلم منه أن العذر إن كان من قبل الله تعالى لا تجب الإعادة وإن كان من قبل العبد وجبت الإعادة. ثم الاختلاف في الخوف من العدوّ هل هو من الله فلا تجب الإعادة. أو هو بسبب العبد فتجب الإعادة؟ ذهب صاحب معراج الدراية إلى الأول، وذهب صاحب النهاية إلى الثاني، والذي يظهر ترجيح ما في النهاية لما نقلناه مسألة من منع السيد عبده بوعيد من الحبس أو وقع (يتيمم ويصلي بالإيماء) أقول : إن كان المنع من الوضوء فقط كما هو ظاهر كلام الدرر يتيمم ويصلي بالركوع والسجود وإن كان من الوضوء والصلاة معاً يتيمم ويصلي بالإيماء ثم يعيد الصلاة في الصورتين إذا زال المانع. كذا في حاشية الدرر للعلامة نوح قوله فلا تجب الإعادة) وبه جزم الشرنبلالي في شرح نور الإيضاح قوله : (معراج الدراية إلى (الأول) أي إلى كونه من قبل الله تعالى . قوله : (صاحب النهاية إلى الثاني أي إلى كونه من قبل العباد قوله : (وتحرر إن المراد بالخوف من القتل فإنه ليس فيه إلا الخوف لا المنع الحسي، وكذا ظاهر ما نقلناه عن التنجيس كما لا يخفى لكن قد يقال لا مخالفة بين ما في النهاية والدراية، فإن ما في النهاية محمول على ما إذا حصل وعيد من العبد نشأ منه الخوف فكان هذا من قبل العباد وما في الدراية محمول على ما إذا لم يحصل وعيد من العبد أصلاً بل حصل خوف منه فكان هذا من قبل الله تعالى إذا لم يتقدّمه وعيد بدليل أن صاحب الدراية ذكر مسألة الخوف في الأسير بدار الحرب، وبه يندفع ما ذكره في فتح القدير من أن صاحب الدراية نص على مخالفة ما في النهاية كما لا يخفى. ثم بعد هذا رأيت العلامة ابن أمير حاج صرح بما فهمته فقال : وتحرر أن المراد بالخوف من العدوّ الخوف الذي لم ينشأ عن وعيد من قادر عليه ونحو ذلك كما في الخوف من السبع، ولا بأس بأن يكون مرادهم ذلك. وإنما نسب هذا الخوف إلى الله تعالى في هذه الصورة مع أن فيها وفي غيرها منه تعالى أيضاً خلقاً وإرادة لتجرده في هذه الصورة عن مباشرة سبب له من الغير في حق الخائف. وفي المحيط : ولو حبس في السفر تيمم وصلى أو لا يعيد لأنه انضم عذر السفر إلى العذر الحقيقي والغلب في السفر عدم الماء فتحقق العدم من كل وجه ا هـ.
His statement: 'or fear of an enemy, or a wild beast, or thirst, or lack of equipment' means tayammum is permitted for these excuses because water is considered non-existent in both meaning and form. But if between him and the water there is an enemy, human or otherwise, and he fears for himself if he goes to it, then because throwing oneself into destruction is forbidden, thus inability to use water is realized. Whether he fears for himself or his property, it is the same. Thus in al-Inayah and al-Mubtagha: even if he has an amanah (trust) that he fears for if he goes to perform tayammum. In al-Tawshih: if a woman fears for herself because the water is with a fasiq, or if a bankrupt debtor fears imprisonment because the creditor is near the water. In al-Khulasah and Fatawa Qadikhan and others: a captive in enemy hands, if the disbeliever prevents him from wudu and prayer, he performs tayammum and prays with gestures, then repeats when he gets out. Similarly, if one says to his slave: 'If you perform wudu, I will imprison you or kill you,' he prays with tayammum and then repeats, like the imprisoned one, because the purification of tayammum does not prevent the obligation of repetition. And in al-Tanjis: a man wanted to perform wudu, but another man prevented him with a threat. It is said that he should perform tayammum and pray, then repeat the prayer after the hindrance is removed, because this excuse comes from the people, so the obligation of wudu is not waived. So it is understood: if the excuse is from Allah, no repetition is required; if it is from the servant, repetition is required. Then there is disagreement: is the fear from an enemy from Allah (so no repetition) or is it due to the servant (so repetition required)? The author of Mi'raj al-Diraya held the first; the author of al-Nihayah held the second. The apparent preference is for what is in al-Nihayah due to what we have narrated about the case of the master preventing his slave with a threat of imprisonment. He said: if the prevention is only from wudu, as is apparent from the words of al-Durar, he performs tayammum and prays with bowing and prostration; if it is from both wudu and prayer, he performs tayammum and prays with gestures, then repeats the prayer in both cases when the impediment is removed. Thus in Hashiyat al-Durar by Allamah Nuh. His statement: 'so no repetition is required' – Shurunbulali confirmed this in Sharh Nur al-Idah. His statement: 'Mi'raj al-Diraya to the first' i.e., that it is from Allah. His statement: 'author of al-Nihayah to the second' i.e., that it is from the servants. His statement: 'It is established that what is meant by fear of killing is that there is only fear, not sensory prevention; likewise apparent is what we narrated from al-Tanjis, as is not hidden. But it may be said there is no contradiction between al-Nihayah and al-Diraya, because what is in al-Nihayah is applied to when there is a threat from the servant that gave rise to fear, so this is from the servants; and what is in al-Diraya is applied to when there is no threat from the servant at all, but rather fear arose from him, so this is from Allah if no threat preceded, as evidenced by the author of al-Diraya mentioning the case of fear in the captive in dar al-harb. Thus what was mentioned in Fath al-Qadir about the author of al-Diraya clearly contradicting what is in al-Nihayah is rebutted, as is not hidden. Then after this, I saw Allamah Ibn Amir Hajj explicitly stating what I understood, saying: It is established that what is meant by fear from the enemy is the fear that did not arise from a threat from someone capable, and the like, like fear of a wild beast. It is not wrong that this is their intention. This fear is attributed to Allah in this form, even though in this and other forms it is also from Him in creation and will, because it is free in this form from direct involvement of a cause from another in the right of the fearful one. And in al-Muhit: If a traveler is imprisoned, he performs tayammum and prays and does not repeat, because the excuse of travel is added to the real excuse, and the predominant condition in travel is lack of water, so non-existence is realized from every aspect.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the excuses for tayammum related to fear of enemies, wild beasts, thirst, and lack of equipment. The author first explains that fear of an enemy or beast makes water inaccessible because going to it would endanger life, which is forbidden. He then presents various cases from earlier works: a woman fearing a fasiq, a debtor fearing imprisonment, a captive prevented by an enemy, a slave threatened by his master, and a person threatened by another. From these, the general principle emerges: if the excuse comes directly from Allah (like a natural fear without human agency), no repetition of prayer is required after tayammum; but if the excuse arises from human action (like a threat from another person), repetition is required. Then the author reports a disagreement between two Hanafi scholars: the author of Mi'raj al-Diraya held that fear from an enemy is from Allah (no repetition), while the author of al-Nihayah held it is from people (repetition required). The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq leans towards al-Nihayah but reconciles the two by distinguishing between fear arising from an explicit human threat (requires repetition) and general fear without a threat (no repetition). This is supported by Ibn Amir Hajj and a case from al-Muhit where a traveler imprisoned is excused due to the added difficulty of travel. The practical outcome: the ruling depends on the source of the fear.

Key Terms
خوف عدو (khawf 'aduww): Fear of an enemy; a valid excuse for tayammum because going to water would endanger life.
إعادة (i'ada): Repetition of the prayer after tayammum once the excuse is removed.
عذر من قبل الله (udhr min qib Allah): An excuse that comes directly from Allah's creation without human intermediary.
عذر من قبل العباد (udhr min qib al-'ibad): An excuse caused by a human action, such as a threat or prevention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reconciliation in this passage, when does fear from an enemy require i'ada after tayammum?
A) In all cases of fear of an enemy.
B) Only when the fear is from a wild beast.
C) When the fear arises from an explicit human threat (wa'id).
D) Only for a captive in dar al-harb.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, i'ada after tayammum is required only when the excuse arises from human action; excuses from Allah do not require repetition.

Tayammum Permitted Due to Thirst and Lack of Equipment
Explaining that water needed for drinking is considered non-existent, and clarifying conditions for lack of equipment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which water needed for drinking permits tayammum and identify when lack of equipment allows tayammum.

Core Idea
Water needed for drinking is treated as nonexistent; lack of bucket or rope permits tayammum unless a garment can draw water.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on two critical scenarios where tayammum is permitted despite the presence of water: when water is needed to quench thirst (for oneself or dependents) and when equipment to draw water is lacking. Understanding these rulings ensures one does not inadvertently perform tayammum incorrectly when water is actually attainable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first scenario: water needed for drinking
Recognize that water required to save a life (thirst) is considered effectively nonexistent, making tayammum permissible.
2
Analyze the ruling on forceful taking of water
If the water owner refuses and the needy person is compelled, he may take by force; note the different liabilities if killing occurs.
3
Identify the second scenario: lack of equipment
If one cannot reach water because he lacks a bucket or rope, tayammum is allowed.
4
Consider the condition regarding using garment or handkerchief
If he can use his garment to extract water (even slowly), tayammum is invalid.
5
Evaluate the handkerchief ruling from al-Khulasah
Having a pure handkerchief that could absorb water prevents tayammum, as per Shafi'i agreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الماء المحتاج إليه للعطش فإنه مشغول بحاجته والمشغول بالحاجة كالمعدوم وعطش رفيقه ودابته وكلبه الماشيته أو صيده في الحال أو ثاني الحال كعطشه وسواء كان المحتاج إليه للعطش رفيقه المخالط له أو آخر من أهل القافلة، فإن امتنع صاحب الماء ذلك محتاج إليه للعطش وهناك مضطر إليه للعطش كان له أخذه منه قهراً وله أن يقاتله، فإن قتل أحدهما صاحبه إن كان المقتول صاحب الماء فدمه هدر ولا قصاص فيه ولا دية ولا كفارة، وإن كان المضطر فهو مضمون بالقصاص أو الدية والكفارة. وإن كان صاحب الماء محتاجاً إليه للعطش فهو أولى به من غيره فإن احتاج إليه الأجنبي للوضوء وكان مستغنياً عنه لم يلزمه بذله ولا يجوز للأجنبي أخذه منه قهراً. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وكذا الماء المحتاج إليه للعجين لما قلنا وإن كان يحتاج إليه لاتخاذ المرقة لا يتيمم لأن حاجة الطبخ دون حاجة العطش، وأما جوازه بفقد الآلة فلتحقق العجز لأنه إذا لم يجد دلواً يستقي به فوجود البئر وعدمها سواء. ويشترط أن لا يمكنه إيصال ثوبه إليه، أما إذا أمكنه إيصال ثوبه ويخرج الماء قليلاً بالبلل لا يجوز له التيمم. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي الخلاصة: ولو كان معه منديل طاهر لا يجزئه التيمم وهذا يوافق فروعاً ذكرها الشافعية، وهي أنه لو وجد بئراً فيها ماء ولا يمكنه النزول إليه وليس معه ما يدليه إلا ثوبه أو
As for water needed for drinking, it is occupied by his need, and that which is occupied by need is like non-existent. Likewise the thirst of his companion, his mount, and his dog that protects his livestock or his game, immediately or in the next moment, is like his own thirst. Whether the one in need of water for drinking is his intimate companion or another from the caravan, if the owner of the water refuses while the other is in need of it for drinking and is compelled to drink, then he may take it from him by force, and he may fight him. If one of them kills the other: if the killed is the owner of the water, his blood is wasted, and there is no retaliation, blood money, or expiation; but if the compelled person is killed, then it is guaranteed by retaliation or blood money and expiation. If the owner of the water himself needs it for drinking, he has priority over others. If a stranger needs it for wudu while the owner is self-sufficient, the owner is not obliged to give it, and the stranger may not take it by force. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Similarly, water needed for kneading dough (we say) because the need for dough is less than thirst. But if he needs it for making soup, he does not perform tayammum because the need for cooking is less than the need for drinking. As for the permissibility due to lack of equipment, it is because inability is realized: if he does not find a bucket to draw water, the existence of the well and its non-existence are the same. It is conditioned that he cannot reach it with his garment; if he can reach it with his garment and the water comes out little by little with wetness, tayammum is not permissible. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And in al-Khulasah: If he has a pure handkerchief, tayammum does not suffice him. This agrees with branches mentioned by the Shafi'is, namely that if he finds a well with water and cannot descend to it, and he has nothing to let down except his garment or... [incomplete]
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq covers two additional scenarios for tayammum. First, the case of water needed for drinking: water is considered non-existent if it is required to quench thirst (of oneself, companion, or animal). The text discusses the extreme situation where one may take water by force from an owner who refuses, with detailed rulings on liability if killing occurs. However, if the owner himself needs the water for drinking, he has priority. Water for wudu is secondary to drinking. Water needed for cooking (e.g., making soup) does not permit tayammum because the need is less urgent. Second, the ruling on lack of equipment: if one cannot reach water because he lacks a bucket or rope, tayammum is permitted, provided he cannot use his garment to extract water. If he can use his garment to draw water (even slowly), tayammum is not allowed. Finally, the text mentions a ruling from al-Khulasah about having a clean handkerchief: if one has a handkerchief that could be used to absorb water, tayammum is not valid. This aligns with Shafi'i rulings. The passage is unfortunately cut off, so the full ruling on the handkerchief is not complete.

Key Terms
عطش (atash): Thirst; a valid excuse for using water for drinking rather than wudu, permitting tayammum.
فقد آلة (faqd alah): Lack of equipment (e.g., bucket, rope) needed to draw water from a well.
منديل (mandeel): A handkerchief or cloth that can be used to absorb water from a well or source.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if a traveler needs water for drinking to save his life, but another person owns the water and refuses, what may the traveler do?
A) He must perform tayammum.
B) He may take the water by force, and if the owner dies, no retaliation.
C) He must negotiate and pay triple the price.
D) He cannot take the water because it belongs to the owner.

Key Takeaway
Water needed for drinking takes priority over wudu, and lack of equipment permits tayammum only if no alternative means to obtain water exist.

Tayammum Due to Fear: When Repetition Is Required
Clarifies the ruling of tayammum due to fear and when repetition is required.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether tayammum due to fear requires repetition of prayer and distinguish between fear from a human enemy and fear from other causes.

Core Idea
If tayammum is performed due to fear from a human enemy, the prayer must be repeated; if due to natural causes, no repetition.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the source of the fear that necessitates tayammum. The author resolves an apparent contradiction between two earlier texts by showing that the ruling depends on whether the fear originated from a human threat (requiring repetition) or from a natural cause (no repetition). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of tayammum and i'ada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing tayammum due to fear. The ruling concerns whether the prayer performed with that tayammum must be repeated (i'ada) after the fear subsides and water becomes available.
Repetition is considered wajib in the Hanafi school when certain conditions are met.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the distinction between fear originating from a human (from the servants) and fear from natural causes (from Allah). The author uses the rulings from al-Nihaya and al-Diraya to illustrate this.
The dalil is not a specific text but a rational legal reasoning (ta'lil) based on the source of the excuse.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The distinction shows that a human-caused excuse does not remove the obligation of wudu permanently; it only temporarily prevents use. Therefore, after the excuse ends, the original obligation (wudu) returns, necessitating repetition. A natural-caused excuse, being from Allah, indicates true unavailability of water, thus no repetition.
The phrase 'العذر جاء من قبل العباد لا يؤثر في إسقاط فرض الوضوء' is key.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an apparent contradiction between al-Nihaya and al-Diraya, but the author reconciles them by interpreting each according to the source of fear. This shows that the ikhtilaf is resolved within the Hanafi school.
Ibn Amir Haj explicitly clarifies the reconciliation.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that repetition is wajib when fear is from a human enemy, and not wajib when fear is from natural causes. This is affirmed by the author of al-Hidayah and later Hanafi masters.
See al-Bahr al-Raiq for the final tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم القتل فإنه ليس فيه إلا الخوف لا المنع الحسي، وكذا ظاهر ما نقلناه عن التنجيس كما لا يخفى لكن قد يقال لا مخالفة بين ما في النهاية والدراية، فإن ما في النهاية محمول على ما إذا حصل وعيد من العبد نشأ منه الخوف فكان هذا من قبل العباد وما في الدراية محمول على ما إذا لم يحصل وعيد من العبد أصلاً بل حصل خوف منه فكان هذا من قبل الله تعالى إذا لم يتقدّمه وعيد بدليل أن صاحب الدراية ذكر مسألة الخوف في الأسير بدار الحرب، وبه يندفع ما ذكره في فتح القدير من أن صاحب الدراية نص على مخالفة ما في النهاية كما لا يخفى. ثم بعد هذا رأيت العلامة ابن أمير حاج صرح بما فهمته فقال : وتحرر أن المراد بالخوف من العدوّ الخوف الذي لم ينشأ عن وعيد من قادر عليه ونحو ذلك كما في الخوف من السبع، ولا بأس بأن يكون مرادهم ذلك. وإنما نسب هذا الخوف إلى الله تعالى في هذه الصورة مع أن فيها وفي غيرها منه تعالى أيضاً خلقاً وإرادة لتجرده في هذه الصورة عن مباشرة سبب له من الغير في حق الخائف. وفي المحيط : ولو حبس في السفر تيمم وصلى أو لا يعيد لأنه انضم عذر السفر إلى العذر الحقيقي والغلب في السفر عدم الماء فتحقق العدم من كل وجه ا هـ . ويلحق بخوف العدو والسبع ما هو مثله كخوف الحية أو النار لكن بعد زوال العذر يجب الإعادة بالوضوء فيما إذا كان خائفاً من عدوّ لما أن العذر جاء من قبل العباد، وذلك لا يؤثر في إسقاط فرض الوضوء. كذا ذكر صاحب الهداية في التنجيس. وكذا المحبوس في السجن والأسير
The Book of Purification - Chapter of Tayammum: Killing, for it contains only fear, not physical prevention. And similarly apparent is what we transmitted from al-Tanjis, as is not hidden. But it may be said there is no contradiction between what is in al-Nihaya and al-Diraya, because what is in al-Nihaya is interpreted as when a threat arises from a slave, generating fear, so this is from the side of the servants. And what is in al-Diraya is interpreted as when no threat from a slave occurs at all, but rather fear arises from it, so this is from the side of Allah the Exalted when no threat preceded it, evidenced by the fact that the author of al-Diraya mentioned the issue of fear regarding a captive in dar al-harb. And thereby is rebutted what was mentioned in Fath al-Qadir that the author of al-Diraya explicitly contradicted what is in al-Nihaya, as is not hidden. Then after this, I saw the scholar Ibn Amir Haj explicitly stating what I understood, saying: It is established that the intended meaning of fear from an enemy is the fear that does not arise from a threat from one who is capable over it, and similar to that is fear from a beast, and there is no harm that their intent is that. And this fear is attributed to Allah the Exalted in this instance, although in it and in others He the Exalted also creates and wills, because it is devoid in this instance of direct causation by another in the context of the fearful person. And in al-Muhit: If one is imprisoned during travel, he performs tayammum and prays and does not repeat, because the excuse of travel joins the real excuse, and the prevailing condition in travel is lack of water, so non-existence is realized from every aspect. End quote. And appended to fear of an enemy and a beast is whatever is like it, such as fear of a snake or fire, but after the excuse ceases, repetition of wudu is obligatory when one is fearful of an enemy, because the excuse came from the side of the servants, and that does not affect the dropping of the obligation of wudu. Thus mentioned the author of al-Hidaya in al-Tanjis. And similarly the imprisoned in prison and the captive.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of tayammum due to fear. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the legal reasoning behind two related rulings from al-Nihaya and al-Diraya. The key distinction is the source of the fear: if it arises from a threat uttered by a person (a 'slave' meaning a human being), then the excuse is from the side of the servants and does not completely lift the obligation of wudu; prayer performed with tayammum must be repeated after the excuse ends. If the fear arises spontaneously without a human threat, like fear from a beast, then it is from Allah and does not necessitate repetition. The author cites Ibn Amir Haj's clarification that the 'fear of an enemy' in the texts refers to fear not preceded by a threat from a capable being. A quote from al-Muhit adds that a prisoner in travel does not repeat because travel is combined with the real excuse of imprisonment, and lack of water is prevalent in travel. The ultimate ruling: if the fear was from a human enemy, repetition is wajib after the excuse ends, because a human-caused excuse does not nullify the obligation of wudu. This is affirmed from al-Hidaya via al-Tanjis. The same applies to one imprisoned or captive.

Key Terms
الخوف (al-khawf): Fear that prevents one from using water, either from a human enemy or from a natural threat like a beast.
العدو (al-aduww): An enemy, specifically a human enemy whose threat causes fear.
السبع (al-sabu): A beast or predatory animal; fear from it is considered from Allah, not requiring repetition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, when does tayammum due to fear require repetition of prayer?
A) When the fear is from a beast.
B) When the fear is from a human enemy with a threat.
C) When the fear is from a snake.
D) When the fear is from fire.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires repetition of prayer after tayammum only when the fear originates from a human enemy, because a human-caused excuse does not permanently lift the obligation of wudu.

Water for Thirst and Its Effect on Tayammum
Rules regarding water needed for drinking and its effect on the permissibility of tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water needed for thirst and explain why it permits tayammum and, in extreme cases, taking water by force.

Core Idea
Water needed for survival is legally treated as non-existent, making tayammum permissible and even allowing forceful acquisition.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a critical intersection of ritual purity and survival. In the Hanafi school, the need to preserve life overrides the obligation to use water for wudu. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly applying tayammum rulings when water is scarce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Recognize the maxim 'al-mashghul bi al-haja ka al-ma'dum' (what is occupied by need is like non-existent). This is the foundation of the ruling.
This is a rational principle (istihsan), not a textual one.
2
Apply the principle to thirst
Water needed for one's own thirst or that of dependents (companion, animal, hunting dog) is considered non-existent for wudu. Thus, tayammum is allowed.
Includes immediate and near-future need.
3
Examine the case of refusal
If the owner of water withholds it while the needy person is compelled by thirst, the needy may take it by force, even if it leads to fighting.
If the owner is killed, no penalty; if the compelled person is killed, it is guaranteed.
4
Distinguish owner's priority
If the owner himself needs the water for thirst, he has priority. A stranger cannot take it for wudu if the owner needs it.
This respects the owner's right while upholding necessity.
5
Consider other needs
Water needed for dough (essential bread) also permits tayammum, but not for soup (lesser need). Lack of equipment (e.g., no bucket) also permits tayammum.
Condition: if one can get water with a cloth, tayammum is not allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الماء المحتاج إليه للعطش فإنه مشغول بحاجته والمشغول بالحاجة كالمعدوم وعطش رفيقه ودابته وكلبه الماشيته أو صيده في الحال أو ثاني الحال كعطشه وسواء كان المحتاج إليه للعطش رفيقه المخالط له أو آخر من أهل القافلة، فإن امتنع صاحب الماء ذلك محتاج إليه للعطش وهناك مضطر إليه للعطش كان له أخذه منه قهراً وله أن يقاتله، فإن قتل من وهو غير أحدهما صاحبه إن كان المقتول صاحب الماء فدمه هدر ولا قصاص فيه ولا دية ولا كفارة، وإن كان المضطر فهو مضمون بالقصاص أو الدية والكفارة. وإن كان صاحب الماء محتاجاً إليه للعطش فهو أولى به من غيره فإن احتاج إليه الأجنبي للوضوء وكان مستغنياً عنه لم يلزمه بذله ولا يجوز للأجنبي أخذه منه قهراً. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وكذا الماء المحتاج إليه للعجين لما قلنا وإن كان يحتاج إليه لاتخاذ المرقة لا يتيمم لأن حاجة الطبخ دون حاجة العطش، وأما جوازه بفقد الآلة فلتحقق العجز لأنه إذا لم يجد دلواً يستقي به فوجود البئر وعدمها سواء. ويشترط أن لا يمكنه إيصال ثوبه إليه، أما إذا أمكنه إيصال ثوبه ويخرج الماء قليلاً بالبلل لا يجوز له التيمم. كذا في السراج الوهاج.
As for water needed for thirst, it is occupied by one's need, and what is occupied by need is like non-existent. And the thirst of his companion, his animal, his dog that tends his livestock, or his game, whether immediately or in the near future, is like his own thirst. And whether the one in need of water for thirst is his close companion or another from the caravan, if the owner of the water withholds it while being in need of it for thirst, and there is one compelled by thirst, he may take it from him by force and may fight him. If one of them kills the other, if the killed is the owner of the water, his blood is wasted (no retaliation, blood-money, or expiation); if the killed is the compelled one, it is guaranteed by retaliation or blood-money and expiation. And if the owner of the water is also in need of it for thirst, he has more right to it than others. If a stranger needs it for wudu while the owner is independent of it, the owner is not obliged to give it, and the stranger may not take it by force. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And similarly water needed for dough, as we said. But if it is needed for making soup, one does not perform tayammum because the need for cooking is less than the need for thirst. As for its permissibility due to lack of equipment, it is due to the realization of incapacity. Because if he does not find a bucket to draw water, the existence of the well and its non-existence are the same. And it is conditioned that he cannot make his cloth reach it. If he can make his cloth reach it and water comes out a little by wetting, tayammum is not permitted. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the status of water needed for drinking in the context of tayammum. The author establishes that water required to quench thirst is considered legally non-existent because the need for survival takes precedence. This applies to the traveler’s own thirst, as well as that of his companion, animal, or dog. If a person has water and refuses to share it with someone who is compelled by thirst, the compelled person may take it by force; if killing occurs, the owner’s blood is worthless (no penalty) if he is killed, but the compelled person’s life is protected. However, if the owner himself needs the water for thirst, he has priority. A stranger cannot forcibly take water from the owner for wudu if the owner is independent. The same principle applies to water needed for dough (for bread) but not for soup, as cooking is a lesser need. Additionally, if one lacks equipment to draw water (e.g., no bucket), tayammum is permitted because the inability is real. But if one can use a cloth to soak up water, tayammum is not allowed unless the cloth is damaged beyond the value of water.

Key Terms
المشغول بالحاجة (al-mashghul bi al-haja): Something that is occupied by a need, legally treated as non-existent for the purpose of another obligation.
الاضطرار (al-idtirar): Compulsion due to dire need, permitting otherwise prohibited actions like taking property by force.
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution using earth as a substitute for wudu when water is unavailable or cannot be used.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on taking water by force from someone who refuses to give it to a person dying of thirst?
A) Not permitted; the owner's rights are absolute.
B) Permitted, and if the owner is killed, blood-money is due.
C) Permitted, and if the compelled person is killed, it is wasted blood.
D) Permitted only if the owner is not in need himself.

Key Takeaway
Water needed for survival legally counts as non-existent, making tayammum valid and property rights secondary to preserving life.

Using a Cloth to Draw Water: Ruling and Conditions for Tayammum
Expansion on tayammum conditions when cloth is available

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using a cloth to draw water for wudu and apply the principle of harm to determine when tayammum is permitted.

Core Idea
Using a cloth to draw water is wajib unless the loss exceeds the water's value – harm defines the boundary between wudu and tayammum.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq examines a practical scenario: you have a well but no bucket, only your garment. Must you lower it even if it gets damaged? The Hanafi school balances the obligation to use water with the principle of avoiding harm, leading to specific rules about acceptable loss. The author also compares with Shafi'i views and notes an intra-Hanafi difference regarding the exact threshold.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is using a cloth (garment) to draw water from a well when one has no bucket. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory) to do so if the decrease in the cloth's value does not exceed the price of the water.
This is based on the general obligation to use water for purification when possible without harm.
2
Apply the harm principle
The principle: harm (darar) must be avoided. If the loss from using the cloth exceeds the fair price of the water (thaman al-mithl), then using it would cause harm, and tayammum is permitted without repetition. If the loss is less, one must use the cloth.
Fair price is the market rate; paying more is not required.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Fakhr al-Din in al-Tatarkhaniyya set a fixed threshold of one dirham for the loss, regardless of the water's value. The author clarifies that this contradicts the general principle but advises following the transmitted school position.
The author leans to the Shafi'i view as more consistent but relies on the Hanafi texts.
4
Compare with purchase scenario
Purchasing water is an exchange, not destruction of property. One must buy at fair price even if expensive, because it does not involve loss without compensation. Lowering a cloth destroys its value without compensation, so the threshold applies.
This distinction explains why the ruling differs from buying water.

And in al-Khulasa: If one has a clean handkerchief, tayammum is not sufficient for him. And this agrees with branches mentioned by the Shafi'is: namely, if he finds a well containing water and cannot descend into it and has nothing to lower except his garment or turban, he must lower it and then wring it out, if the decrease in the value of the garment does not exceed the price of the water. If the decrease exceeds the price of the water, he performs tayammum and no repetition is upon him. And if he is able to hire someone to descend, he must do so and tayammum is not permitted; otherwise it is permitted without repetition. And if he has a garment, if he tears it into two halves and reaches the water, otherwise not; if the loss from tearing does not exceed the price of the water and the price of the equipment for drawing, he must do it and tayammum is not permitted; otherwise it is permitted without repetition. All this agrees with our principles, as in al-Tawshih. The principle is that whenever he can use water in any way without harm to himself or his property, he must use it. What exceeds the fair price is harm, so it is not required, contrary to the fair price. And in al-Mubtagha (with mu'jama ghayn): With the existence of equipment for hollowing in a frozen river under which there is water, he does not perform tayammum. It is said he performs tayammum. And in his travel, if it froze or snowed and he has equipment for melting, he does not perform tayammum. It is said he performs tayammum, and the apparent is the first, as is not hidden. And in al-Muhit: Water placed in the desert in a jar and the like does not prevent permissibility of tayammum, because it is not placed for wudu generally, but rather for drinking, unless the water is abundant, so its abundance indicates that it is placed for both drinking and wudu. End quote. And similarly in al-Tanjis and Fatawa al-Walwalji and Qadikhan. And 'al-habb' with damma ha' is the large earthenware jar. And from Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad b. al-Fadl: That which is placed for drinking may be used for wudu, and that which is placed for wudu is not permitted for drinking. And in al-Khulasa and other: Three persons in travel: a junub, a menstruating woman who became pure from menstruation, and a deceased person. With them is water sufficient for one of them. If the water belongs to one of them, he has more right. If the water belongs to them all, none of them should perform ghusl. If the water is ownerless, the junub has more right. He performs tayammum. End quote. And the restriction is contrary to Abu Yusuf regarding repetition. And in Munyat al-Musalli: If one prays with ishara due to fear of an enemy, beast, illness, or mud, he does not repeat by consensus. The restriction: if he prays sitting, he repeats according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf. End quote. Ibn Malik on al-Tuhfa: His saying: (This all agrees with our principles.) I say: It is so, but in al-Tatarkhaniyya there is something contradicting it, where he said after what was mentioned from al-Khulasa, al-Qadi Imam Fakhr al-Din said: If the decrease in the value of the handkerchief is the amount of a dirham, he performs tayammum and is not obliged to lower the handkerchief. So if the decrease is less than a dirham, not. Just as if he is in prayer and sees someone stealing his property, if it is a dirham's amount, he cuts the prayer; if less, he does not cut. That is similar here. End quote. And you are aware that what he mentioned from the Shafi'is is closer to the principles, because if he finds water for sale, he must buy it at the fair price even if its value is more than a dirham, but the recourse to what is transmitted in the school is better. So reflect. And it has appeared to me in the difference between this and purchase that purchase, even if the value is much, is an exchange for compensation, so it does not involve destruction of property, unlike lowering the handkerchief and tearing it, for it involves destruction of property without compensation and no necessity calls for it, because when water is absent, one resorts to its substitute, which is tayammum, so one does not commit what is prohibited for its sake. Reflect. And they have reasoned the non-requirement of purchase with gross fraud because the increase is not compensated by an exchange, so it is not required due to the absence of harm legally. And what makes it close is: if he has a impure garment and no water, he prays in it and is not required to cut the place of impurity from it, as will come. And they did not differentiate between whether by cutting it decreases by the amount of the value of the water if it were present or more. And that is only because of the necessity.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This is a detailed expansion on the conditions for tayammum when one has a cloth but no bucket. The passage, drawing from al-Khulasa and other sources, discusses several scenarios: if one can lower a garment or turban to draw water, he must do so unless the decrease in the garment's value exceeds the price of the water. If hiring someone is possible at fair cost, tayammum is not allowed. The principle is that using water in any way without harm is obligatory; harm includes loss exceeding fair price. The author then compares this with the Shafi'i view and notes a difference in al-Tatarkhaniyya from Fakhr al-Din, who set the threshold at one dirham. The author concludes that the Shafi'i view seems more consistent with principles, but the transmitted Hanafi position is to follow the school's texts. He also discusses the case of frozen rivers, water stored in jars, and the famous scenario of three people (junub, menstruating woman, deceased) with limited water. The passage also touches on the repetition of prayer when praying sitting due to fear, with an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf. The common thread is the principle of avoiding harm and the boundary between tangible loss and mere inconvenience.

Key Terms
إدلاء الثوب (idla' al-thawb): Lowering a garment into a well to draw water.
ثمن المثل (thaman al-mithl): The fair market price of water; spending this is obligatory, but not paying more.
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghabn al-fahish): Gross fraud or excessive overpricing; such purchase is not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the Hanafi school permit tayammum instead of using a cloth to draw water from a well?
A) Always, if one has a cloth.
B) When the loss from using the cloth exceeds the price of the water.
C) When the water is frozen.
D) Only if the cloth is made of silk.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of tayammum depends on whether using water would cause harm exceeding the fair price of the water, as per the Hanafi principle of avoiding unnecessary loss.

Tayammum Permitted When Water Use Causes Excessive Loss
Statutes the conditions for when tayammum is valid despite available water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that financial harm exceeding the fair price of water permits tayammum, and evaluate scenarios involving property loss.

Core Idea
If water use causes property damage greater than its local price, tayammum is valid—financial harm lifts obligation.

In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation to use water for wudu is not absolute. When water is available but accessing it would cause disproportionate financial loss, the Shari'ah permits tayammum instead. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the precise conditions using real-life scenarios of turban wringing, hiring help, and tearing cloth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine whether the person is obliged to use water or may perform tayammum. The passage gives specific scenarios with conditional rulings.
The default is obligation; exemption only when loss exceeds thaman al-mithl.
2
Identify the financial threshold
Compare the property loss from accessing water to the local fair price of water (thaman al-mithl). If loss > thaman al-mithl, tayammum is valid; otherwise, wudu is wajib.
Exactly equal loss does not exempt.
3
Apply to each scenario
Work through the turban, hiring, and cloth examples, applying the threshold to each.
Cost of tools (bucket) is included in the comparison.
4
Extract the underlying principle
The passage concludes with a general rule: any loss exceeding the fair price is darar (harm) that removes the obligation.
This is a rational (aqli) proof derived from the maxim 'al-darar yuzal'.
5
Understand the epistemological weight
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi, though some later sources differed on the exact threshold.
The relied-upon position uses thaman al-mithl as the benchmark.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عمامته لزمه إدلاؤه ثم يعصره، إن لم تنقص قيمة الثوب أكثر من ثمن الماء، فإن زاد النقص على ثمن الماء تيمم ولا إعادة عليه. وإن قدر على استئجار من ينزل إليها بأجرة المثل لزمه ولم يجز التيمم وإلا جاز بلا إعادة ولو كان مع ثوب إن شقه نصفين وصل إلى الماء وإلا لم يصل، فإن كان نقصه بالشق لا يزيد على ثمن الماء وثمن آلة الاستقاء لزمه مشقه ولم يجز التيمم وإلا جاز بلا إعادة. وهذا كله موافق لقواعدنا كذا في التوشيح. والأصل أنه متى أمكنه استعمال الماء بوجه من الوجوه من غير لحوق ضرر في نفسه أو ماله وجب عليه استعماله، وما زاد على ثمن المثل ضرر فلا يلزمه بخلاف ثمن المثل.
If he has a turban, he must lower it and then wring it. If the value of the cloth does not decrease by more than the price of water, he must do so; if the decrease exceeds the price of water, he performs tayammum and no repetition is required. If he is able to hire someone to go down to the water for a fair wage, he must do so and tayammum is not permissible; otherwise, tayammum is valid without repetition. And if he has a cloth that he can tear in half to reach the water, he does so; if the loss from tearing does not exceed the price of water plus the cost of a bucket, he must do so and tayammum is not permissible; otherwise, tayammum is valid without repetition. All of this is consistent with our principles, as in al-Tawshih. The principle is: whenever he can use water in any way without harm to himself or his property, its use is obligatory; any loss exceeding the fair price is harm and he is not obliged, unlike the fair price.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the detailed rulings on when a person must use water if it is available but requires effort or causes property damage. The author presents a series of scenarios, each with a condition tied to the monetary value of water. The overarching principle is that the obligation to perform wudu is not absolute if doing so would cause disproportionate financial harm. The ruling is in accordance with Hanafi principles, as noted from al-Tawshih. The key is that any loss exceeding the fair price of water is considered harm (ضرر) that excuses tayammum.

Key Terms
ثمن الماء (thaman al-ma'): The price or value of water in the locality.
ضرر (darar): Financial harm that exceeds the fair price of water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must lower and wring the turban, then do wudu.
B) He may perform tayammum and his prayer is valid without repetition.
C) He must perform tayammum but repeat the prayer later.
D) He must use the turban as a bucket and pay compensation.

Key Takeaway
Financial harm that exceeds the fair price of water excuses the obligation to use water, and tayammum suffices without repetition.

The Muqayyad's Prayer and the Principle of Financial Harm
Intra-Hanafi dispute and financial harm analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi dispute on i'ada for the muqayyad and apply the principle that uncompensated property loss excuses tayammum.

Core Idea
The muqayyad must repeat his prayer if he could have used water; property destroyed without compensation excuses tayammum.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the muqayyad—a person under physical restriction—who prays sitting. The dispute centers on whether he must repeat the prayer if he later gains access to water. The author then extends the discussion to financial harm: when can a person resort to tayammum due to property loss? By distinguishing between purchase (exchange) and destruction (loss), the Hanafi school clarifies the boundary of necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for the muqayyad
Understand the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad vs. Abu Yusuf on i'ada for a muqayyad who prays sitting. Note the consensus for other cases like fear or illness.
The text states that for fear, illness, etc., there is no i'ada by consensus.
2
Examine the financial harm principle
Analyze the distinction between buying water (exchange with compensation) and destroying property (uncompensated loss). Determine when property loss excuses tayammum based on the one-dirham threshold and the principle of harm.
The author compares with the Shafi'i position and then prefers the Hanafi transmitted view.
3
Apply the principle to new cases
Apply the same principle to other scenarios, such as a najis garment where cutting out the najasa is not required if it causes uncompensated loss.
The principle is that one does not incur uncompensated property loss for a substitute (tayammum) when the original (water) is absent.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
