And the muqayyad, contrary to Abu Yusuf regarding i'ada. In Munyat al-Musalli: if one prayed by gesture due to fear of an enemy, a beast, illness, or mud, he does not repeat by consensus; but the muqayyad, if he prayed sitting, repeats according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf. End. Ibn Malik on al-Tuhfah says: (this is all consistent with our principles). I say: yes, but in al-Tatarkhaniyya there is something contradicting it, where after the passage from al-Khulasa, Qadi Imam Fakhr al-Din said: if the decrease in value of the handkerchief is the amount of a dirham, he performs tayammum and need not send the handkerchief; but if the decrease is less than a dirham's value, no, just as if he were in prayer and saw someone stealing his money: if it is a dirham, he breaks prayer; if less, he does not. So here. End. And you are aware that what he mentioned from the Shafi'is is closer to the principles, because if he finds water for sale, he must buy it at the fair price even if its value is more than a dirham, but returning to the transmitted in the madhhab is preferable, so reflect. And it appeared to me the difference between this and purchase: purchase, even if the value is great, is an exchange for compensation, so there is no destruction of property, unlike lowering the handkerchief or tearing it, which is destruction of property without compensation and without a necessary reason, because when water is absent, one turns to its substitute, tayammum, so one does not commit a prohibited act for its sake. And they argued that purchase is not obligatory when there is gross overcharge because the excess is not matched by compensation, so it is not incumbent due to the absence of harm legally. And what brings it close is that if he had a najis garment and no water, he prays in it and is not obliged to cut out the najasa, as will come. And they did not distinguish between cutting that reduces by the value of water if it were present or more; that is only due to the necessity of harm without compensation.

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the muqayyad—a person who is restrained or unable to perform wudu normally. The main point is the i'ada (repetition) of prayer when praying seated due to inability. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require repetition if the person could have used water but did not, while Abu Yusuf does not. The author then critiques a statement from al-Tatarkhaniyya that sets a threshold of one dirham for property loss, comparing it to the Shafi'i position and arguing that the Hanafi principle is based on fair compensation (thaman al-mithl). The discussion distinguishes between buying water (an exchange without net loss) and destroying property (a net loss without benefit), which is why the latter is not required. This clarifies the finer points of financial harm as an excuse for tayammum.

Key Terms
المقيد (al-muqayyad): A person who is under some restriction (e.g., tied up, imprisoned, or unable to perform wudu normally) but may have access to water.
الإعادة (al-i'ada): Repetition of a prayer that was performed with tayammum or ima' when water later becomes available.

Key Takeaway
The muqayyad's i'ada is wajib according to the relied-upon view, and uncompensated property loss excuses tayammum.

Praying Without Taharah: The Hanafi Ruling on Kufr and the Imprisoned Person
Legal tricks, the imprisoned person who cannot find water, and the ruling on kufr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether intentionally praying without purification constitutes kufr, and explain the intra-madhab difference regarding the imprisoned person.

Core Idea
Intentionally praying without taharah is not kufr according to the preferred Hanafi view; the imprisoned person's obligation is also disputed.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq by Ibn Nujaym delves into a controversial issue: whether a person who deliberately prays without taharah commits kufr. It also examines a legal trick (hila) for a pilgrim with only Zamzam water, and the ruling for an imprisoned person who cannot find water or earth. By comparing different opinions, the author critically refines the school's position, ultimately settling on the view that such an act, while severely sinful, does not expel one from Islam.

Guided Path
1
State the act and ruling under dispute
Identify the specific act: a person intentionally praying without wudu or tayammum when they are able to perform purification. The central question is whether this constitutes kufr (disbelief) or is merely a major sin.
2
Locate the source of disagreement
The text cites a case of an imprisoned person who cannot find any purifier. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say he should not pray at all, while Abu Yusuf says he prays by gesture and repeats later. This difference implies a deeper disagreement about the gravity of praying without taharah.
3
Trace the analogy (tashbih) used for tarjih
The author draws an analogy between praying without taharah and praying to a wrong qibla or with a najis garment. Since the preferred view is that those do not make one a disbeliever, consistency demands the same ruling here, despite claims that this case is unique because it is never permissible.
The author argues using qiyas (analogical reasoning) to refine the position.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The text records that Abu Yusuf differs from the other two imams on the imprisoned person's duty, but all agree that the act is haram. The dispute is about whether the obligation of salah is waived when taharah is impossible, or whether one should still perform it out of respect for the time.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (relied-upon opinion)
The author explicitly states that the view that it is not kufr is 'the most correct' and consistent with earlier fatwas. This becomes the operative ruling for fatwa.
Authority: fatawa mutakhkhirin; the author's tarjih is based on textual consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد آلة مستوعباً وجهه ويديه مع مرفقيه بضربتين ولو جنباً أو حائضاً بطاهر من جنس فتتيمم وينبغي من بسبب المرأة, وييمم الميت ولو كان مكان الحائض محدث يصرف إلى الجنب ا هـ. وفي الظهيرية قال عامة المشايخ الميت أولى وقيل الجنب أولى وهو الأصح ا هـ . . وفي المحيط : أن يصرفا نصيبهما إلى غسل الميت ويتيمما فيما إذا كان مشتركاً. وفي التنجيس : رجل كان في البادية وليس معه إلا قمقمة ماء زمزم في رحله وقد رصص رأسه، ولا يجوز له التيمم إذا كان لا يخاف على نفسه العطش لأنه واحد للماء وكثيراً ما يبتلى به الحاج الجاهل ويظن أنه يجزئه والحيلة فيه أن يهبه من غيره. ثم يستودع منه الماء ا هـ. قال قاضيخان في فتاواه إلا أن هذا ليس بصحيح عندي فإنه لو رأى . غيره ماء مع يبيعه بمثل الثمن أو بغبن يسير يلزمه الشراء، ولا يجوز له التيمم فإذا تمكن من الرجوع في الهبة كيف تملك يجوز له التيمم ا هـ . ودفعه في فتح القدير بأنه يمكن أن يفرق بأن الرجوع مكروه وهو مطلوب العدم شرعاً فيجوز أن يعتبر الماء معدوماً في حقه كذلك وإن قدر عليه حقيقة كماء الحب بخلاف البيع .اهـ. وقيل الحيلة فيه أن يخلطه بماء الورد حتى يغلب عليه فلا يبقى طهوراً كذا في التوشيح والمحبوس الذي لا يجد طهوراً لا يصلي عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف يصلي بالايماء ثم يعيد وهو رواية عن محمد تشبهاً بالمصلين قضاء لحق الوقت كما في الصوم. ولهما أنه ليس بأهل للأداء لمكان الحدث فلا يلزمه التشبه كالحائض، وبهذه المسألة تبين أن الصلاة بغير طهارة متعمداً ليس بكفر فإنه لو كان كفراً لما أمر أبو يوسف به، وقيل كفر كالصلاة إلى غير القبلة أو مع الثوب النجس عمداً لأنه كالمستخف، والأصح أنه لو صلى إلى غير القبلة أو مع الثوب النجس لا يكفر لأن ذلك لا يجوز أداؤه بحال. ولو صلى بغير طهارة متعمداً يكفر لأن ذلك يحرم بكل حال فإذا صلى بغير طهارة متعمداً فقد تهاون واستخف بأمر الشرع فيكفر كذا في المحيط، وقد قدمنا عن الفتاوى الظهيرية أن مقطوع اليدين والرجلين إذا كان بوجهه جراحة يصلي بغير طهارة ولا يتيمم ولا يعيد وهذا هو الأصح ، فكانت الصلاة بغير طهارة نظير الصلاة على غير القبلة أو مع الثوب النجس فينبغي التسوية بينهما في الحكم وهو عدم التكفير كما لا يخفى. قوله : (مستوعباً وجهه ويديه مع (مرفقيه أي يتيمم تيمماً مستوعباً فهو صفة المصدر
Then he has an instrument, covering his face and hands together with the elbows with two strikes, even if he is junub or menstruating, with pure earth of the same type, so she performs tayammum, and it is recommended that he (the woman?) due to the woman, and tayammum is performed for the deceased, and if instead of the menstruating woman there was a person with minor impurity, it is diverted to the junub. End. In al-Dhahiriyya: the general mashayikh said the deceased is more entitled; it was said the junub is more entitled, and that is the most correct. End. In al-Muhit: they should divert their shares to the washing of the deceased and perform tayammum when it is shared. In al-Tanjis: a man was in the desert and had only a flask of Zamzam water in his saddle, and he had sealed its mouth; tayammum is not permissible for him if he does not fear thirst because it is a single portion of water, and many ignorant pilgrims are afflicted and think it suffices them. The trick is to gift it to someone else, then borrow the water from him. End. Qadi Khan in his Fatawa said: this is not correct in my view, because if he sees someone else's water being sold at the fair price or with a small overcharge, he must buy it and tayammum is not permissible; so if he can take back the gift, how can he own it and then perform tayammum? End. And it was refuted in Fath al-Qadir: it can be distinguished because taking back a gift is disliked and is legally sought to be non-existent, so it is permissible to consider the water as non-existent in his regard, even if he can actually reach it, like the water in a jar, unlike purchase. End. And it was said that the trick is to mix it with rose water until it dominates and it no longer remains purifying. So in al-Tawshih. And the imprisoned person who cannot find a purifier, he does not pray according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), but according to Abu Yusuf he prays by gesture and then repeats, and it is a narration from Muhammad, imitating the praying people, fulfilling the right of the time as in fasting. And for them (the two) he is not qualified for performance due to the hadath, so he is not obliged to imitate, like a menstruating woman. This case shows that praying without taharah intentionally is not kufr, because if it were kufr, Abu Yusuf would not have commanded it. And it was said it is kufr like praying towards a direction other than the qibla or with a najis garment intentionally, because he is like one who ridicules. And the most correct is that if he prays towards other than the qibla or with a najis garment, he does not become a disbeliever because that cannot be performed at all. But if he prays without taharah intentionally, he becomes a disbeliever because that is prohibited in all circumstances, so if he prays without taharah intentionally, he has been careless and ridiculed the command of Sharia, so he disbelieves, as in al-Muhit. And we have already mentioned from al-Fatawa al-Dhahiriyya that the one with amputated hands and feet, if he has a wound on his face, prays without taharah and does not perform tayammum and does not repeat, and this is the most correct. So praying without taharah is analogous to prayer towards other than the qibla or with a najis garment, so consistency should be made in the ruling, which is non-kufr, as is not hidden. His statement: (covering his face and hands together with the elbows) means he performs tayammum covering, so it is a description of the verbal noun.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage covers several issues. First, the definition of tayammum: covering the face and hands to the elbows with two strikes (ضربتين) using pure earth, even for a junub or menstruating woman, and it is recommended that a woman do so due to her hair, and the deceased is also given tayammum. A conflict is resolved: if water is shared, the deceased takes priority over the junub for ghusl, and those alive do tayammum. Then a hila (legal trick) is discussed: a pilgrim with only Zamzam water, unable to use it for wudu because it is his only drinking water, is told to gift it and then borrow it back. Qadi Khan rejects this, saying if the gift can be taken back, the water is still reachable. Fath al-Qadir defends the hila by distinguishing disliked takings from purchase. Another hila is to mix with rose water to nullify its purifying quality. Then the infamous case of the imprisoned person who cannot find water: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say he does not pray, while Abu Yusuf says he prays by gesture and repeats. This leads to the theological question of whether intentionally praying without taharah constitutes kufr. The text presents both views: some say it is kufr because it is disrespectful; others say it is not kufr because it is analogous to praying without facing qibla or with najis garments, which is not kufr. The author concludes that the most correct view is that it is not kufr, based on earlier rulings. Finally, the meaning of 'covering' in the matn is explained.

Key Terms
الحيلة (al-hila): A legal stratagem to circumvent a prohibition while remaining within the law, here to make Zamzam water available for drinking while avoiding tayammum invalidly.
المحبوس (al-mahbus): A person imprisoned or restrained who cannot access water or earth for purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on a person intentionally praying without taharah?
A) It is always kufr without exception.
B) It is not kufr, similar to praying without facing the qibla.
C) It is a minor sin.
D) It is permissible if the person cannot find water.

Key Takeaway
The favoured Hanafi view is that deliberately praying without purification is not kufr, but a grave sin; the dispute shows the importance of distinguishing between kufr and major sin through careful analogical reasoning.

Manner of Tayammum and Shared Water Priority
Expands ruling of tayammum and water sharing priority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi manner of tayammum and explain the ruling when water is shared between a dead body and a person in janabah.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires full coverage of face and hands with two strikes; washing the dead takes precedence over the living's ghusl.

This passage details the obligatory manner of tayammum: two strikes covering the face and hands to the elbows. It then addresses a scenario where water is shared between a dead body and a person in major impurity (junub), resolving the priority in favor of the dead.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tayammum is fard when water is unavailable. The manner is specified: two strikes covering the face and hands (including elbows) entirely (isti'ab).
The text uses 'mustaw'ib' (covering entirely).
2
Determine the conditions
Pure earth of its kind must be used. The ruling applies even for janabah or menstruation.
3
Examine the ikhtilaf on priority
When water is shared between a dead body and a junub, there is a dispute: most scholars say the dead is more deserving, some say the junub. The correct view is the dead first.
The text says 'al-ashah' (most correct) for dead.
4
Apply the resolution
According to al-Muhit, if water is shared, both parties should divert their share to wash the dead, and both perform tayammum.
This ensures the dead is purified and the living fulfill their obligation.

فقد آلة مستوعباً وجهه ويديه مع مرفقيه بضربتين ولو جنباً أو حائضاً بطاهر من جنس فتتيمم وينبغي من بسبب المرأة, وييمم الميت ولو كان مكان الحائض محدث يصرف إلى الجنب ا هـ. وفي الظهيرية قال عامة المشايخ الميت أولى وقيل الجنب أولى وهو الأصح ا هـ . . وفي المحيط : أن يصرفا نصيبهما إلى غسل الميت ويتيمما فيما إذا كان مشتركاً. وفي التنجيس : رجل كان في البادية وليس معه إلا قمقمة ماء زمزم في رحله وقد رصص رأسه، ولا يجوز له التيمم إذا كان لا يخاف على نفسه العطش لأنه واحد للماء وكثيراً ما يبتلى به الحاج الجاهل ويظن أنه يجزئه والحيلة فيه أن يهبه من غيره. ثم يستودع منه الماء ا هـ. قال قاضيخان في فتاواه إلا أن هذا ليس بصحيح عندي فإنه لو رأى . غيره ماء مع يبيعه بمثل الثمن أو بغبن يسير يلزمه الشراء، ولا يجوز له التيمم فإذا تمكن من الرجوع في الهبة كيف تملك يجوز له التيمم ا هـ . ودفعه في فتح القدير بأنه يمكن أن يفرق بأن الرجوع مكروه وهو مطلوب العدم شرعاً فيجوز أن يعتبر الماء معدوماً في حقه كذلك وإن قدر عليه حقيقة كماء الحب بخلاف البيع .اهـ. وقيل الحيلة فيه أن يخلطه بماء الورد حتى يغلب عليه فلا يبقى طهوراً كذا في التوشيح والمحبوس الذي لا يجد طهوراً لا يصلي عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف يصلي بالايماء ثم يعيد وهو رواية عن محمد تشبهاً بالمصلين قضاء لحق الوقت كما في الصوم. ولهما أنه ليس بأهل للأداء لمكان الحدث فلا يلزمه التشبه كالحائض، وبهذه المسألة تبين أن الصلاة بغير طهارة متعمداً ليس بكفر فإنه لو كان كفراً لما أمر أبو يوسف به، وقيل كفر كالصلاة إلى غير القبلة أو مع الثوب النجس عمداً لأنه كالمستخف، والأصح أنه لو صلى إلى غير القبلة أو مع الثوب النجس لا يكفر لأن ذلك لا يجوز أداؤه بحال. ولو صلى بغير طهارة متعمداً يكفر لأن ذلك يحرم بكل حال فإذا صلى بغير طهارة متعمداً فقد تهاون واستخف بأمر الشرع فيكفر كذا في المحيط، وقد قدمنا عن الفتاوى الظهيرية أن مقطوع اليدين والرجلين إذا كان بوجهه جراحة يصلي بغير طهارة ولا يتيمم ولا يعيد وهذا هو الأصح ، فكانت الصلاة بغير طهارة نظير الصلاة على غير القبلة أو مع الثوب النجس فينبغي التسوية بينهما في الحكم وهو عدم التكفير كما لا يخفى.
He struck the instrument covering his face and his hands including his elbows with two strikes, even if in a state of major impurity or menstruation, with pure earth of its kind. Then she performs tayammum. And it is appropriate that due to the woman, and the dead person is performed tayammum upon, and if instead of a menstruating woman there was a person in minor impurity, it is diverted to the junub [major impurity]. etc. And in al-Zahiriya: the generality of scholars said the dead is more deserving, and it was said the junub is more deserving, and it is the most correct. etc. And in al-Muhit: they should divert their share to washing the dead and both perform tayammum when it is shared. And in al-Tanjish: a man was in the desert and he had only a bottle of Zamzam water in his saddlebag and he has bandaged his head, and it is not permissible for him to perform tayammum if he does not fear for himself thirst because it is one water, and frequently the ignorant pilgrim is afflicted with this and thinks it suffices him, and the legal trick is that he gift it to someone else, then he deposits the water from him. etc. Qadikhan said in his Fatawa: except that this is not correct according to me, for if he saw another person with water selling it at the same price or with a slight loss, he is obliged to buy, and tayammum is not permissible for him. If he is able to revoke the gift, how can he own it? Tayammum is permissible for him. etc. And it is rebutted in Fath al-Qadir by saying that it can be differentiated: that revocation is disliked and it is required not to exist legally, so it is permissible to consider the water as non-existent in his right similarly, even if he is able over it actually, like the water of a water-skin, contrary to sale. etc. And it was said the legal trick is that he mixes it with rose water until it prevails, so it no longer remains purifying. Thus in al-Tawshih. And the imprisoned who does not find purifying water, he does not pray according to them two, and according to Abu Yusuf he prays with gesture then repeats, and it is a narration from Muhammad imitating the worshippers to fulfill the right of time, as in fasting. And according to both of them, he is not fit for performance due to the state of impurity, so he is not obliged to imitate, like the menstruating woman. And by this issue it is shown that praying intentionally without purification is not disbelief, for if it were disbelief, Abu Yusuf would not have commanded it. And it was said it is disbelief like praying toward a direction other than qibla or with a najis garment intentionally because he is like a contemptuous person, and the most correct is that if he prays toward other than qibla or with a najis garment, he does not become a disbeliever because that cannot be performed at all. And if he prays without purification intentionally, he becomes a disbeliever because that is forbidden in every case; so if he prays without purification intentionally, he has been careless and contemptuous of the command of Shari'ah, so he becomes a disbeliever. Thus in al-Muhit. And we have previously presented from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya that the one whose hands and feet are cut off, if he has a wound on his face, he prays without purification, does not perform tayammum, and does not repeat, and this is the most correct. So praying without purification is analogous to praying toward other than qibla or with a najis garment; thus the ruling should be equal between them, which is non-disbelief, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding the ruling of tayammum from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It begins by stating the manner of tayammum: two strikes covering the face and hands to the elbows, using pure earth, even for janabah or menstruation. It then discusses cases where water is scarce, such as having only Zamzam water and fearing thirst. The legal trick (hila) of giving away water to permit tayammum is examined, with Qadikhan noting that if one can buy water at a reasonable price, tayammum is not allowed. The passage then addresses the case of an imprisoned person who cannot find water: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two), he does not pray; Abu Yusuf allows prayer with gesture. This leads to a discussion on whether praying without tayammum intentionally constitutes kufr. The text presents two views: one distinguishes it from prayer without qibla or with najis garment, deeming it not kufr; another considers it kufr. The author leans toward the view that it is not kufr, citing the ruling for an amputee with facial wounds who prays without purification. The commentary concludes that the ruling should be consistent: intentional prayer without tayammum is not disbelief, just as prayer toward the wrong qibla or with najis garment is not disbelief.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution using pure earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
مستوعب (mustaw'ib): Covering entirely; in tayammum, the entire face and hands to elbows must be wiped.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct ruling when water is shared between a dead body and a person in janabah?
A) Both use water equally.
B) The dead is washed and the junub performs tayammum.
C) The junub purifies first.
D) Both perform tayammum.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates two strikes with full coverage for tayammum and prioritizes washing the dead over the living's ghusl when water is shared.

Legal Stratagems (Hiyal) for Tayammum: The Case of Scarce Water
Expands ruling on tayammum with hiyal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi legal trick of gifting water to permit tayammum and evaluate the critiques by later Hanafi scholars.

Core Idea
Gifting water to enable tayammum is a Hanafi hila, but its validity is contested if the gift can be revoked or water can be bought.

This passage addresses a common dilemma: a pilgrim has only Zamzam water and fears thirst if he uses it for wudu. It presents a legal stratagem (hila): gift the water to another, then borrow it back, permitting tayammum. The text then records critiques by Qadikhan and a rebuttal from Fath al-Qadir, highlighting the nuanced Hanafi approach to necessity and legal fictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
A person has only a bottle of Zamzam water in the desert, enough to drink but not for wudu without risking thirst. He has bandaged his head.
The text warns that ignorant pilgrims often think using Zamzam for wudu suffices.
2
Understand the hila
The legal trick is to gift the water to someone else, then take it back as a deposit, so he no longer owns it and can perform tayammum.
This transfers ownership, making the water 'not his' for wudu purposes.
3
Analyze Qadikhan's objection
Qadikhan argues that if he can buy water at a fair price, he must buy it and tayammum is invalid. Also, if the gift is revocable (ruju') it is not a true transfer.
The objection is that the hila does not genuinely remove access to water.
4
Consider the rebuttal in Fath al-Qadir
The rebuttal distinguishes that revocation is disliked (makruh) and legally considered as non-existent, so the water is treated as unavailable, similar to water in a water-skin that cannot be accessed.
This allows the hila to stand despite revocability.
5
Note an alternative hila
Another trick is to mix the water with rose water until it becomes non-purifying (ghayr tahur), then tayammum is allowed.
This is from al-Tawshih.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding the ruling of tayammum from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It begins by stating the manner of tayammum: two strikes covering the face and hands to the elbows, using pure earth, even for janabah or menstruation. It then discusses cases where water is scarce, such as having only Zamzam water and fearing thirst. The legal trick (hila) of giving away water to permit tayammum is examined, with Qadikhan noting that if one can buy water at a reasonable price, tayammum is not allowed. The passage then addresses the case of an imprisoned person who cannot find water: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two), he does not pray; Abu Yusuf allows prayer with gesture. This leads to a discussion on whether praying without tayammum intentionally constitutes kufr. The text presents two views: one distinguishes it from prayer without qibla or with najis garment, deeming it not kufr; another considers it kufr. The author leans toward the view that it is not kufr, citing the ruling for an amputee with facial wounds who prays without purification. The commentary concludes that the ruling should be consistent: intentional prayer without tayammum is not disbelief, just as prayer toward the wrong qibla or with najis garment is not disbelief.

Key Terms
حيلة (hila): A legal stratagem to achieve a lawful result while avoiding a prohibition, e.g., gifting water to permit tayammum.
رجوع (ruju'): Revocation of a gift; legally allowed but disliked (makruh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person can buy water at the same price?
A) Tayammum is allowed.
B) He must buy the water.
C) He should use the hila of gifting.
D) He may choose between buying and hila.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits tayammum only when water is genuinely unavailable; legal tricks are scrutinized and not universally accepted.

The Imprisoned Person and the Ruling on Kufr for Praying Without Purification
Discusses imprisoned person and kufr implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on the imprisoned person's prayer and evaluate whether intentionally praying without tayammum constitutes kufr.

Core Idea
Praying without purification intentionally is not necessarily kufr, according to the more correct Hanafi view, but some scholars deem it so.

This passage tackles a practical and theological issue: an imprisoned person who cannot find water must decide whether to pray or not. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say do not pray; Abu Yusuf says pray with gesture and repeat. This leads to a deeper question: is intentionally praying without tayammum an act of disbelief? The author weighs evidence from various sources and concludes that the correct view is that it is not kufr, drawing analogy with the case of an amputee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
An imprisoned person cannot find purifying water (tahur). According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two), he does not pray at all. According to Abu Yusuf, he prays with gesture (ima') and repeats later.
There is also a narration from Muhammad supporting Abu Yusuf.
2
Analyze each proof
The two argue: he is not fit for performance due to hadath (impurity), like a menstruating woman who does not pray. Abu Yusuf argues: he should imitate the worshippers and fulfill the right of time, like a traveler fasting in Ramadan.
The analogy to fasting is interesting: a traveler can fast or not; here, the imprisoned can pray or not?
3
Implications for kufr
The passage notes that if Abu Yusuf's view is followed, then praying without tayammum is not kufr, because he would have commanded it. This leads to a discussion: some say intentionally praying without purification is kufr, like praying towards wrong qibla or with a najis garment; others say it is not.
The author clarifies that even the opposing view does not consider the amputee case as kufr.
4
Examine the amputee analogy
The text cites from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya: the one whose hands and feet are cut off and has a wound on his face prays without purification, does not do tayammum, and does not repeat. This is the most correct view.
This shows that there are cases where prayer without purification is permitted and not considered kufr.
5
Conclude on kufr
The author argues that praying without tayammum is analogous to praying without qibla or with najis garment; the ruling should be the same: not kufr. The more correct view is that it is not disbelief, though it is still sinful.
The text says 'فينبغي التسوية بينهما في الحكم وهو عدم التكفير'.

He struck the instrument covering his face and his hands including his elbows with two strikes, even if in a state of major impurity or menstruation, with pure earth of its kind. Then she performs tayammum. And it is appropriate that due to the woman, and the dead person is performed tayammum upon, and if instead of a menstruating woman there was a person in minor impurity, it is diverted to the junub [major impurity]. etc. And in al-Zahiriya: the generality of scholars said the dead is more deserving, and it was said the junub is more deserving, and it is the most correct. etc. And in al-Muhit: they should divert their share to washing the dead and both perform tayammum when it is shared. And in al-Tanjish: a man was in the desert and he had only a bottle of Zamzam water in his saddlebag and he has bandaged his head, and it is not permissible for him to perform tayammum if he does not fear for himself thirst because it is one water, and frequently the ignorant pilgrim is afflicted with this and thinks it suffices him, and the legal trick is that he gift it to someone else, then he deposits the water from him. etc. Qadikhan said in his Fatawa: except that this is not correct according to me, for if he saw another person with water selling it at the same price or with a slight loss, he is obliged to buy, and tayammum is not permissible for him. If he is able to revoke the gift, how can he own it? Tayammum is permissible for him. etc. And it is rebutted in Fath al-Qadir by saying that it can be differentiated: that revocation is disliked and it is required not to exist legally, so it is permissible to consider the water as non-existent in his right similarly, even if he is able over it actually, like the water of a water-skin, contrary to sale. etc. And it was said the legal trick is that he mixes it with rose water until it prevails, so it no longer remains purifying. Thus in al-Tawshih. And the imprisoned who does not find purifying water, he does not pray according to them two, and according to Abu Yusuf he prays with gesture then repeats, and it is a narration from Muhammad imitating the worshippers to fulfill the right of time, as in fasting. And according to both of them, he is not fit for performance due to the state of impurity, so he is not obliged to imitate, like the menstruating woman. And by this issue it is shown that praying intentionally without purification is not disbelief, for if it were disbelief, Abu Yusuf would not have commanded it. And it was said it is disbelief like praying toward a direction other than qibla or with a najis garment intentionally because he is like a contemptuous person, and the most correct is that if he prays toward other than qibla or with a najis garment, he does not become a disbeliever because that cannot be performed at all. And if he prays without purification intentionally, he becomes a disbeliever because that is forbidden in every case; so if he prays without purification intentionally, he has been careless and contemptuous of the command of Shari'ah, so he becomes a disbeliever. Thus in al-Muhit. And we have previously presented from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya that the one whose hands and feet are cut off, if he has a wound on his face, he prays without purification, does not perform tayammum, and does not repeat, and this is the most correct. So praying without purification is analogous to praying toward other than qibla or with a najis garment; thus the ruling should be equal between them, which is non-disbelief, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding the ruling of tayammum from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It begins by stating the manner of tayammum: two strikes covering the face and hands to the elbows, using pure earth, even for janabah or menstruation. It then discusses cases where water is scarce, such as having only Zamzam water and fearing thirst. The legal trick (hila) of giving away water to permit tayammum is examined, with Qadikhan noting that if one can buy water at a reasonable price, tayammum is not allowed. The passage then addresses the case of an imprisoned person who cannot find water: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two), he does not pray; Abu Yusuf allows prayer with gesture. This leads to a discussion on whether praying without tayammum intentionally constitutes kufr. The text presents two views: one distinguishes it from prayer without qibla or with najis garment, deeming it not kufr; another considers it kufr. The author leans toward the view that it is not kufr, citing the ruling for an amputee with facial wounds who prays without purification. The commentary concludes that the ruling should be consistent: intentional prayer without tayammum is not disbelief, just as prayer toward the wrong qibla or with najis garment is not disbelief.

Key Terms
كفر (kufr): Disbelief; an act that removes one from the fold of Islam.
محبوس (mahbus): Imprisoned person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the imprisoned person who cannot find water according to Abu Hanifa?
A) He prays with gesture and repeats.
B) He does not pray.
C) He prays normally.
D) He combines prayers.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that an imprisoned person without water should not pray (according to Abu Hanifa), but if he does, it is not disbelief.

Taharah — Purification

Isti'ab in Tayammum: Condition or Pillar
Grammatical and legal analysis of 'mustaw'iban'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a condition and a pillar in tayammum and state the Hanafi ruling on full coverage.

Core Idea
Full coverage in tayammum is a pillar, not a condition—its omission invalidates the act entirely.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks a seemingly simple word in the matn: 'mustaw'iban' (covering completely). The commentator uses grammatical analysis to settle whether full coverage (isti'ab) is a condition external to the act or a pillar integral to it. Understanding this distinction is crucial because it determines whether a small omission requires a full repeat or just compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical status
Examine how the word 'mustaw'iban' functions in the matn: is it a description (sifah) of the omitted infinitive or a circumstantial accusative (hal)? The commentator argues it is a description, which strengthens the case for isti'ab being a pillar.
Al-Zayla'i allowed the hal reading, but the preferred view is sifah.
2
Understand the legal consequence
If isti'ab is a pillar (rukn), leaving even a tiny area unwiped invalidates tayammum. If it were a condition (shart), it might be external and perhaps dispensable under necessity.
The passage quotes many authorities affirming the fard (obligatory) nature of isti'ab.
3
Note the minority narration
Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa that covering the majority suffices, likening it to wiping the head. This is a weak (nawadir) transmission and not acted upon.
The analogy to masah al-ra's is rejected because tayammum is a substitute for wudu, which requires full coverage.
4
Apply to practical details
The passage applies the rule to real cases: removing a ring, interlocking fingers, wiping elbows, amputee stumps, and the requirement to wipe with the whole or most of the hand.
Order (tartib) is not a condition; 'wa' indicates simultaneity, not sequence.
5
Resolve the terminology confusion
Some early Hanafi scholars called isti'ab a 'condition' but meant 'indispensable part', which is effectively a pillar. The commentator clarifies that the correct classification is rukn.
This resolves apparent contradictions in the school.

His saying: (covering his face and his hands including his elbows) meaning he performs tayammum completely covering; so it is a description of the source omitted, and al-Zayla'i allowed that it be a circumstantial accusative from the pronoun in 'he performs tayammum' so it becomes an expected circumstance. Know that isti'ab is an obligatory duty in the apparent transmission from our companions so that even if he leaves a little from the places of tayammum, it is not permissible. And more than one stated that this is the correct view: among them Qadikhan, and the author of al-Majma' and the author of al-Ikhtiyar stated it is the most correct, and the author of al-Khulasa and al-Walwaliji stated it is the chosen view, and the commentator of al-Wiqaya said that the fatwa is upon it. Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the word 'mustaw'iban' (covering) from the matn. It begins with a grammatical analysis: whether it is a description (sifah) of the omitted source or a circumstantial accusative (hal). The preferred view is that it is a description, because isti'ab (full coverage) is a pillar (rukn) of tayammum without which it is not valid. The passage then discusses the substantive ruling: in the zahir al-riwayah of the Hanafi school, isti'ab is fard (obligatory), so leaving any part uncovered invalidates tayammum. This is affirmed by many scholars including Qadikhan. However, a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa says that covering the majority suffices due to necessity or because wiping does not require full coverage, analogous to wiping the head. Another view, attributed to Khulasa, holds that if the omitted part is less than a quarter, it suffices. The commentary then addresses practical details: the need to interlace fingers, remove or move a ring, and wipe the elbows with the forearms. This is according to the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), contrary to Zufar. For an amputee, the stump is wiped. For amputation above the elbow, no wiping is required. The passage also mentions wiping under the brows and above the eyes, and notes that beard wiping is not required in tayammum. It clarifies that order (tartib) is not a condition in tayammum, as indicated by the use of 'wa' instead of 'thumma'. It also specifies that wiping must be with the whole or most of the hand, not one or two fingers. The passage concludes with a quotation from al-Nahr on a terminological point and a reference to al-Hilya.

Key Terms
استيعاب (isti'ab): Full coverage of the face and hands to elbows in tayammum.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known and authoritative transmission from Abu Hanifa and his two companions, as recorded in the six books of Imam Muhammad.
ركن (rukn): A fundamental integral part of an act; its omission invalidates the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person leaves a very small area (less than a quarter) unwiped in tayammum?
A) It is acceptable because the area is small.
B) It is acceptable according to the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa.
C) It is not permissible; tayammum is invalid because isti'ab is fard.
D) It is makruh but tayammum is valid.

Key Takeaway
Isti'ab (full coverage) in tayammum is a pillar (rukn) according to the authoritative Hanafi position; any omission, however small, invalidates the tayammum.

The Obligation of Comprehensive Coverage (Isti'ab) in Tayammum
Determining the ruling on comprehensive wiping of face and hands in tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that comprehensive coverage (isti'ab) is farḍ in tayammum according to the relied-upon Hanafi position and explain the proof from the Quranic command and the analogy to wudu.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires full coverage of face and hands; any omission invalidates it.

Tayammum is a substitute for wudu, so its rules must closely mirror those of wudu. One key rule is that the wiping must cover the entire face and hands. This lesson examines the textual proof and the internal Hanafi discussion about whether a slight omission might be excused. By the end, you will understand why the school insists on complete coverage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the opening sentence: 'الاستيعاب فرض لازم في ظاهر الرواية' — comprehensive coverage is a binding obligation. Recognise that this is the ruling for tayammum, not wudu.
The term 'ظاهر الرواية' indicates this is the standard transmitted position.
2
Locate the primary proof (naqli)
The author argues that the command in the Quran (فَامْسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِكُمْ وَأَيْدِيكُمْ) uses definite nouns (الوجه, اليدين) which, according to Hanafi usul, imply the entire entity. This is the wajh al-dalalah.
The proof is from the text itself, not from istihsan.
3
Understand the secondary proof (qiyas)
Tayammum is a substitute for wudu (بدل عن الوضوء). In wudu, full coverage is integral to the act; thus in the substitute, the same requirement applies. This is an analogical argument.
The analogy reinforces the textual command.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa that the majority suffices, citing widespread need (kathrat al-balwa) or analogy to wiping the head (where full coverage is not required). This is a weaker riwayah.
The text explicitly overrides this with 'وجه غير لازم' (a non‑binding reason).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author lists multiple authorities (Qaḍīkhān, Ṣāḥib al‑Ikhtiyār, etc.) who affirm that the correct view is full coverage, and that fatwa is given accordingly. The weaker view is not relied upon.
This establishes the operative position for practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أن الاستيعاب فرض لازم في ظاهر الرواية عن أصحابنا حتى لو ترك شيئاً قليلاً من مواضع التيمم لا يجوز. ونص غير واحد أن هذا هو الصحيح منهم قاضيخان ونص صاحب المجمع وصاحب الاختيار على أنه الأصح، وصاحب الخلاصة والولوالجي على أنه المختار، وشارح الوقاية أن عليه الفتوى، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أن الأكثر يقوم مقام الكل لوجه غير لازم وهو إما لكثرة البلوى أو لأنه مسح فلا يجب فيه الاستيعاب كمسح الرأس. وفي تفصيل عقد الفوائد بتكميل قيد الشرائد معزياً إلى الخلاصة أن المتروك لو كان أقل من الربع يجزئه وهو الأصح والظاهر أن ليس المراد بها خلاصة الفتاوى المشهورة فإن فيها أن المختار افتراض الاستيعاب، ووجه ظاهر الرواية أن الأمر بالمسح في باب التيمم تعلق باسم الوجه واليدين وأنه يعم الكل، ولأن التيمم بدل عن الوضوء والاستيعاب في الأصل من تمام الركن في البدل فيلزمه تخليل الأصابع ونزع الخاتم أو تحريكه ولو ترك لم يجز، وعلى رواية الحسن لا يلزمه ويمسح المرفقين مع الذراعين عند أصحابنا الثلاثة خلافاً لزفر حتى لو كان مقطوع اليدين من المرفقين يمسح موضع القطع عندنا خلافاً لزفر . والكلام فيه كالكلام في الوضوء وقد مر . كذا في البدائع وفي المحيط : وإن كان القطع فوق المرفق لا يجب المسح ويمسح تحت الحاجبين وفوق العينين. وفي فتح القدير معزياً إلى الحلية تبعاً للدراية : يمسح من وجهه ظاهر البشرة والشعر على الصحيح ا هـ. لكن في السراج الوهاج : لا يجب عليه مسح اللحية في التيمم ولا مسح الجبيرة ولو مسح بإحدى يديه وجهه وبالأخرى يديه أجزأه في الوجه واليد الأولى ويعيد الضرب لليد الأخرى ا هـ. وفي تعبيره بالواو في قوله ويديه» دون «ثم» إشارة إلى أن الترتيب ليس بشرط فيه كأصله. ويشترط المسح بجميع اليد أو بأكثرها حتى لو مسح بأصبع واحدة أو اصبعين لا يجوز، ولو كرر المسح حتى استوعب بخلاف مسح الرأس. كذا في السراج الوهاج معزياً إلى الايضاح. وفي تتميماً للحيلة تأمل قوله : ( ولعل وجهه الخ) قال في النهر : فإن قلت قد وقع في عبارة بعض علمائنا المتقدمين أنه شرط و به صرح الشارح وعليه فلا يتجه التوجيه قلت : حمله في عقد الفرائد على ما لا بد منه وإلا فهو ركن قطعاً. وفي البدائع هل هو من تمام الركن لم يذكر في الأصل ولكنه ذكر ما يدل عليه قال : وهو ظاهر الرواية على أن مجيء اسم الفاعل صفة أكثر من مجيئه حالاً. إذا عرف هذا فما جرى عليه العيني من أنه حال وكونه صفة احتمال فيه نظر لا يخفى قوله: (وفي فتح القدير معزياً إلى الحلية أقول : في حفظي أن الحلية التي ينقل عنها في معراج الدراية من كتب لا المجتبى : ومسح العذار شرط على ما حكي عن أصحابنا والناس عنه غافلون. وفي المحيط عن محمد في رجل يرى التيمم إلى الرسغ والوتر ركعة ثم رأى التيمم إلى المرفق والوتر ثلاثاً يعيد ما صلى لأنه مجتهد فيه، وإن فعل ذلك من غير أن يسأل أحد ثم سأل فأمر بثلاث يعيد ما صلى لأنه غير مجتهد ا.هـ. وفي معراج الدراية : ولو أمر غيره أن ييممه ونوى هو جاز. وقال ابن القاضي : لا يجزئه ا هـ . والناوي هو الأمر كما لا يخفى. وفي شرح المجمع : وأما استيعاب الوجه في التيمم فليس مستفاداً من الإلصاق بل لأنه عن الغسل فلزم الاستيعاب في الخلف حسب لزومه في الأصل ا.هـ. وقد قدمناه في مسح الرأس.
Know that comprehensive coverage (isti'ab) is an obligatory requirement in the zahir al-riwayah from our scholars, such that if one leaves even a small part of the places of tayammum, it is not permissible. Several scholars have stated that this is the correct view: Qadikhan, the author of al-Majma', and the author of al-Ikhtiyar held it as the most correct; the author of al-Khulasah and al-Walwaliji held it as the chosen view; and the commentator of al-Wiqayah stated that the fatwa is upon it. Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifah that the majority suffices for the whole for a reason not binding, either due to widespread need or because it is wiping, so comprehensive coverage is not required, like wiping the head. In the detail of 'Uqd al-Fawa'id... that if the omitted part is less than a quarter, it suffices him, and that is the most correct. The apparent meaning is that this is not from the well-known Khulasat al-Fatawa, for therein the chosen view is the obligation of comprehensive coverage. The evidence of the zahir al-riwayah is that the command to wipe in the chapter of tayammum is attached to the term 'face' and 'hands', and that term encompasses the whole. Also, because tayammum is a substitute for wudu, and comprehensive coverage in the original (wudu) is part of the complete integral, so in the substitute it becomes necessary. Thus he must cause water to reach between fingers and remove or move his ring; if he leaves it, it is not valid. According to the riwayah of al-Hasan, it is not required of him. He also wipes the elbows together with the forearms according to our three imams, contrary to Zufar, such that if his hands are amputated at the elbows, he wipes the place of amputation according to us, contrary to Zufar. The discussion about it is like the discussion in wudu, and it has passed. Similarly in al-Bada'i' and in al-Muhit: If the amputation is above the elbow, wiping is not required. He wipes under the eyebrows and above the eyes. In Fath al-Qadir attributed to al-Hilyah following al-Dirayah: He wipes from his face the apparent skin and hair according to the correct view. But in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: He is not required to wipe the beard in tayammum, nor to wipe the splint. If he wipes his face with one hand and his hands with the other, it suffices for the face and the first hand, and he repeats the strike for the other hand. His expression with 'and' in saying 'and his hands' instead of 'then' indicates that order is not a condition in it, as in its original (wudu). It is required to wipe with the entire hand or most of it, such that if he wipes with one finger or two fingers, it is not valid, even if he repeats the wiping until he covers the area, unlike wiping the head. Similarly in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj attributed to al-Idah. And as a completion... [continues with further commentary]
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the obligation of comprehensive coverage (isti'ab) in tayammum. The author establishes that in the zahir al-riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad), wiping must cover the entire face and hands. Leaving any part invalidates the tayammum. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). The proof is that the Quranic command to wipe the face and hands uses general terms that imply full coverage, and tayammum substitutes for wudu, where isti'ab is integral. A weaker riwayah from Hasan ibn Ziyad holds that majority suffices, akin to wiping the head. Some later scholars (like in 'Uqd al-Fawa'id) suggest that if the omitted area is less than a quarter, it may be excused, but this is not the standard fatwa. The passage then details related rulings: wiping the elbows, amputation cases, beard, splints, wiping with one hand vs. two, and that order is not a condition. The overall message is clarity: full coverage is the strict requirement, with minimal concessions only in rare riwayat.

Key Terms
استيعاب (isti'ab): Comprehensive coverage of the entire face and hands during wiping in tayammum
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted position from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad through the six core books (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.)
تخليل الأصابع (tahlil al-asabi'): Making water or dust reach between the fingers; required in wudu and tayammum for full coverage

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, what is the ruling if someone leaves a small part of the face unwiped during tayammum?
A) Tayammum is valid as long as most of the face is wiped.
B) Tayammum is invalid because comprehensive coverage (isti'ab) is fard.
C) Tayammum is valid if the omitted area is smaller than a quarter of the face.
D) Tayammum is valid and no compensation is needed.

Key Takeaway
In tayammum, comprehensive coverage (isti'ab) of face and hands is fard; leaving any uncovered area invalidates the act.

Two Strikes Are the Rukn of Tayammum: Text and Application
Ruling with proof on number of strikes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that two strikes are a rukn of tayammum, explain the evidence from the hadith, and apply the ruling in scenarios involving a third strike for tahlil.

Core Idea
Two strikes are a rukn; a third strike is only for tahlil, not part of the essence.

The matn states that tayammum is performed with two strikes. The commentator expands on whether the third strike is part of the act or merely for tahlil. This passage clarifies the Hanafi ruling: two strikes are a rukn based on the explicit hadith, and any need for a third is only to ensure dust enters between the fingers, not as an integral part of tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being discussed? Tayammum. What is the ruling? Two strikes are obligatory (fard/rukn).
The matn says 'with two strikes' – directly stating the number.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith 'التيمم ضربتان' (Tayammum is two strikes) is cited as the evidence. Why is this a strong proof?
The phrase explicitly specifies the number.
3
Understand the dispute over three strikes
Ibn Sirin and some early scholars argued for three strikes by analogy with wudu (three washes for arms). How does the Hanafi school respond?
The hadith overrides qiyas; the third strike is only a means for tahlil, not a rukn.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi nuance
Even among Hanafis, there is a discussion: if after the first strike an invalidating event occurs, must one repeat the strike? Abu Shuja' says yes; al-Isbijabi says it suffices. Which view is mufta bihi?
The relied-upon position (al-Khulasah, Shams al-A'immah) is that two strikes are a rukn, so the first strike alone is not sufficient.
5
Apply the ruling to edge cases
What if dust is blown onto the limbs by wind? The text mentions that the striking of the ground is not necessary if dust already reaches the limbs. The key is the wiping (mash), not the act of striking.
This aligns with the principle that the essence is applying dust, not the specific motion of striking.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بضربتين) الباء متعلقة بتيمم أي يتيمم بضربتين، وقد وقع ذكر الضرب في كثير الكتب والمذكور في الأصل الوضع دون الضرب، وفي بعض الروايات الضرب فاختلف من المشايخ فيه؛ فمنهم كالمصنف في المستصفى من قال بأنهم إنما اختاروه، وإن كان الوضع جائزاً لما أن الآثار جاءت بلفظ الضرب وفي غاية البيان والمقصود من الضرب أن يدخل الغبار في خلال الأصابع تحقيقاً لمعنى الاستيعاب وتعقب ما في المستصفى بأن الضرب لم . يذكر في الآية ولا في سائر الآثار وإنما جاء في بعضها ومنهم من ذهب إلى أن المقصود بذكر الضربتين الرد على ابن سيرين ومن تبعه أنه لا بد من ثلاث ضربات ضربة للوجه وضربة للكفين وضربة للذراعين وأما ما روي عن محمد من الاحتياج إلى ثلاث ضربات فليس افتراضاً للثالثة لذاتها بل لتخليل الأصابع إذا لم يدخل الغبار بينها وهو خلاف النص والمقصود هو التخليل لا يتوقف عليه ومنهم من ذهب إلى أن الضربتين ركن للخبر الوارد «التيمم ضربتان فهما من ماهية التيمم، ومن ثم قال السيد أبو شجاع : إنه لو أحدث بعد الضربة أعادها ولا يجزئه المسح بما في يده من التراب وصححه في الخلاصة وهو مختار شمس الأئمة ولكن قال القاضي الاسبيجابي : إن الضربة تجزئه كما في الوضوء حيث يتوضأ بذلك الماء. وفرق السيد أبو شجاع بينهما بأن الشرط في الوضوء الحصول وفي التيمم التحصيل. وأجيب عنه بأن التحصيل شرط فلا ينافي الحدث كما لو أحرم مجامعاً. وفي فتح القدير بعد ما ذكر الخلاف وعلى هذا فما صرحوا به من أنه لو ألقت الريح الغبار على وجهه ويديه فمسح بنية التيمم أجزاء وإن لم يمسح لا يجوز يلزم فيه، إما كونه قول من أخرج الخوبة لا قول الكل، وإنا اعتبار الضربة أعم من كونها على الأرض أو على العضو مسحاً، والذي يقتضيه النظر عدم اعتبار ضربة الأرض من مسمى التيمم شرعاً فإن المأمور به المسح الشافعية وحينئذ فلا ينافي ما في السراج قوله : (وتعقب ما في المستصفى الخ) قال في النهر : هذا لا يصلح دفعاً كما لا يخفى قوله: (والمقصود وهو التخليل لا يتوقق عليه) أي على الضرب الثالث ولكن سيأتي أن محمداً يشترط الغبار فلو لم يدخل بين أصابعه يحتاج إلى الثالثة ليخلل بالغبار على
His statement: 'with two strikes' – the ba' is attached to 'tayammum', meaning he performs tayammum with two strikes. The mention of 'strike' occurs in many books, but in the original (matn) it is 'placing' not 'striking'. In some transmissions it is 'striking', so the scholars differed on it. Among them, like the author in al-Mustasfa, said that they chose it even though 'placing' is permissible, because the traditions came with the wording 'striking', and in Ghayat al-Bayan, the purpose of striking is to cause dust to enter between the fingers, achieving comprehensive coverage. The objection to al-Mustasfa is that 'striking' is not mentioned in the verse nor in all traditions, only in some. Some scholars held that the purpose of mentioning two strikes is to refute Ibn Sirin and his followers, who held that three strikes are necessary: one for the face, one for the palms, and one for the forearms. As for what is narrated from Muhammad about needing three strikes, it is not because the third is obligatory in itself, but for tahlil (making dust reach between fingers) if dust does not enter between them otherwise. This is contrary to the text (hadith), and the purpose is tahlil, not the third strike. Other scholars held that two strikes are a pillar (rukn) because of the hadith 'Tayammum is two strikes, so they are part of the essence of tayammum.' Hence, al-Sayyid Abu Shuja' said: If he had an invalidating event after the first strike, he must repeat it, and it is not valid for him to wipe with the dust on his hand. This is authenticated in al-Khulasah and is the chosen view of Shams al-A'immah. But al-Qadi al-Isbijabi said: The strike suffices him, like in wudu where one performs wudu with that water. Al-Sayyid Abu Shuja' differentiated: In wudu, the condition is obtaining (water), while in tayammum it is seeking (the dust). The response was: Seeking is a condition, so it does not conflict with having an invalidating event, like one who enters ihram while in a state of major impurity. In Fath al-Qadir after mentioning the dispute... [continues]
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof lesson on the number of strikes required in tayammum. The matn states 'with two strikes', and the commentator expands on it. The core ruling is that tayammum is performed with two strikes: one for the face and one for the hands. This is based on the hadith 'التيمم ضربتان' (Tayammum is two strikes). Some scholars, like Ibn Sirin, argued for three strikes, but the Hanafi school rejects this, considering the third only for tahlil (making dust enter between fingers) if needed. A key intra-Hanafi dispute emerges: Abu Shuja' holds that if one breaks wudu after the first strike, he must repeat the strike; al-Isbijabi says the first strike suffices. The relied-upon position is that two strikes are a rukn (integral part) of tayammum, and any event invalidating wudu necessitates starting over. The passage also discusses whether striking the ground is required if dust reaches the limbs by wind; the sounder view is that a strike on the ground is not required - what matters is applying dust to the limbs.

Key Terms
ضربة (darbah): The act of striking the hands on the ground for tayammum; each strike is a distinct action
تخليل (tahlil): Making dust enter between the fingers by rubbing or a third strike if needed
ركن (rukn): An integral part of an act; omission invalidates the act entirely

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, how many strikes are an integral part (rukn) of tayammum?
A) One strike
B) Two strikes
C) Three strikes
D) Four strikes

Key Takeaway
Two strikes are a rukn of tayammum; the third is only a means for tahlil, not part of the essence.

The Two Strikes in Tayammum: Rukn or Not?
Commentary on the ruling of two strikes in tayammum and intra-Hanafi opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the number of strikes in tayammum, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Two strikes in tayammum: a pillar or a sunnah? The Hanafi school is divided, but the relied-upon view is that striking the ground is not an essential part.

The Hanafi school is not monolithic on every detail. One such internal disagreement concerns the number of strikes (ḍarbatayn) in tayammum. The Quran only mentions wiping, but a hadith mentions 'two strikes.' Does this make two strikes a pillar (rukn) without which tayammum is void, or merely a recommended practice? This lesson explores the positions of major Hanafi authorities and the reasoning behind the preferred opinion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and disputed element
The act is tayammum. The disputed element is the nature of the two strikes: are they a rukn (integral) or something less?
The Quran (4:43) commands wiping, not striking, so striking is derived from hadith.
2
List the intra-Hanafi opinions
Three main views: (1) Two strikes are rukn (Abu Shuja', Shams al-A'imma). (2) One strike suffices (Qadi al-Isbijabi). (3) Two strikes are not rukn but recommended (majority, including the author of this commentary). Also note the refutation of Ibn Sirin's required three strikes.
Imam Muhammad's reported need for a third strike is for intercalation only, not an obligation.
3
Analyze the proofs for each opinion
The hadith 'al-tayammum ḍarbatān' is the primary proof. Those who consider it a rukn take it literally. Others argue it is descriptive, not prescriptive, and the Quran only requires wiping.
The Hanafi principle: an isolated hadith (khabar wāḥid) creates obligation but not necessity of a rukn.
4
Determine the tarjih (preferred position)
The author favors that striking the ground is not part of the legal definition of tayammum; wiping suffices. This is the mufta bihi position.
Tarjih authority: the commentator (Ibn Nujaym) in Bahr al-Rā’iq and the author of Fath al-Qadīr support this view.
5
Apply the mufta bihi in practice
A Hanafi following the relied-upon view may perform tayammum with a single wipe of the hands on the ground, as long as the entire face and hands are covered with dust. However, two strikes are still recommended to follow the prophetic practice.
This affects fatwa: if someone misses one strike, tayammum is still valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بضربتين) الباء متعلقة بتيمم أي يتيمم بضربتين، وقد وقع ذكر الضرب في كثير الكتب والمذكور في الأصل الوضع دون الضرب، وفي بعض الروايات الضرب فاختلف من المشايخ فيه؛ فمنهم كالمصنف في المستصفى من قال بأنهم إنما اختاروه، وإن كان الوضع جائزاً لما أن الآثار جاءت بلفظ الضرب وفي غاية البيان والمقصود من الضرب أن يدخل الغبار في خلال الأصابع تحقيقاً لمعنى الاستيعاب وتعقب ما في المستصفى بأن الضرب لم . يذكر في الآية ولا في سائر الآثار وإنما جاء في بعضها ومنهم من ذهب إلى أن المقصود بذكر الضربتين الرد على ابن سيرين ومن تبعه أنه لا بد من ثلاث ضربات ضربة للوجه وضربة للكفين وضربة للذراعين وأما ما روي عن محمد من الاحتياج إلى ثلاث ضربات فليس افتراضاً للثالثة لذاتها بل لتخليل الأصابع إذا لم يدخل الغبار بينها وهو خلاف النص والمقصود هو التخليل لا يتوقف عليه ومنهم من ذهب إلى أن الضربتين ركن للخبر الوارد «التيمم ضربتان فهما من ماهية التيمم، ومن ثم قال السيد أبو شجاع : إنه لو أحدث بعد الضربة أعادها ولا يجزئه المسح بما في يده من التراب وصححه في الخلاصة وهو مختار شمس الأئمة ولكن قال القاضي الاسبيجابي : إن الضربة تجزئه كما في الوضوء حيث يتوضأ بذلك الماء. وفرق السيد أبو شجاع بينهما بأن الشرط في الوضوء الحصول وفي التيمم التحصيل. وأجيب عنه بأن التحصيل شرط فلا ينافي الحدث كما لو أحرم مجامعاً. وفي فتح القدير بعد ما ذكر الخلاف وعلى هذا فما صرحوا به من أنه لو ألقت الريح الغبار على وجهه ويديه فمسح بنية التيمم أجزاء وإن لم يمسح لا يجوز يلزم فيه، إما كونه قول من أخرج الخوبة لا قول الكل، وإنا اعتبار الضربة أعم من كونها على الأرض أو على العضو مسحاً، والذي يقتضيه النظر عدم اعتبار ضربة الأرض من مسمى التيمم شرعاً فإن المأمور به المسح
الشافعية وحينئذ فلا ينافي ما في السراج قوله : (وتعقب ما في المستصفى الخ) قال في النهر : هذا لا يصلح دفعاً كما لا يخفى قوله: (والمقصود وهو التخليل لا يتوقق عليه) أي على الضرب الثالث ولكن سيأتي أن محمداً يشترط الغبار فلو لم يدخل بين أصابعه يحتاج إلى الثالثة ليخلل بالغبار على
في الكتاب ليس غير قال تعالى فتيمموا صعيداً طيباً فامسحوا بوجوهكم﴾ [النساء : ٤٣] ويحمل قوله عليه السلام) التيمم ضربتان إما على إرادة الأعم من المسحتين كما قلنا أو أنه أخرج مخرج الغالب والله سبحانه أعلم ا هـ
His statement: (with two strikes) – the ba' is related to tayammum, i.e. he performs tayammum with two strikes. Mention of striking occurs in many books, but what is mentioned in the original (matn) is 'placing' (wad') not striking. In some narrations, striking is mentioned, so the early scholars differed on it. Among them is the author of al-Mustasfa who said they only chose striking (even though placing is permissible) because the traditions (athar) came with the wording 'striking'. In Ghayat al-Bayan, the purpose of striking is to make dust enter between the fingers to achieve comprehensive coverage. It was objected to what is in al-Mustasfa that striking is not mentioned in the Quran nor in other traditions, but only in some of them. Among them is one who opined that mentioning two strikes is a refutation of Ibn Sirin and those who followed him that three strikes are necessary: a strike for the face, a strike for the hands, and a strike for the forearms. As for what is reported from Muhammad of the need for three strikes, it is not an obligation of a third for itself, but for intercalating the fingers if dust does not enter between them, which is contrary to the text. The purpose is intercalation, which does not depend on it. Among them is one who opined that two strikes are a pillar due to the reported hadith 'Tayammum is two strikes', and they are part of the essence of tayammum. Hence al-Sayyid Abu Shuja' said: If he breaks his wudu after the strike, he repeats it and it is not sufficient to wipe with the dust in his hand. This was authenticated in al-Khulasa and is the chosen view of Shams al-A'imma. But al-Qadi al-Isbijabi said: The one strike suffices him, just as in wudu he performs wudu with that water. Abu Shuja' distinguished between them by saying: The condition in wudu is obtaining (husul), and in tayammum is securing (tahsil). It was answered that securing is a condition, so it does not conflict with breaking wudu, just as if he assumed ihram while in a state of intercourse. In Fath al-Qadir after mentioning the disagreement: On this basis, what they explicitly stated that if the wind blew dust on his face and hands and he wiped with the intention of tayammum, it suffices, but if he did not wipe, it is not permissible. It necessarily entails either that it is the view of those who exclude the void (khawba), not the view of all, and that we consider the strike to be generic, whether on the ground or on the limb as wiping. What is required by consideration is that striking the ground is not part of the meaning of tayammum legally, because what is commanded is wiping. The Shafi'is? At that point, it does not contradict what is in al-Siraj. His statement: (And what is objected to what is in al-Mustasfa...) al-Nahr said: This is not a valid refutation, as is not hidden. His statement: (And the purpose is intercalation does not depend on it) i.e. on the third strike, but it will come that Muhammad requires dust, so if it does not enter between his fingers, he needs the third to intercalate with dust on... In the book it says nothing else, Allah said: 'So perform tayammum with clean earth and wipe your faces and your hands.' [4:43] And his statement, peace be upon him: 'Tayammum is two strikes' is interpreted either to mean the generic from two wipings as we said, or that it came as the dominant case. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the number of strikes (ضربتين) in tayammum. The author first notes that the original text (matn) says 'with two strikes' but some sources mention 'placing' instead. The dispute centers on whether the two strikes are essential (rukn) or merely recommended. The first opinion, attributed to the author of Mustasfa, holds that striking is chosen due to prophetic practice but placing is permissible. The purpose of striking is to ensure dust enters between the fingers for comprehensive coverage. The second opinion refutes Ibn Sirin's requirement of three strikes—the third is not a separate strike but only for intercalation if dust did not enter. The third opinion, from al-Sayyid Abu Shuja' and Shams al-A'imma, considers the two strikes a pillar based on the hadith 'Tayammum is two strikes'; thus, if one performs one strike and then breaks wudu, he must repeat the strike and cannot use the remaining dust. Qadi al-Isbijabi disagrees, analogizing to wudu where one can use water after minor impurity. Abu Shuja' distinguishes: in wudu, water is already obtained (husul), while in tayammum, one must secure (tahsil) the dust. The author notes the response that tahsil is a condition and does not conflict with breaking wudu. The passage also refutes the idea that wind-blown dust suffices without an act—this only applies to those who exclude the 'void' (khawba) from the definition of strike. Ultimately, the author favors that 'strike' is broader than just hitting the ground—any action that brings dust to the limb suffices, as the Quran only mentions wiping. The hadith's mention of 'two strikes' is interpreted as referring to two wipings or as the common occurrence.

Key Terms
ضربتين (ḍarbatayn): Two strikes of the hands on the ground in tayammum.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with dust, replacing wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
ركن (rukn): An essential part; omission invalidates the act entirely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Sayyid Abu Shuja', what is the ruling if a person performs one strike in tayammum and then breaks their wudu?
A) The tayammum is complete and they may wipe with the dust remaining on their hands.
B) They must repeat the strike and cannot use the remaining dust.
C) They must repeat both strikes and start anew.
D) The tayammum is valid but they must repeat wudu.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that two strikes in tayammum are not a pillar; a single wipe suffices as long as the entire face and hands are covered with dust.

Method of Tayammum and the Ruling on Used Dust
Method and conditions of tayammum with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the valid method of tayammum according to the Hanafi school and explain the ruling on using already-used dust (musta'mal).

Core Idea
Tayammum requires intentional action; the cautious method avoids using 'used' dust, which remains valid for reuse.

In this lesson, we examine the detailed method of tayammum as recorded by the Hanafi masters. The text from al-Bahr al-Raiq explores the condition of an intentional act, the proper sequence of strikes and wipings, and the debated issue of whether dust becomes 'used' (musta'mal) after the first wipe, affecting the second wipe. Understanding these details ensures the validity of tayammum in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core condition
Recognize that tayammum requires an intentional action from the person, not merely the presence of dust. For example, if dust blows onto the face without intention, it does not count.
This is from al-Khulasa: the condition is 'the existence of an action from him'.
2
Outline the two-strike method
Learn the standard method: first strike hands on earth, shake, wipe face; second strike, shake, wipe hands and forearms up to elbows. Some scholars add a specific order for the arms.
The method from al-Muhit is cited.
3
Locate the cautious method (al-ahwat)
Understand the 'most cautious' method described by 'our scholars' which details wiping each arm with specific fingers to avoid using dust that may have become musta'mal.
This prevents reuse of possibly used dust.
4
Understand the used dust debate
Analyze the disagreement: some Hanafis hold that dust becomes musta'mal (like used water) after wiping and cannot be reused; others argue it does not become used and can be reapplied. The cautious method avoids this issue.
The author notes that the cautious method is preferred.
5
Apply the ruling to examples
Consider scenarios: paralyzed hands wiping on a wall, tayammum by proxy, and timing of intention relative to strikes. Use the rules derived from the text to determine validity.
These examples are from the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أعلم أن الشرط وجود الفعل منه أعم من أن يكون مسحاً أو ضرباً أو غيره فقد قال في الخلاصة : ولو أدخل رأسه في موضع الغبار بنية التيمم يجوز، ولو انهدم الحائط وظهر الغبار فحرك رأسه ونوى التيمم جاز والشرط وجود الفعل منه ا هـ . وهذا يعين أن هذه الفروع مبنية على قول من أخرج الضربة من مسمى التيمم، وأما من أدخلها فلا يمكنه القول بها فيما نقلناه عن الخلاصة إذا ليس فيها ضرب أصلاً لا على الأرض ولا على العضو إلا أن يقال : مراده بالضرب الفعل منه أعم من كونه ضرباً أو غيره وهو بعيد كما لا يخفى وتظهر ثمرة الخلاف أيضاً فيما إذا نوى بعد الضرب فمن جعله ركناً لم يعتبر النية بعده، ومن لم يجعله ركناً اعتبرها بعده. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي الخلاصة : ولو شلت كلا يديه يمسح وجهه وذراعيه على الحائط ا هـ. وقد قدمنا أنه لو أمر غيره بأن ييممه جاز بشرط أن ينوي الآمر ، فلو ضرب المأمور يده على الأرض بعدنية الأمر ثم أحدث الآمر قال في التوشيح : ينبغي أن يبطل بحدث الآمر على قول أبي شجاع وظاهره أنه لا يبطل بحدث المأمور لما أن المأمور آلة وضربه ضرب للآمر فالعبرة للأمر ولهذا اشترطنا نيته لا نية المأمور وفي المحيط : وكيفية التيمم أن يضرب يديه على الأرض ثم ينفضهما فيمسح بهما وجهه بحيث لا يبقى منه شيء وإن قل، ثم يضرب يديه ثانياً على الأرض ثم ينفضهما فيمسح بهما كفيه وذراعيه كليهما إلى المرفقين .
اه.
6
وقال مشايخنا : يضرب يديه ثانياً ويمسح بأربع أصابع يده اليسرى ظاهر يده اليمنى من رؤوس الأصابع إلى المرفق ثم يمسح بكفه اليسرى باطن يده اليمنى إلى الرسغ ويمر باطن إبهامه اليسرى على ظاهر إبهامه اليمنى، ثم يفعل باليد اليسرى كذلك وهو الأحوط لأن فيه احترازاً عن استعمال المستعمل بالقدر الممكن فإن التراب الذي على يده يصير مستعملاً بالمسح
قوله قوله : (فيمسح بهما كفيه وذراعيه أي ويمر بباطن إبهامه اليسرى على ظاهر إبهامه اليمني . قال العارف في شرح الهدية وقال والدي رحمه الله بعد نقله هذه الكيفية : وهذه الصورة حكاية ابن عمر رضي الله تعالى عنهما تيمم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وكذا روى جابر أيضاً قوله : (فإن التراب الذي على يده يصير مستعملاً بالمسح فيه نظر لأنه إن استعمل بأول الوضع يلزم أن لا يجزىء في باقي العضو وألا يستعمل بأول الوضع كالماء لا يلزم ما ذكره وهو كذلك، يؤيده ما قاله العارف في شرح هدية ابن العماد عن جامع الفتاوى . وقيل : يمسح بجميع الكف والأصابع لأن التراب لا مستعملاً يصير في محله كالماء اهـ. ولذا عبر بعضهم في هذه الكيفية بقوله والأحسن إشارة إلى تجويز خلافه إلا أن يقال : المراد أنه يصير مستعملاً صورة لا حقيقة ولكن الفرق ظاهر بين هذا وبين قوله «حتى لو ضرب يديه مرة الخ» تأمل . قوله : (إذ لا جمع بينهما كما لا يخفى قال في النهر : وغير خاف أن
Then know that the condition is the existence of an action from him, whether it be wiping, striking, or otherwise. For it is said in al-Khulasa: If he puts his head into a place of dust with the intention of tayammum, it is permissible. If a wall collapses and dust appears, and he moves his head and intends tayammum, it is permissible, and the condition is the existence of an action from him, end. This determines that these branches are based on the view of those who exclude the strike from the meaning of tayammum. As for those who include it, they cannot say this regarding what we related from al-Khulasa, because there is no strike at all, neither on the ground nor on the limb, unless it is said: He means by 'strike' the action itself, whether it be a strike or otherwise, which is far-fetched as is not hidden. The fruit of the disagreement also appears concerning if he intended after the strike: for whoever makes it a rukn does not consider intention after it, and whoever does not make it a rukn considers it after it. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And in al-Khulasa: If both his hands are paralyzed, he wipes his face and forearms on the wall, end. We have already stated that if he orders someone else to perform tayammum for him, it is permissible provided that the one ordering intends. So if the one ordered strikes his hand on the ground with the intention of the orderer, then the orderer breaks his wudu, it is said in al-Tawshih: It should be invalidated by the orderer's breaking of wudu according to Abu Shuja'. Apparently, it is not invalidated by the breaking of wudu of the one ordered, because the one ordered is a tool and his strike is the orderer's strike, so consideration is for the orderer, and for this reason we required his intention, not the intention of the one ordered. And in al-Muhit: The method of tayammum is that he strikes his hands on the ground, then shakes them off, then wipes his face with them, leaving no part unwiped even if little. Then he strikes his hands a second time on the ground, shakes them off, then wipes his hands and forearms both up to the elbows. End. And our scholars said: He strikes his hands a second time and wipes with four fingers of his left hand the back of his right hand from the tips of the fingers to the elbow, then wipes with the palm of his left hand the inside of his right hand to the wrist, and passes the inside of his left thumb over the back of his right thumb. Then he does the same for the left hand. This is the most cautious because it avoids using already used dust as much as possible, for the dust on his hand becomes used by wiping. His statement: (Then wipes with them his hands and forearms) i.e. and passes the inside of his left thumb over the back of his right thumb. Al-Arif said in Sharh al-Hidayah: And my father, may Allah have mercy on him, said after quoting this method: This form is the narration of Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, of the tayammum of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. And similarly Jabir also narrated. His statement: (For the dust on his hand becomes used by wiping) requires consideration because if it is used by the first placement, then it would not suffice for the remaining limb; but if it is not used by the first placement, like water, then what he mentioned does not necessarily follow. This is supported by what al-Arif said in Sharh Hadiyyat Ibn al-Imad from Jami' al-Fatawa. And it is said: He wipes with the entire palm and fingers because dust does not become used; rather it is like water. End. Hence some expressed this method by saying 'and it is better' indicating the permissibility of the contrary, unless it is said: It becomes used in form, not reality. But the difference between this and his statement 'even if he strikes his hands once etc.' is apparent. Contemplate. His statement: (For there is no combination between them as is not hidden) al-Nahr said: And it is not hidden that...
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage covers the conditions and method of tayammum. The key condition is that there must be an action from the person, not merely the presence of dust. For example, if wind blows dust onto the face, one must still actively intend and move to achieve tayammum. The passage then discusses the practical consequence of the earlier disagreement on whether strikes are a rukn: if strikes are a rukn, intention must precede; if not, intention can follow. Next, the method is given: first strike hands on earth, shake, wipe face; second strike, shake, wipe right arm from fingertips to elbow with left hand's four fingers, then palm for inner side, then left arm similarly. This cautious method avoids using already used dust. The issue of 'used dust' (musta'mal) is debated: some say dust becomes used after wiping and cannot be reused, similar to used water; others say it does not become 'used' and can be used again, because dust is not a substance that becomes impure. The author notes that the cautious method avoids this issue. The narration from Ibn Umar and Jabir supports the described method.

Key Terms
مستعمل (musta'mal): Dust that has already been used for wiping; debate whether it remains pure for reuse.
الأحوط (al-ahwat): The more precautionary method, avoiding potential invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Dust must reach the face naturally.
B) There must be an intentional action from the person.
C) The person must recite a specific du'a.
D) The person must face the Qibla.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum requires an intentional act; the cautious method ensures validity and avoids disputes over used dust.
