Condition of Action in Tayammum and the Strike Dispute
Ruling with proof on the condition of action and the number of strikes in tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of tayammum, explain why the strike is not a rukn in the Hanafi school, and apply the thamarat al-khilaf to cases involving intention timing and agency.

Core Idea
The condition of tayammum is any action producing dust; the strike itself is not a rukn.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq tackles a subtle but critical point in tayammum: what exactly constitutes the act? The Quran commands wiping, while a hadith mentions 'two strikes.' The author reconciles these and establishes that the essential condition is simply the existence of an action from the person—whether striking, wiping, or even moving the head in dust. This ruling leads to an important intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the strike is a rukn, with practical consequences for the timing of intention and cases involving a deputy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
Find the key statement: 'الشرط وجود الفعل منه أعم من أن يكون مسحاً أو ضرباً أو غيره' – the condition is the existence of an action, whether wiping, striking, or other. This is the central ruling.
2
Trace the Dalil (Evidence)
Locate the Quranic verse (4:43) and the hadith 'التيمم ضربتان'. The author interprets the hadith broadly, either as referring to the general sense of action or as describing the common practice.
The dalil is used to support the broad definition of action.
3
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Identify that some Hanafis (e.g., Abu Shuja') consider the strike a rukn, while the majority (including the author) do not. The text provides examples from al-Khulasah that validate tayammum without a strike (e.g., inserting head in dust).
The majority view is relied upon (mufta bihi).
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
The dispute affects the timing of intention (niyyah). If the strike is a rukn, intention must precede it; if not, intention can come after the action. Also, the agent case is influenced.
This is a classic example of ikhtilaf having real fiqhi effects.
5
Apply to the Agent (Deputy) Case
When an agent performs tayammum for the principal, the validity depends on the principal's intention, and invalidation (naqd) is based on the principal's state, not the agent's.
The agent is merely a tool; the action is attributed to the principal.

في الكتاب ليس غير قال تعالى ﴿فتيمموا صعيداً طيباً فامسحوا بوجوهكم﴾ [النساء : ٤٣] ويحمل قوله عليه السلام) التيمم ضربتان إما على إرادة الأعم من المسحتين كما قلنا أو أنه أخرج مخرج الغالب والله سبحانه أعلم ا هـ . ثم أعلم أن الشرط وجود الفعل منه أعم من أن يكون مسحاً أو ضرباً أو غيره فقد قال في الخلاصة : ولو أدخل رأسه في موضع الغبار بنية التيمم يجوز، ولو انهدم الحائط وظهر الغبار فحرك رأسه ونوى التيمم جاز والشرط وجود الفعل منه ا هـ . وهذا يعين أن هذه الفروع مبنية على قول من أخرج الضربة من مسمى التيمم، وأما من أدخلها فلا يمكنه القول بها فيما نقلناه عن الخلاصة إذا ليس فيها ضرب أصلاً لا على الأرض ولا على العضو إلا أن يقال : مراده بالضرب الفعل منه أعم من كونه ضرباً أو غيره وهو بعيد كما لا يخفى وتظهر ثمرة الخلاف أيضاً فيما إذا نوى بعد الضرب فمن جعله ركناً لم يعتبر النية بعده، ومن لم يجعله ركناً اعتبرها بعده. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي الخلاصة : ولو شلت كلا يديه يمسح وجهه وذراعيه على الحائط ا هـ. وقد قدمنا أنه لو أمر غيره بأن ييممه جاز بشرط أن ينوي الآمر ، فلو ضرب المأمور يده على الأرض بعدنية الأمر ثم أحدث الآمر قال في التوشيح : ينبغي أن يبطل بحدث الآمر على قول أبي شجاع وظاهره أنه لا يبطل بحدث المأمور لما أن المأمور آلة وضربه ضرب للآمر فالعبرة للأمر ولهذا اشترطنا نيته لا نية المأمور
In the book there is nothing else. He said, the Exalted, 'So perform tayammum with clean earth and wipe your faces and your hands' [An-Nisa 4:43]. And his saying (peace be upon him) 'Tayammum is two strikes' is interpreted either as meaning the general sense of the two wipes as we said, or that it was brought out in the dominant manner. And Allah the Exalted knows best. Then know that the condition is the existence of an action from him, whether it be wiping, striking, or other. For it is stated in al-Khulasah: If he inserts his head into a place of dust with the intention of tayammum, it is permissible. If the wall collapses and dust appears and he moves his head and intends tayammum, it is permissible. The condition is the existence of an action from him. This determines that these branches are based on the opinion of the one who excludes the strike from the definition of tayammum. As for the one who includes it, he cannot say so regarding what we have transmitted from al-Khulasah, since there is no strike at all in it, neither on the ground nor on the limb, unless it is said: He means by strike the action from him, whether it is a strike or other, which is far-fetched as is not hidden. The fruit of the difference also appears in the case when he intends after the strike: the one who makes it a pillar does not consider the intention after it, and the one who does not make it a pillar considers it after it. This is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. In al-Khulasah: If both hands are paralyzed, he wipes his face and forearms on the wall. And we have already stated that if he orders someone else to perform tayammum for him, it is permissible on condition that the one ordering intends. So if the agent strikes his hand on the ground with the intention of the orderer, then the orderer breaks his wudu, in al-Tawshih it says: It should be invalidated by the event of the orderer according to Abu Shuja', and apparently it is not invalidated by the event of the agent because the agent is a tool and his strike is the strike of the orderer, so the consideration is for the orderer, and for this we stipulated his intention, not the intention of the agent.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran and hadith regarding the fundamental condition of tayammum. It begins by quoting the Quranic verse on tayammum and the hadith 'Tayammum is two strikes.' The author reconciles the apparent discrepancy between the verse (which mentions only wiping) and the hadith (which mentions two strikes) by offering two interpretations: either the hadith uses 'strike' in a broad sense to mean any action, or it describes the common practice. The core ruling is that the condition for tayammum is that the person performs some action, whether it is striking, wiping, or any other movement that produces dust. This is supported by examples from al-Khulasah: inserting the head into dust or shaking the head after a wall collapse. The text then explains that these examples are based on the view that the strike itself is not a pillar (rukn) of tayammum; rather, any action suffices. This leads to a practical difference (thamaratu al-khilaf): if the strike is considered a pillar, then intention (niyyah) must precede it, but if it is not, intention can come after. The passage also covers the case of a person with paralyzed hands wiping on a wall, and the ruling on a person appointing an agent to perform tayammum. In the agent case, the validity depends on the intention of the principal, not the agent, because the agent is merely a tool. The text cites al-Tawshih to clarify that invalidation (naqd) occurs by the principal's event, not the agent's. All these rulings derive from the same principle: the essential condition is the existence of an action from the person, not a specific form of striking.

Key Terms
ضربة (darba): A strike or tapping of the hands on the earth in tayammum.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarat al-khilaf): The practical consequence (fruit) of a juristic disagreement, here affecting the validity of intention after the strike.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the fundamental condition for the validity of tayammum?
A) Hitting both hands on the ground twice.
B) The existence of any action from the person, such as wiping, striking, or moving the head in dust.
C) Having the intention before any action.
D) Using only clean earth without any moisture.

Key Takeaway
In tayammum, the condition is any action producing dust; the strike is not a rukn, and the timing of intention depends on this dispute.

Method of Tayammum: Strikes, Wiping, and the Issue of Used Dust
Detailed description of tayammum's obligatory and recommended actions with scholarly debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi method of performing tayammum and explain the disagreement regarding the use of used dust (musta'mal).

Core Idea
Tayammum requires two distinct strikes: first for the face, second for the arms; the detailed method avoids using dust that has already wiped a limb.

In this lesson, we will walk through the exact method of tayammum as transmitted from the Hanafi masters. You will learn the two-strike procedure, the precise wiping sequence including the thumb, and the scholarly debate on whether dust becomes 'used' (musta'mal) like water. Understanding these details ensures your tayammum is valid and complete.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two strikes
The basic method consists of two strikes on pure earth: the first for wiping the face, the second for wiping the arms. This is the foundation.
The text quotes al-Muhit: first strike → wipe face; second strike → wipe hands and forearms up to elbows.
2
Describe the detailed wiping of the arms
Our scholars (مشايخنا) prescribe a specific sequence: using four fingers of the left hand to wipe the back of the right arm from fingertips to elbow, then the palm to wipe the inside to the wrist, then the thumb over the back of the right thumb, and then repeat for the left arm.
This method is الأحوط (more precautionary) to avoid using dust that has already been placed on a limb.
3
Analyze the musta'mal debate
Some argue that the dust applied to the hand becomes 'used' after first wiping, so a second strike is needed for the second limb. Others say dust does not become musta'mal like water because it remains on the limb; thus the same dust can suffice if the method allows.
The author notes a difference between dust and water: dust is not absorbed like water, so the issue is only in form, not reality.
4
Determine the correct hand placement for the strike
There is disagreement whether the strike is with the inner palms, outer palms, or both. The most correct view (الأصح) from Sharh al-Niqayah is that the strike is with both surfaces.
A conflicting transmission from Ibn Amir Hajj indicates striking with inner palms only. The author reconciles by noting the intended meaning of 'palm' may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : وكيفية التيمم أن يضرب يديه على الأرض ثم ينفضهما فيمسح بهما وجهه بحيث لا يبقى منه شيء وإن قل، ثم يضرب يديه ثانياً على الأرض ثم ينفضهما فيمسح بهما كفيه وذراعيه كليهما إلى المرفقين . اه. 6 وقال مشايخنا : يضرب يديه ثانياً ويمسح بأربع أصابع يده اليسرى ظاهر يده اليمنى من رؤوس الأصابع إلى المرفق ثم يمسح بكفه اليسرى باطن يده اليمنى إلى الرسغ ويمر باطن إبهامه اليسرى على ظاهر إبهامه اليمنى، ثم يفعل باليد اليسرى كذلك وهو الأحوط لأن فيه احترازاً عن استعمال المستعمل بالقدر الممكن فإن التراب الذي على يده يصير مستعملاً بالمسح

قوله قوله : (فيمسح بهما كفيه وذراعيه أي ويمر بباطن إبهامه اليسرى على ظاهر إبهامه اليمني . قال العارف في شرح الهدية وقال والدي رحمه الله بعد نقله هذه الكيفية : وهذه الصورة حكاية ابن عمر رضي الله تعالى عنهما تيمم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وكذا روى جابر أيضاً قوله : (فإن التراب الذي على يده يصير مستعملاً بالمسح فيه نظر لأنه إن استعمل بأول الوضع يلزم أن لا يجزىء في باقي العضو وألا يستعمل بأول الوضع كالماء لا يلزم ما ذكره وهو كذلك، يؤيده ما قاله العارف في شرح هدية ابن العماد عن جامع الفتاوى . وقيل : يمسح بجميع الكف والأصابع لأن التراب لا مستعملاً يصير في محله كالماء اهـ. ولذا عبر بعضهم في هذه الكيفية بقوله والأحسن إشارة إلى تجويز خلافه إلا أن يقال : المراد أنه يصير مستعملاً صورة لا حقيقة ولكن الفرق ظاهر بين هذا وبين قوله «حتى لو ضرب يديه مرة الخ» تأمل . قوله : (إذ لا جمع بينهما كما لا يخفى قال في النهر : وغير خاف أن

٢٥٥
حتى لو ضرب يديه مرة ومسح بهما وجهه وذراعيه لا يجوز ولا يجب مسح باطن الكف لأن ضربهما على الأرض يغني عنه. وفي شرح النقاية للشمني معزياً إلى الذخيرة: لم يرد نص هل الضربة بباطن الكفين أو بظاهرهما والأصح أنها بظاهرهما وباطنهما ا هـ. والمراد بالواو إذ لا جمع بينهما كما لا يخفى، وهذا النقل عن الذخيرة مخالف لما نقله عنها ابن أمير حاج في شرح منية المصلي ولفظة تنبيه في الذخيرة لم يذكر محمد أنه يضرب على الأرض ظاهر كفيه أو باطنهما وأشار إلى أنه يضرب باطنهما فإنه قال في الكتاب : لو ترك المسح على ظاهر كفيه لا يجوز إنما يكون تاركاً للمسح على ظاهر كفيه إذا ضرب باطن كفيه على الأرض ا هـ . ثم قال : قلت وبهذا يعلم أن المراد بالكف باطنها لا ظاهرها ا.هـ. وهكذا في التوشيح معزياً إلى الذخيرة إلا أنه أسطر ذكر ما في شرح النقاية من التصحيح وسنن التيمم سبعة : إقبال بعد اليدين بعد وضعهما على التراب وإدبار هما ونفضهما وتفريج الأصابع والتسمية في أوله والترتيب والموالاة. ذكر الأربعة الأول في المبتغى والباقية في المبسوط، وبعضهم أطلق على بعض هذه الاستحباب، وفي ظاهر الرواية ينفضهما مرة وعن أبي يوسف مرتين وهذا ليس كالزيلعي باختلاف لأن المقصود وهو تناثر التراب إن حصل بمرة اكتفى بها وإن لم يحصل ينفض مرتين. كذا في البدائع ولهذا قال في الهداية : ينفض يديه بقدر ما يتناثر التراب كيلا يصير جمهور مثلة ا هـ .
In al-Muhit: The method of tayammum is that he strikes his hands on the earth, then shakes them, then wipes his face with them so that nothing remains [unwiped] even if little, then he strikes his hands a second time on the earth, then shakes them, then wipes his hands and both forearms up to the elbows. End. And our scholars said: He strikes his hands a second time and wipes with four fingers of his left hand the back of his right hand from the tips of the fingers to the elbow, then wipes with his left palm the inside of his right hand to the wrist, and passes the inner part of his left thumb over the back of his right thumb, then does similarly with the left hand. This is the more precautionary because it avoids using used dust as much as possible, because the dust on his hand becomes used by wiping. His saying: He wipes with both hands his hands and forearms, meaning: he passes the inner part of his left thumb over the back of his right thumb. Al-Arif said in Sharh al-Hidayah: My father (may Allah have mercy on him) said after quoting this method: This form is the narration of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) of the tayammum of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and similarly Jabir also narrated. His saying: 'The dust on his hand becomes used by wiping' is debatable, because if it is used at the beginning of the placement, it would not suffice for the rest of the limb; but if it is not used at the beginning, like water, then what he mentioned does not apply. This is correct. This is supported by what al-Arif said in Sharh Hadiyyat Ibn al-Imad from Jami' al-Fatawa. And it is said: He wipes with the entire palm and fingers because dust does not become used in its place like water. Therefore, some express this method by saying 'and better', indicating permission of the opposite, unless it is said that the intended meaning is that it becomes used in form not reality. But the difference between this and his saying 'even if he strikes his hands once...' is apparent. His saying: 'since there is no combination between them as is not hidden.' He said in al-Nahr: It is not hidden that even if he strikes his hands once and wipes his face and forearms, it is not permissible, and wiping the inner palm is not necessary because striking them on the earth suffices for it. In Sharh al-Niqayah by al-Shumnni quoting al-Dhakhirah: There is no explicit text whether the strike is with the outer part of the palms or their inner parts, and the most correct is that it is with both their outer and inner parts. The conjunction 'waw' means there is no combination between them as is not hidden. This transmission from al-Dhakhirah contradicts what Ibn Amir Hajj transmitted from it in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. The wording 'tanbih' in al-Dhakhirah: Muhammad did not mention whether he strikes on the ground with the outer part of his hands or their inner parts, and he indicated that he strikes with their inner parts, for he said in the book: If he leaves wiping the back of his hands, it is not permissible; he only becomes one who left wiping the back of his hands if he struck the inner palms on the ground. Then he said: I say: By this it is known that the intended meaning of 'palm' is its inner part, not its outer. This is also in al-Tawshih quoting al-Dhakhirah, except that in a few lines it mentions what is in Sharh al-Niqayah of correction. The sunnahs of tayammum are seven: bringing the hands forward after placing them on the dust, bringing them back, shaking them, spreading the fingers, saying the basmalah at the beginning, order, and continuity. The first four are mentioned in al-Muntaha and the rest in al-Mabsut. Some labelled some of these as recommended. In the apparent transmission, he shakes them once, and from Abu Yusuf twice. This is not like al-Zayla'i's difference because the purpose, which is the scattering of dust, if achieved with one shake, it suffices, and if not, he shakes twice. This is in al-Bada'i', and therefore he said in al-Hidayah: He shakes his hands to the extent that the dust scatters so that it does not become...? (unclear)...
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the method (kayfiyyah) of tayammum and its sunnah acts. It begins by quoting the method from al-Muhit: two strikes on the earth, shaking the hands, then wiping the face (first strike) and then wiping the hands and forearms up to the elbows (second strike). Then it presents a more detailed method from مشايخنا (our scholars), which specifies wiping with four fingers on the back of the right arm and the inner palm, with a particular sequence to avoid using dust that has already been used on another limb (استعمال المستعمل). The text then addresses a potential issue: whether the dust becomes 'used' (musta'mal) like water. The author notes that some scholars argue that dust does not become used because it remains on the limb, unlike water which is absorbed. This leads to a difference in practice: some prefer the detailed method (الأحوط) while others simply wipe with the whole palm. The text then discusses the correct hand placement during the strike: should one strike with the inner palms or the outer? It transmits a disagreement from al-Dhakhirah, with the most correct view being that one strikes with both surfaces. However, a conflicting transmission from Ibn Amir Hajj indicates that the ruling is to strike with the inner palms alone. The author attempts to reconcile these. After this, the seven sunnah acts of tayammum are listed: 1) bringing the hands forward after placing them on the dust, 2) bringing them back, 3) shaking them, 4) spreading the fingers, 5) saying Basmalah, 6) order, 7) continuity (muwalat). The text also mentions that some consider these as recommended (mustahabb) and that there is a difference of opinion on the number of shakes: once or twice, depending on need. This passage covers the practical execution of tayammum in detail, reflecting the Hanafi school's precision in method.

Key Terms
مستعمل (musta'mal): Dust that has already been wiped on one limb, and the debate is whether it is ineffective for a second limb.
الضربة (darbah): The act of striking the hands on the earth; tayammum requires two strikes.
الأحوط (al-ahwat): The more precautionary method, recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) With the outer part of the palms only.
B) With the inner part of the palms only.
C) With both the outer and inner parts of the palms.
D) With the fingers spread without touching the palm.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum requires two strikes; the dust does not become used (musta'mal) like water, so the basic method is valid, though a detailed precautionary method is recommended.

The Sunnah Acts of Tayammum
Listing and explanation of the sunnah acts of tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven sunnah acts of tayammum and identify the difference of opinion regarding the number of times to shake the hands.

Core Idea
Seven sunnah acts enhance tayammum; the number of shakes depends on achieving dust scatter.

After learning the obligatory method of tayammum, this lesson covers the recommended (sunnah) acts that perfect the practice. The Hanafi school enumerates seven specific sunnahs, including bringing the hands forward and back, shaking, spreading fingers, saying Basmalah, maintaining order, and continuity. We will also examine a minor difference on whether to shake once or twice.

Guided Path
1
List the seven sunnah acts
The text enumerates: 1) إقبال (bringing hands forward after placing them on dust), 2) إدبار (bringing them back), 3) نفض (shaking off dust), 4) تفريج الأصابع (spreading fingers), 5) التسمية (saying Basmalah), 6) الترتيب (order), 7) الموالاة (continuity).
The first four are from al-Muntaha; the rest from al-Mabsut.
2
Understand the purpose of shaking
Shaking removes excess dust so that it does not clump and cause unsightliness (مثلة). The extent of shaking is to scatter the dust.
The text quotes al-Hidayah: 'He shakes his hands to the extent that the dust scatters.'
3
Analyze the dispute on number of shakes
In ظاهر الرواية (apparent transmission), he shakes once. From Abu Yusuf, he shakes twice. The difference is not like other disagreements because it depends on the need: if one shake suffices to scatter dust, it is enough; otherwise, two are required.
This is practical difference, not rigid rule.

كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم
٢٥٥
حتى لو ضرب يديه مرة ومسح بهما وجهه وذراعيه لا يجوز ولا يجب مسح باطن الكف لأن ضربهما على الأرض يغني عنه. وفي شرح النقاية للشمني معزياً إلى الذخيرة: لم يرد نص هل الضربة بباطن الكفين أو بظاهرهما والأصح أنها بظاهرهما وباطنهما ا هـ. والمراد بالواو إذ لا جمع بينهما كما لا يخفى، وهذا النقل عن الذخيرة مخالف لما نقله عنها ابن أمير حاج في شرح منية المصلي ولفظة تنبيه في الذخيرة لم يذكر محمد أنه يضرب على الأرض ظاهر كفيه أو باطنهما وأشار إلى أنه يضرب باطنهما فإنه قال في الكتاب : لو ترك المسح على ظاهر كفيه لا يجوز إنما يكون تاركاً للمسح على ظاهر كفيه إذا ضرب باطن كفيه على الأرض ا هـ . ثم قال : قلت وبهذا يعلم أن المراد بالكف باطنها لا ظاهرها ا.هـ. وهكذا في التوشيح معزياً إلى الذخيرة إلا أنه أسطر ذكر ما في شرح النقاية من التصحيح وسنن التيمم سبعة : إقبال بعد اليدين بعد وضعهما على التراب وإدبار هما ونفضهما وتفريج الأصابع والتسمية في أوله والترتيب والموالاة. ذكر الأربعة الأول في المبتغى والباقية في المبسوط، وبعضهم أطلق على بعض هذه الاستحباب، وفي ظاهر الرواية ينفضهما مرة وعن أبي يوسف مرتين وهذا ليس كالزيلعي باختلاف لأن المقصود وهو تناثر التراب إن حصل بمرة اكتفى بها وإن لم يحصل ينفض مرتين. كذا في البدائع ولهذا قال في الهداية : ينفض يديه بقدر ما يتناثر التراب كيلا يصير جمهور مثلة ا هـ .
In al-Muhit: The method of tayammum is that he strikes his hands on the earth, then shakes them, then wipes his face with them so that nothing remains [unwiped] even if little, then he strikes his hands a second time on the earth, then shakes them, then wipes his hands and both forearms up to the elbows. End. And our scholars said: He strikes his hands a second time and wipes with four fingers of his left hand the back of his right hand from the tips of the fingers to the elbow, then wipes with his left palm the inside of his right hand to the wrist, and passes the inner part of his left thumb over the back of his right thumb, then does similarly with the left hand. This is the more precautionary because it avoids using used dust as much as possible, because the dust on his hand becomes used by wiping. His saying: He wipes with both hands his hands and forearms, meaning: he passes the inner part of his left thumb over the back of his right thumb. Al-Arif said in Sharh al-Hidayah: My father (may Allah have mercy on him) said after quoting this method: This form is the narration of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) of the tayammum of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and similarly Jabir also narrated. His saying: 'The dust on his hand becomes used by wiping' is debatable, because if it is used at the beginning of the placement, it would not suffice for the rest of the limb; but if it is not used at the beginning, like water, then what he mentioned does not apply. This is correct. This is supported by what al-Arif said in Sharh Hadiyyat Ibn al-Imad from Jami' al-Fatawa. And it is said: He wipes with the entire palm and fingers because dust does not become used in its place like water. Therefore, some express this method by saying 'and better', indicating permission of the opposite, unless it is said that the intended meaning is that it becomes used in form not reality. But the difference between this and his saying 'even if he strikes his hands once...' is apparent. His saying: 'since there is no combination between them as is not hidden.' He said in al-Nahr: It is not hidden that even if he strikes his hands once and wipes his face and forearms, it is not permissible, and wiping the inner palm is not necessary because striking them on the earth suffices for it. In Sharh al-Niqayah by al-Shumnni quoting al-Dhakhirah: There is no explicit text whether the strike is with the outer part of the palms or their inner parts, and the most correct is that it is with both their outer and inner parts. The conjunction 'waw' means there is no combination between them as is not hidden. This transmission from al-Dhakhirah contradicts what Ibn Amir Hajj transmitted from it in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. The wording 'tanbih' in al-Dhakhirah: Muhammad did not mention whether he strikes on the ground with the outer part of his hands or their inner parts, and he indicated that he strikes with their inner parts, for he said in the book: If he leaves wiping the back of his hands, it is not permissible; he only becomes one who left wiping the back of his hands if he struck the inner palms on the ground. Then he said: I say: By this it is known that the intended meaning of 'palm' is its inner part, not its outer. This is also in al-Tawshih quoting al-Dhakhirah, except that in a few lines it mentions what is in Sharh al-Niqayah of correction. The sunnahs of tayammum are seven: bringing the hands forward after placing them on the dust, bringing them back, shaking them, spreading the fingers, saying the basmalah at the beginning, order, and continuity. The first four are mentioned in al-Muntaha and the rest in al-Mabsut. Some labelled some of these as recommended. In the apparent transmission, he shakes them once, and from Abu Yusuf twice. This is not like al-Zayla'i's difference because the purpose, which is the scattering of dust, if achieved with one shake, it suffices, and if not, he shakes twice. This is in al-Bada'i', and therefore he said in al-Hidayah: He shakes his hands to the extent that the dust scatters so that it does not become...? (unclear)...
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the method (kayfiyyah) of tayammum and its sunnah acts. It begins by quoting the method from al-Muhit: two strikes on the earth, shaking the hands, then wiping the face (first strike) and then wiping the hands and forearms up to the elbows (second strike). Then it presents a more detailed method from مشايخنا (our scholars), which specifies wiping with four fingers on the back of the right arm and the inner palm, with a particular sequence to avoid using dust that has already been used on another limb (استعمال المستعمل). The text then addresses a potential issue: whether the dust becomes 'used' (musta'mal) like water. The author notes that some scholars argue that dust does not become used because it remains on the limb, unlike water which is absorbed. This leads to a difference in practice: some prefer the detailed method (الأحوط) while others simply wipe with the whole palm. The text then discusses the correct hand placement during the strike: should one strike with the inner palms or the outer? It transmits a disagreement from al-Dhakhirah, with the most correct view being that one strikes with both surfaces. However, a conflicting transmission from Ibn Amir Hajj indicates that the ruling is to strike with the inner palms alone. The author attempts to reconcile these. After this, the seven sunnah acts of tayammum are listed: 1) bringing the hands forward after placing them on the dust, 2) bringing them back, 3) shaking them, 4) spreading the fingers, 5) saying Basmalah, 6) order, 7) continuity (muwalat). The text also mentions that some consider these as recommended (mustahabb) and that there is a difference of opinion on the number of shakes: once or twice, depending on need. This passage covers the practical execution of tayammum in detail, reflecting the Hanafi school's precision in method.

Key Terms
إقبال (iqbal): Bringing the hands forward after placing them on the earth.
إدبار (idbar): Bringing the hands back after forward motion.
نفض (nafd): Shaking off dust from the hands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the purpose of shaking the hands during tayammum?
A) To clean the hands completely.
B) To remove excess dust so it does not clump.
C) To signify the end of the act.
D) To count the number of strikes.

Key Takeaway
Seven sunnah acts recommend but not obligate specific gestures; the number of shakes is flexible based on achieving dust scatter.

Taharah — Purification

Tayammum for the Junub: The Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute with proofs from hadith and Quranic interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tayammum for a person in major impurity (junub) and explain the inter-madhhab dispute over the interpretation of the Quranic verse 'aw lamastum al-nisa'.

Core Idea
Tayammum is valid for all states of impurity, including major impurity, based on authentic hadith and the correct interpretation of the Quran.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that a person in a state of major impurity (junub) may perform tayammum when water is absent. We will explore the Quranic verse and hadith evidence that support this, and see how the Hanafis differ from some early scholars who restricted tayammum to minor impurity. Understanding this dispute helps clarify the scope of tayammum in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: tayammum is valid for the junub, the menstruating woman, and the woman with postpartum bleeding, just as for those in minor impurity.
This is the majority view adopted by the Hanafis.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
Recognize that early scholars like Umar and Ibn Mas'ud prohibited tayammum for the junub, interpreting the Quranic verse 'aw lamastum al-nisa' literally as physical touch.
Their view limits tayammum to cases of minor impurity or simple touch.
3
Examine the Hanafi proofs from hadith
Study the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn and Ammar, where the Prophet explicitly ordered tayammum for a junub man. These are authentic (ahad) but clear in command.
The Prophet said: 'عليك بالصعيد' (use the clean earth).
4
Analyze the dispute over the Quranic verse
Understand that the verse 'aw lamastum al-nisa' is ambiguous. The Hanafis, following Ali, Ibn Abbas, and Aisha, interpret it as sexual intercourse, supported by the context of the verse mentioning impurity after sleep.
The majority of scholars (jumhur) adopt this interpretation.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If one follows the minority view, a junub without water cannot pray and must wait; under the Hanafi view, he can pray with tayammum.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (the operative ruling for fatwa).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو جنباً أو حائضاً) يعني يتيمم الجنب والمحدث والحائض والنفساء وهو قول العلماء للأحاديث الواردة، منها ما رواه البخاري ومسلم من حديث عمران بن الحصين إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم رأى رجلاً معتزلاً لم يصل مع القوم فقال : يا فلان ما منعك أن تصلي مع القوم ؟ فقال : يا رسول الله أصابتني جنابة ولا ماء فقال : عليك بالصعيد. ومنها حديث عمار أن النبي الله و أمره بالتيمم وهو جنب رواه الأئمة الستة. وأما الآية وهي قوله تعالى أو لامستم النساء﴾ [النساء : ٤٣] فقد اختلف فيها فذهب عمر وابن مسعود وابن إلى حملها على المس باليد فمنعوا التيمم للجنب، وذهب علي وابن عباس وعائشة إلى أنها محمولة على الجماع فجوزوه للجنب وبه أخذ أصحابنا وجهور العلماء ترجيحاً لسياق الآية
عمر
الجواز حاصل بأيهما كان نعم الضرب بالباطن سنة . قوله : (وهذا النقل عن الذخيرة الخ) أقول : راجعت الذخيرة فرأيته ذكر العبارتين فإنه بعد ما ذكر العبارة التي نقلها ابن أمير حاج قال بعد أسطر والأصح أنه يضرب بباطن كفه وظاهره على الأرض، وهذا يصير رواية أخرى بخلاف ما أشار إليه محمد. اهـ ما رأيته في الذخيرة أقول: وهذا يعين أن المراد بالواو حقيقتها تأمل. قوله : وسنن التيمم سبعة الخ) زاد العارف في شرح الهداية ثلاثة أخرى وهي التيامن كما في جامع الفتاوى والمجتبي وخصوص الضرب على الصعيد لموافقة الحديث. قال في الخانية : والضرب أولى ليدخل التراب في أثناء الأصابع. وأن يكون بالكيفية المخصوصة وهي المتقدمة على الخلاف فيها فهي
His saying (and if he is junub or menstruating) means: the junub, the one in minor impurity, the menstruating woman, and the woman with postpartum bleeding all perform tayammum. This is the statement of the scholars due to the reported hadith. Among them is what Bukhari and Muslim narrated from the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saw a man staying apart who did not pray with the people and said: 'O so-and-so, what prevented you from praying with the people?' He said: 'O Messenger of Allah, I had a seminal emission and there is no water.' He said: 'Use the clean earth.' Among them is the hadith of Ammar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered him to perform tayammum while he was junub, narrated by the six leading scholars. As for the verse, which is His saying 'or you have touched women' [An-Nisa 4:43], there is a difference of opinion: Umar, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn [Umar?] went to interpret it as touching with the hand, so they prohibited tayammum for the junub. Ali, Ibn Abbas, and Aisha went to interpret it as sexual intercourse, so they permitted tayammum for the junub. Our companions adopted this, and the majority of scholars, preferring the context of the verse. Permission is obtained regardless of which interpretation, but striking with the inner palm is sunnah. His saying: (And this transmission from al-Dhakhirah... etc.) I say: I referred to al-Dhakhirah and saw that it mentioned both statements, for after mentioning the statement transmitted by Ibn Amir Hajj, it said after a few lines: 'The most correct is that he strikes with the inner part of his palm and its outer part on the ground, and this becomes another narration contrary to what Muhammad indicated.' This is what I saw in al-Dhakhirah. I say: This determines that the intended meaning of the conjunction (waw) is its literal meaning. His saying: 'The sunnan of tayammum are seven etc.' Al-Arif added three more in Sharh al-Hidayah: using the right side as in Jami' al-Fatawa and al-Mujtaba, and specifically striking on the earth to conform to the hadith. He said in al-Khaniyah: Striking is better so that dust enters between the fingers. And that it should be with the specific method which is previously mentioned, regarding which there is a difference.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the permissibility of tayammum for a person in a state of major impurity (janabah). The matn states that tayammum is valid for the junub, the one in minor impurity, the menstruating woman, and the woman in postpartum bleeding. The commentary provides proofs from hadith: the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn where the Prophet directed a junub man to use earth, and the hadith of Ammar. It then addresses the Quranic verse 'or you have touched women' (أو لامستم النساء) which some early scholars like Umar and Ibn Mas'ud interpreted as physical touch (thus limiting tayammum to when water is absent for those in minor impurity), while others like Ali and Ibn Abbas interpreted it as sexual intercourse (thus allowing tayammum for the junub). The Hanafis adopt the latter interpretation, supported by the majority of scholars and the context of the verse. This is the relied-upon position. The passage then digresses into a comment about the al-Dhakhirah transmission regarding the hand strike, and then adds three additional sunnan acts mentioned by al-Arif: preferring the right side, striking specifically on the earth, and the specific method. The key point is that tayammum is valid for all states of impurity, regardless of the interpretation of the verse.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity due to sexual intercourse or seminal emission.
لامستم (lamastum): The Quranic word 'touched' which is subject to interpretation: either physical touch or sexual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the opposing view to the Hanafi position on tayammum for the junub?
A) Tayammum is valid for the junub only if he is traveling.
B) Tayammum is not valid for the junub because the verse 'lamastum' means physical touch.
C) Tayammum is valid for the junub only if he intends multiple prayers.
D) Tayammum is invalid for all states of impurity.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, tayammum is valid for all states of impurity, including major impurity (janabah), based on authentic hadith and the interpretation of the Quranic verse 'aw lamastum al-nisa' as sexual intercourse.

Taharah — Purification

The Sunnah Acts of Tayammum and the Method of Striking
Ruling statement with additional sunnah details and a transmission clarification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah acts of tayammum and explain the recommended method of striking the earth.

Core Idea
Tayammum has specific sunnah acts that perfect the purification, including striking with both palms and using the right side first.

In addition to the validity of tayammum for all states of impurity, the Hanafi school details recommended (sunnah) acts that enhance the ritual. This lesson covers the seven sunnah acts mentioned in the matn, plus three additional ones noted by later scholars, and clarifies the proper method of striking the earth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven sunnah acts of tayammum from the matn
The matn mentions seven sunnah acts, but the passage only lists three: using the right side first, striking specifically on the earth, and the specific method. Refer to the full list from other sources? Actually, the passage says 'وسنن التيمم سبعة' but then only adds three from al-Arif. So the seven are assumed known. We will focus on what is given.
The original seven sunnah are: 1) reciting bismillah, 2) using both hands, 3) orienting towards qibla, etc. But here only three additional ones are mentioned.
2
Understand the dispute about the method of striking
There is a transmission from al-Dhakhirah about whether to strike with the inner palm, outer palm, or both. The most correct (asahh) is to strike with both the inner and outer palm on the ground.
This is a refinement of the sunnah method.
3
Note the additional sunnah acts from al-Arif
Al-Arif adds: using the right side (tayammun), striking specifically on the earth (to ensure dust), and performing the striking in the specific manner (inner and outer palm).
These are considered mustahabb (recommended) but not obligatory.
4
Apply the sunnah acts in practice
When performing tayammum, one should strive to incorporate these sunnah details to attain complete sunnah reward.
Missing a sunnah does not invalidate tayammum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو جنباً أو حائضاً) يعني يتيمم الجنب والمحدث والحائض والنفساء وهو قول العلماء للأحاديث الواردة، منها ما رواه البخاري ومسلم من حديث عمران بن الحصين إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم رأى رجلاً معتزلاً لم يصل مع القوم فقال : يا فلان ما منعك أن تصلي مع القوم ؟ فقال : يا رسول الله أصابتني جنابة ولا ماء فقال : عليك بالصعيد. ومنها حديث عمار أن النبي الله و أمره بالتيمم وهو جنب رواه الأئمة الستة. وأما الآية وهي قوله تعالى أو لامستم النساء﴾ [النساء : ٤٣] فقد اختلف فيها فذهب عمر وابن مسعود وابن إلى حملها على المس باليد فمنعوا التيمم للجنب، وذهب علي وابن عباس وعائشة إلى أنها محمولة على الجماع فجوزوه للجنب وبه أخذ أصحابنا وجهور العلماء ترجيحاً لسياق الآية

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the permissibility of tayammum for a person in a state of major impurity (janabah). The matn states that tayammum is valid for the junub, the one in minor impurity, the menstruating woman, and the woman in postpartum bleeding. Key Terms
ضرب (darb): The act of striking or placing the palms on the earth during tayammum.
باطن الكف (batin al-kaff): The inner part (palm) of the hand.
ظاهر الكف (zahir al-kaff): The outer part (back) of the hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the most correct (asahh) method of striking the earth for tayammum according to the Dhakhirah transmission?
A) Striking with the inner palm only.
B) Striking with the outer palm only.
C) Striking with both inner and outer palm.
D) Striking with the side of the hand.

Key Takeaway
The ideal tayammum includes striking the earth with both inner and outer palms, starting with the right side, and ensuring dust enters between the fingers, but missing these sunnah acts does not invalidate the purification.

intermediate
8 min
Manner of Striking and Sunan of Tayammum
Rules on striking and sunan of tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on striking the earth in tayammum, list the seven sunan, and explain the relied-upon practice regarding shaking hands.

Core Idea
Strike with both inner and outer palms; the seven sunan complete tayammum, and one shake suffices if dust scatters.

Tayammum is a purification substitute with specific actions. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq refines the manner of striking the hands and enumerates the sunan that accompany the act. Understanding these details ensures that tayammum is performed in accordance with the Hanafi school's relied-upon practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being discussed and whether it is obligatory, sunnah, or optional. The text addresses striking the hands on earth and wiping the inner palm.
The ruling is that striking suffices for wiping the inner palm; wiping is not obligatory.
2
Analyze the dispute on striking method
Examine the conflicting reports on whether to strike with the inner palm only or both inner and outer palms. Note the reconciliation: 'both sides' is the soundest opinion, but the conjunction implies alternation.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi, resolved by al-ashah in favor of both sides.
3
List the seven sunan
Identify the seven recommended acts from the text: bringing hands forward after placing on dust, bringing back, shaking, separating fingers, basmalah, sequence, and continuity.
Some scholars consider these mustahabb; they enhance but do not invalidate tayammum.
4
Understand the ikhtilaf on shaking
Note that Zahir al-Riwayah prescribes one shake, while Abu Yusuf allows two. The decisive criterion is achieving dust scattering.
This is not a genuine contradiction but a difference in means to the same end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حتى لو ضرب يديه مرة ومسح بهما وجهه وذراعيه لا يجوز ولا يجب مسح باطن الكف لأن ضربهما على الأرض يغني عنه. وفي شرح النقاية للشمني معزياً إلى الذخيرة: لم يرد نص هل الضربة بباطن الكفين أو بظاهرهما والأصح أنها بظاهرهما وباطنهما ا هـ. والمراد بالواو إذ لا جمع بينهما كما لا يخفى، وهذا النقل عن الذخيرة مخالف لما نقله عنها ابن أمير حاج في شرح منية المصلي ولفظة تنبيه في الذخيرة لم يذكر محمد أنه يضرب على الأرض ظاهر كفيه أو باطنهما وأشار إلى أنه يضرب باطنهما فإنه قال في الكتاب : لو ترك المسح على ظاهر كفيه لا يجوز إنما يكون تاركاً للمسح على ظاهر كفيه إذا ضرب باطن كفيه على الأرض ا هـ . ثم قال : قلت وبهذا يعلم أن المراد بالكف باطنها لا ظاهرها ا.هـ. وهكذا في التوشيح معزياً إلى الذخيرة إلا أنه أسطر ذكر ما في شرح النقاية من التصحيح وسنن التيمم سبعة : إقبال بعد اليدين بعد وضعهما على التراب وإدبار هما ونفضهما وتفريج الأصابع والتسمية في أوله والترتيب والموالاة. ذكر الأربعة الأول في المبتغى والباقية في المبسوط، وبعضهم أطلق على بعض هذه الاستحباب، وفي ظاهر الرواية ينفضهما مرة وعن أبي يوسف مرتين وهذا ليس كالزيلعي باختلاف لأن المقصود وهو تناثر التراب إن حصل بمرة اكتفى بها وإن لم يحصل ينفض مرتين. كذا في البدائع ولهذا قال في الهداية : ينفض يديه بقدر ما يتناثر التراب كيلا يصير جمهور مثلة ا هـ .
Even if he strikes his hands once and wipes his face and forearms with them, it is not permissible, and wiping the inner palm is not obligatory because striking them on the earth suffices for it. And in Sharh al-Niqayah by al-Shumni, citing al-Dhakhira: no text has been transmitted whether the strike is with the inner palms or their outer sides, and the soundest opinion is that it is with both their outer and inner sides. The intended meaning of 'waw' is that there is no combination between them, as is not hidden. And this citation from al-Dhakhira contradicts what Ibn Amir Hajj cited from it in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, and the word 'tanbih' in al-Dhakhira: Muhammad did not mention whether he strikes the earth with the outer palms or the inner ones, and he indicated that he strikes with the inner ones, for he said in the book: 'If he leaves wiping the outer part of his palms, it is not permissible; he is only considered to have left wiping the outer part of his palms when he strikes the inner part of his palms on the earth.' Then he said: 'I say: By this it is known that the intended meaning of 'kaf' is its inner part, not its outer part.' Similarly in al-Tawshih, citing al-Dhakhira, except that he mentioned in a few lines what is in Sharh al-Niqayah of correction. And the sunan of tayammum are seven: bringing forward the hands after placing them on the dust, bringing them back, shaking them, separating the fingers, saying the basmalah at its beginning, sequence, and continuity. The first four are mentioned in al-Mubtagha, and the rest in al-Mabsut. Some scholars declared some of these as recommended. In the Zahir al-Riwayah, he shakes them once, and from Abu Yusuf, twice. This is not like the difference of al-Zayla'i because the intended purpose, which is the scattering of dust, if achieved with one shake, suffices; if not achieved, he shakes twice. Thus in al-Bada'i, and hence al-Hidayah said: 'He shakes his hands to the extent that the dust scatters, so that he does not become disfigured.'
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the manner of striking the hands in tayammum and the sunan associated with it. The author begins by stating a ruling: if one strikes once and wipes face and forearms, it is valid, but it is not obligatory to wipe the inner palm because striking already cleans it. Then a dispute is cited from al-Dhakhira: should the strike be with the outer or inner palm? The soundest opinion (al-ashah) is that it should be with both inner and outer sides, but the conjunction 'waw' here is not for combination; rather it means either. A contradiction is noted: Ibn Amir Hajj transmitted that Muhammad indicated striking with the inner palms only. The author reconciles by noting that the term 'kaf' in the primary texts refers to the inner palm. Then the seven sunan of tayammum are listed: bringing hands forward after placing them on the earth, bringing them back, shaking them, separating fingers, saying basmalah, sequence, and continuity (muwalat). Some scholars consider these as mustahabb. On shaking, the relied-upon transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) is once, but Abu Yusuf said twice; the actual requirement is to shake until dust falls. This is a Hanafi refinement: the act is sunnah with flexibility based on need.

Key Terms
الكف (al-kaf): The palm of the hand; in this context, the inner part of the hand used for striking.
السنة (al-sunnah): An act that is recommended and rewarded, but not obligatory; omitting it does not invalidate tayammum.
النفض (al-nafd): Shaking or dusting off the hands after striking the earth, to remove excess dust.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many sunan of tayammum are listed in this passage?
A) Five
B) Six
C) Seven
D) Eight

Key Takeaway
Strike the earth with both inner and outer palms, observe the seven sunan, and shake hands until dust scatters – one shake suffices if the purpose is achieved.

Tayammum for Junub and Ha'id: Verse Interpretation and Dispute
Ruling on tayammum for junub and ha'id with scriptural proofs and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits tayammum for junub and ha'id, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding the interpretation of 'lams'.

Core Idea
Tayammum for junub relies on interpreting Quranic 'lams' as intercourse—context, not touch.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a critical Quranic interpretation that underpins the Hanafi ruling on tayammum for major impurity. It establishes the proofs from hadith and then delves into the ikhtilaf with Imam al-Shafi'i, ultimately affirming the position. The lesson will walk through the textual reasoning and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school permits tayammum for junub, ha'id, and nufasa' based on hadith and Quranic context. Note that tayammum substitutes for both wudu and ghusl when water is absent or harmful.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i and some Companions (Umar, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Umar) interpreted 'lams' literally as touching by hand, leading to different rulings on wudu and tayammum.
Shafi'i also permits tayammum for junub but views it as a separate ruling not derived from the verse.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the literal interpretation: 'lams' means tactile contact; thus the verse only covers minor impurity. The hadith on tayammum for junub is accepted but seen as an exception.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine Hanafi contextual reasoning: since the verse already mentions minor hadath ('from the toilet'), 'lams' must refer to major hadath (janabah) to avoid redundancy. This is supported by the interpretation of Ali, Ibn Abbas, and Aisha.
This uses the principle of siyaq (context) and ilgha' al-takrar (eliminating redundancy).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: both schools allow tayammum for junub, but Shafi'i holds that any touching of a woman (even without desire) breaks wudu, while Hanafi restricts this to intercourse or direct contact with desire.
The disputed ruling on ha'id with less than ten days is resolved by preferring the permissive view based on consensus of early authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو جنباً أو حائضاً) يعني يتيمم الجنب والمحدث والحائض والنفساء وهو قول العلماء للأحاديث الواردة، منها ما رواه البخاري ومسلم من حديث عمران بن الحصين إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم رأى رجلاً معتزلاً لم يصل مع القوم فقال : يا فلان ما منعك أن تصلي مع القوم ؟ فقال : يا رسول الله أصابتني جنابة ولا ماء فقال : عليك بالصعيد. ومنها حديث عمار أن النبي الله و أمره بالتيمم وهو جنب رواه الأئمة الستة. وأما الآية وهي قوله تعالى أو لامستم النساء﴾ [النساء : ٤٣] فقد اختلف فيها فذهب عمر وابن مسعود وابن إلى حملها على المس باليد فمنعوا التيمم للجنب، وذهب علي وابن عباس وعائشة إلى أنها محمولة على الجماع فجوزوه للجنب وبه أخذ أصحابنا وجهور العلماء ترجيحاً لسياق الآية لأن الله تعالى بين حكم الحدث الأصغر والأكبر حال وجود الماء ثم نقل الحكم إلى التراب حال عدم الماء، وذكر الحدث الأصغر بقوله أو جاء أحد منكم من الغائط [النساء : ٤٣] فتعين حمل الملامسة على الجماع ليكون بياناً لحكم الحدثين عند وجوده، والشافعي حمل الآية على الجماع والمس باليد فقال بإباحته للجنب ونقض الوضوء بالمس باليد، والحيض والنفاس ملحقان بالجنابة لأنهما في معناهما هكذا في كثير من الكتب لكن في الفتاوى الظهيرية كما نقله مسكين من شرح الكنز والشمني في شرح النقاية تفصيل في الحائض وهي أنها إذا ظهرت لعشرة أيام يجوز لها التيمم، وإن طهرت لأقل لا يجوز إلا أن الشمني نقله عنها في تيممها لصلاة الجنازة والعيد والأول في مطلق التيمم. والذي يظهر أن هذا التفصيل غير صحيح بدليل ما اتفقوا على نقله في باب الحيض والرجعة أن الحائض إذا انقطع دمها لأقل من عشرة فتييمت عند عدم القدرة على الماء وصلت جاز للزوج وطؤها، وهل تنقطع الرجعة بمجرد التيمم أو لا بد من الصلاة به فيه خلاف، فهذا صريح في جواز التيمم لها. وممن صرح به القاضي الاسبيجابي في شرح مختصر الطحاوي ولفظه : الأصل أن المرأة إذا كانت أيامها دون العشرة فوقت اغتسالها من الحيض حتى إنها لا تخرج من الحيض ما لم تغتسل أو يمضي عليها أدنى وقت الصلاة إليها مع قدرة الاغتسال فيه، ولو تيممت وصلت خرجت من الحيض ،بالاتفاق ولو تيممت ولم تصل لا ينقطع حق الرجعة في قولهما خلافاً لمحمد ،وزفر، وأجمعوا أنها لا تتزوج حتى تصلي بذلك التيمم إلى آخر ما ذكر من الفروع، لكن صحح شمس الأئمة السرخسي في مبسوطه أنه لا يطؤها حتى تصلي به إجماعاً لأن محمداً إنما جعل التيمم كالاغتسال فيما هو مبني على الاحتياط وهو قطع الرجعة والاحتياط في الوطء تركه فليس التيمم فيه كالاغتسال كما لم يفعله في الحل للأزواج. وفي المحيط : جنب مر على مسجد فيه ماء يتيمم للدخول ولا يباح له إلا بالتيمم وإن كان فيه عين صغيرة ولا يستطيع الاعتراف منه لا يغتسل فيها ويتيمم لأن الاغتسال فيه يفسده ولا يخرج طاهراً فلا يكون مفيداً، ولو أصابته الجنابة في المسجد قيل لا يباح له الخروج من غير تيمم اعتباراً بالدخول وقيل يباح لأن في الخروج تنزيه المسجد عن النجاسة وفي الدخول تلويثه بها اهـ. وسيأتي في الحيض تمامه إن شاء الله تعالى .
His saying: (Even if junub or ha'id) means that the junub, the one with minor hadath, the menstruating woman, and the woman in postpartum bleeding perform tayammum. This is the statement of the scholars due to the hadiths that have come. Among them is what al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated from the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, saw a man isolating himself and not praying with the people. He said: 'O so-and-so, what prevented you from praying with the people?' He said: 'O Messenger of Allah, janabah befell me and there is no water.' He said: 'Use the pure earth (al-sa'id).' Among them is the hadith of Ammar that the Prophet, peace be upon him, commanded him to perform tayammum while he was junub, narrated by the six Imams. As for the verse, which is His saying 'or you have touched women' (4:43), there is a difference of opinion about it. Umar, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn [Umar] went to interpret it as touching by hand, so they forbade tayammum for the junub. Ali, Ibn Abbas, and Aisha went that it is interpreted as sexual intercourse, so they permitted tayammum for the junub, and our companions and the majority of scholars adopted this, giving preference to the context of the verse, because Allah explained the ruling of minor and major hadath in the presence of water, then transferred the ruling to earth in the absence of water, and mentioned minor hadath by His saying 'or one of you comes from the toilet' (4:43). So it is determined that 'touch' (mulasama) is interpreted as intercourse to be an explanation of the rulings of the two hadaths in the presence of water. Al-Shafi'i interpreted the verse as both intercourse and touching by hand, so he said tayammum is permissible for the junub and that wudu is broken by touching by hand. Menstruation and postpartum bleeding are annexed to janabah because they are similar in meaning. This is found in many books, but in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, as transmitted by Miskin from Sharh al-Kanz and al-Shumni in Sharh al-Niqayah, there is a detail concerning the menstruating woman: if she becomes pure within ten days, tayammum is permissible for her; if she becomes pure in less than ten days, it is not permissible, except that al-Shumni transmitted from it concerning her tayammum for the funeral prayer and Eid prayer, and the first is concerning absolute tayammum. And it appears that this detail is incorrect, as evidence of what they all agree on in the chapter of menstruation and revocability: if a menstruating woman's blood stops in less than ten days, she performs tayammum when unable to use water, prays, and it is permissible for her husband to have intercourse with her. Whether revocability expires with mere tayammum or requires prayer with it, there is a difference. This is explicit in permitting tayammum for her. Among those who stated it explicitly is al-Qadi al-Asbijabi in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, his wording: 'The principle is that if a woman's days are less than ten, then the time for her ghusl from menstruation is such that she does not exit menstruation until she performs ghusl or the minimum time for prayer passes while she is able to perform ghusl within it. If she performs tayammum and prays, she exits menstruation by agreement. If she performs tayammum but does not pray, the right of revocability does not expire according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), contrary to Muhammad and Zufar. And they unanimously agree that she cannot marry until she prays with that tayammum.' To the end of the branches mentioned. But Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi in his Mabsut corrected that he (the husband) should not have intercourse with her until she prays with it unanimously, because Muhammad only made tayammum like ghusl in matters built on precaution, which is cutting off revocability, and precaution in intercourse is to leave it. So tayammum is not like ghusl regarding it, just as he did not make it like ghusl in being permissible for husbands. And in al-Muhit: A junub passes by a mosque containing water; he performs tayammum for entry, and it is not permissible for him except with tayammum, even if it contains a small spring and he cannot perform ghusl from it, he does not perform ghusl in it and performs tayammum because ghusl in it would spoil it and he would not exit pure, so it is not beneficial. If janabah befalls him in the mosque, it is said that it is not permissible for him to exit without tayammum, analogizing to entry, and it is said it is permissible because in exiting there is purification of the mosque from impurity, while in entry there is soiling it. This is and the complete discussion on menstruation will come, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the ruling of tayammum for major impurity (junub) and menstruation. The author explains that tayammum is valid for both junub, ha'id, and nufasa' based on authoritative hadiths from Bukhari, Muslim, and the six major hadith collections. The key issue is the interpretation of the verse 'or you have touched women' (4:43). The Hanafi school, following Ali, Ibn Abbas, and Aisha, interprets 'touch' metaphorically as sexual intercourse, not literal touching, because the verse already mentions minor hadath (from toilet). This interpretation allows tayammum for junub. Al-Shafi'i, on the other hand, takes the literal meaning and also says that touching a woman breaks wudu. The Hanafis argue that the context (siyaq) of the verse, which sequentially treats minor and major hadath, necessitates that mulasama refers to intercourse to cover major hadath. The author then addresses a specific detail from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah that restricts tayammum for a menstruating woman whose purity period is less than ten days. He rejects this as incorrect, citing the consensus that such a woman can perform tayammum and pray, and her husband may have intercourse after her tayammum and prayer. He provides additional support from al-Qadi al-Asbijabi and al-Sarakhsi on the effects of tayammum on revocability. Finally, he relates a practical ruling from al-Muhit: a junub person passing by a mosque with little water may perform tayammum for entry, but if the water is in a small well, he should not perform ghusl there as it would spoil the water.

Key Terms
جنابة (janabah): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, typically due to sexual intercourse or seminal emission.
لمس (lams / mulasama): In this verse, interpreted by Hanafis as sexual intercourse (mujama'a), not literal touching.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, the Quranic phrase 'aw lamastumu al-nisa' in the tayammum verse refers to what?
A) Literal touching by hand
B) Sexual intercourse
C) Both A and B
D) Only minor hadath

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits tayammum for junub based on the Quranic context interpreting 'lams' as intercourse, supported by multiple hadiths and the majority of scholars.

Condition of Pure Earth for Tayammum
Requirement that the earth used for tayammum be pure (tahir).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of pure earth for tayammum, derive it from the Quranic verse (4:43), and apply it to determine the validity of tayammum on impure surfaces.

Core Idea
For tayammum, the earth must be pure (tahir); impurity invalidates it.

This lesson examines a key condition for the validity of tayammum: the earth used must be ritually pure (tahir). The Hanafi school, relying on the Quranic phrase 'sa'idan tayyiban' (pure earth), establishes that any material impurity (najasa) on the earth renders the tayammum invalid. Understanding this condition is essential for correctly performing tayammum in situations where water is unavailable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Recognize that this passage states 'purity of the earth is a condition (shart) for the validity of tayammum.'
The word 'bi-tahir' in the matn signals this condition.
2
Locate the Quranic evidence
Find the verse 'fa-tayammamu sa'idan tayyiban' (4:43) cited as the primary proof.
The verse is from Surah al-Nisa'.
3
Analyze the derivation
The adjective 'tayyib' (pure) qualifies the earth. An impure earth cannot be described as 'tayyib', so tayammum on it is invalid.
This is a direct linguistic implication (dalala) from the Quran.
4
Apply to a concrete example
Consider tayammum with dust from a najis garment – it is not permissible because the dust is impure.
The example is explicitly given in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بطاهر) متعلق بـ«يتيمم يعني يشترط لصحة التيمم طهارة الصعيد لقوله تعالى فتيمموا صعيداً طيباً [النساء : ٤٣] ولا طيب مع النجاسة حتى لو تيمم بغبار ثوب نجس لا يجوز. قوله : (والذي يظهر أن هذا التفصيل غير صحيح)
His saying: (with pure) is related to 'he performs tayammum', meaning that for the validity of tayammum, the purity of the earth is a condition, due to His saying: 'So perform tayammum with pure earth' (4:43), and there is no purity with impurity, so if he performs tayammum with dust from a najis garment, it is not permissible. His saying: (And it appears that this detail is incorrect.)
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a brief but important ruling from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on a condition of tayammum: the earth must be pure (tahir). The author comments on the word 'bi-tahir' from the matn, explaining that it is a condition (shart) for the validity of tayammum. He cites the Quranic verse 'fa-tayammamu sa'idan tayyiban' (4:43) as evidence, where 'tayyib' means pure. If the earth is najis, it cannot be called tayyib, so tayammum with it is invalid. A practical example: using dust from a garment that is ritually impure (najis) is not permissible. The additional line 'والذي يظهر أن هذا التفصيل غير صحيح' appears to be a return to the earlier discussion about ha'id, but it is included here. It does not affect the ruling on pure earth. The core ruling is clear: the earth must be free from material impurity (najasa). This is a condition based on the explicit text of the Quran.

Key Terms
صعيد (sa'id): The surface of the earth, including dust, sand, stone, or any substance on the ground that can be used for tayammum.
طيب (tayyib): Pure (tahir) and permissible; free from ritual impurity or filth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence for the condition that the earth used for tayammum must be pure?
A) A hadith from Bukhari
B) The Quranic phrase 'sa'idan tayyiban'
C) Consensus of the companions
D) Analogy to water

Key Takeaway
The earth used for tayammum must be free from impurity (najasa); if it is najis, the tayammum is invalid.

Tayammum for a Menstruating Woman: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Early Cessation of Blood
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum for hayd woman after early cessation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on tayammum for a menstruating woman whose blood stops before ten days, and evaluate the conflicting views within the school.

Core Idea
A menstruating woman may perform tayammum even if blood stops before ten days; the minority view restricting it is unsound.

This passage deals with a specific question: if a woman's menstrual bleeding ends before the full ten-day maximum, may she perform tayammum if water is unavailable? The author rejects a restrictive view from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya, citing consensus from the chapters on hayd and raj'a. The passage also explores a sub-dispute on whether tayammum alone severs the husband's right of return (raj'a) or requires actual prayer. By the end of this lesson, you will be able to navigate this dispute and apply the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine what exactly is being disputed: the permissibility of tayammum for a menstruating woman when her blood stops before a full ten-day cycle.
The default Hanafi position is that hayd lasts a minimum of 3 and maximum of 10 days.
2
Contrast the two intra-madhhab views
The author reports a restrictive view from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya that only permits tayammum if bleeding lasted a full ten days (or for janaza/Eid prayers). The majority view, which the author defends, allows tayammum regardless of the duration.
The restrictive view is a minority within the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the evidence for the majority view
The author cites a consensus from the chapters on hayd and raj'a: if a woman performs tayammum and prays when her blood stops before ten days, her husband may validly have intercourse. This proves the tayammum is valid.
The consensus is used as a dalil (evidence) for permissibility.
4
Analyze the sub-dispute on raj'a
The passage notes a disagreement on whether tayammum alone (without prayer) cuts the husband's right of return (raj'a). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, raj'a is not severed by tayammum alone; according to Muhammad and Zufar, it is. Al-Sarakhsi clarifies that caution requires prayer before intercourse.
This sub-dispute does not affect the validity of tayammum itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحيض والنفاس ملحقان بالجنابة لأنهما في معناهما هكذا في كثير من الكتب لكن في الفتاوى الظهيرية كما نقله مسكين من شرح الكنز والشمني في شرح النقاية تفصيل في الحائض وهي أنها إذا ظهرت لعشرة أيام يجوز لها التيمم، وإن طهرت لأقل لا يجوز إلا أن الشمني نقله عنها في تيممها لصلاة الجنازة والعيد والأول في مطلق التيمم. والذي يظهر أن هذا التفصيل غير صحيح بدليل ما اتفقوا على نقله في باب الحيض والرجعة أن الحائض إذا انقطع دمها لأقل من عشرة فتييمت عند عدم القدرة على الماء وصلت جاز للزوج وطؤها، وهل تنقطع الرجعة بمجرد التيمم أو لا بد من الصلاة به فيه خلاف، فهذا صريح في جواز التيمم لها. وممن صرح به القاضي الاسبيجابي في شرح مختصر الطحاوي ولفظه : الأصل أن المرأة إذا كانت أيامها دون العشرة فوقت اغتسالها من الحيض حتى إنها لا تخرج من الحيض ما لم تغتسل أو يمضي عليها أدنى وقت الصلاة إليها مع قدرة الاغتسال فيه، ولو تيممت وصلت خرجت من الحيض ،بالاتفاق ولو تيممت ولم تصل لا ينقطع حق الرجعة في قولهما خلافاً لمحمد ،وزفر، وأجمعوا أنها لا تتزوج حتى تصلي بذلك التيمم إلى آخر ما ذكر من الفروع، لكن صحح شمس الأئمة السرخسي في مبسوطه أنه لا يطؤها حتى تصلي به إجماعاً لأن محمداً إنما جعل التيمم كالاغتسال فيما هو مبني على الاحتياط وهو قطع الرجعة والاحتياط في الوطء تركه فليس التيمم فيه كالاغتسال كما لم يفعله في الحل للأزواج.
And menstruation and postpartum bleeding are annexed to janaba because they are in its meaning. This is the case in many books, but in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya, as reported by Miskin from Sharh al-Kanz and al-Shamni in Sharh al-Nuqaya, there is a detail regarding the menstruating woman: that if her bleeding appears for ten days, it is permissible for her to perform tayammum, but if it stops for less than ten days, it is not permissible. Except that al-Shamni reported from it (al-Zahiriyya) regarding her tayammum for janaza and 'id prayer, and the first (ruling) is for absolute tayammum. And what appears is that this detail is incorrect, based on what they have agreed upon in the chapter of hayd and raj'a: that a menstruating woman whose blood stops for less than ten days and she performs tayammum due to inability to use water and prays, it is permissible for her husband to have intercourse with her. And whether the raj'a is cut off by mere tayammum or must be by prayer with it, there is a difference. So this is explicit in the permissibility of tayammum for her. And among those who explicitly stated it is al-Qadi al-Isbijabi in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, and his words: The principle is that if a woman's days are less than ten, the time for her ghusl from hayd is established such that she does not leave hayd unless she performs ghusl or the minimal time for prayer passes upon her with ability to perform ghusl, and if she performs tayammum and prays, she leaves hayd by agreement, and if she performs tayammum but does not pray, the right of raj'a is not severed according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), contrary to Muhammad and Zufar, and they all agree that she does not marry until she prays with that tayammum, up to the end of the branches he mentioned. But Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi in his Mabsut confirmed that he (the husband) should not have intercourse with her until she prays with it, by consensus, because Muhammad only considered tayammum like ghusl in what is based on caution, which is the cutting of raj'a, and caution regarding intercourse is its avoidance, so tayammum is not like ghusl in it, just as it is not effective regarding permissibility to husbands.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a woman whose menstrual blood stops before ten days can perform tayammum. The author first reports a view from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya that distinguishes between bleeding for a full ten days (permitting tayammum) and less than ten (not permitting). The author rejects this distinction as unsound, citing consensus from the chapters on hayd and raj'a that a woman with less than ten days may perform tayammum if she cannot use water, and her husband may validly have intercourse. The real dispute, also noted, is whether the husband's right of return (raj'a) is cut off by tayammum alone or requires actual prayer. Al-Isbijabi is quoted: if she tayammums and prays, she leaves hayd unanimously; but if only tayammum without prayer, there is disagreement: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, raj'a is not cut; according to Muhammad and Zufar, it is cut. Al-Sarakhsi later clarified that the husband should not have intercourse until she prays, because Muhammad's equating tayammum with ghusl was only for caution in raj'a, not for intercourse. Thus the operative ruling allows tayammum for the woman, but caution is exercised regarding marital relations.

Key Terms
الحائض (al-ha'id): A woman experiencing menstruation (hayd), which is a state of legal impurity preventing prayer, fasting, and intercourse.
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution using earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
الرجعة (al-raj'a): The right of a husband to return to his wife during the waiting period ('idda) after a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when a menstruating woman's blood stops before ten days and she performs tayammum due to inability to use water?
A) Her tayammum is invalid and she must wait until ten days
B) Her tayammum is valid only for janaza and 'id prayers
C) Her tayammum is valid and she may pray; her husband may have intercourse after she prays
D) Her tayammum is valid but she must repeat wudu when water is found

Key Takeaway
A menstruating woman may perform tayammum once her blood stops, even before ten days, and her husband may resume intercourse after she prays.
