Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Condition of Purity for Tayammum Earth
Explaining the requirement of pure earth for tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the Hanafi school requires tayammum earth to be pure (tahir) and explain that earth once impure, even after drying, loses its purifying property (tahuriyyah) and cannot be used.

Core Idea
Impure earth, once dried, becomes pure in essence but loses its purifying property, invalidating tayammum.

This lesson examines the Quranic requirement of 'good earth' (sa'id tayyib) for tayammum and how the Hanafi school interprets the purity condition. We will see why even dried impurity prevents tayammum, and how the true position is that such earth is pure but not purifying, like used water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tayammum requires pure earth; if the earth is impure (najis), tayammum is invalid even if the impurity has dried and disappeared.
The impurity may be visible or not; the key is that the earth once contacted impurity.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse (4:43) commands 'tayammum with good (tayyib) earth'. 'Tayyib' includes purity; impurity contradicts it.
The dalil is Quranic (qati al-thubut, zanni al-dalala).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'tayyib' in Arabic implies purity. Any impurity negates the description 'tayyib', thus the earth is not permissible for tayammum.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some (including possibly other schools) hold that drying removes the impurity, making the earth pure for tayammum. The Hanafi position rejects this because the impurity is only reduced, not eliminated.
The Hanafi view distinguishes between purity (taharah) and purifying power (tahuriyyah).
5
Understand the analogy to used water
Used water (musta'mal) is pure but not purifying; similarly, earth that was impure and dried is pure but has lost its tahuriyyah, so tayammum is invalid.
This analogy clarifies why tayammum is not valid even though the earth may be considered pure for prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : جنب مر على مسجد فيه ماء يتيمم للدخول ولا يباح له إلا بالتيمم وإن كان فيه عين صغيرة ولا يستطيع الاعتراف منه لا يغتسل فيها ويتيمم لأن الاغتسال فيه يفسده ولا يخرج طاهراً فلا يكون مفيداً، ولو أصابته الجنابة في المسجد قيل لا يباح له الخروج من غير تيمم اعتباراً بالدخول وقيل يباح لأن في الخروج تنزيه المسجد عن النجاسة وفي الدخول تلويثه بها اهـ. وسيأتي في الحيض تمامه إن شاء الله تعالى . قوله : (بطاهر) متعلق بـ«يتيمم يعني يشترط لصحة التيمم طهارة الصعيد لقوله تعالى فتيمموا صعيداً طيباً [النساء : ٤٣] ولا طيب مع النجاسة حتى لو تيمم بغبار ثوب نجس لا يجوز إلا إذا وقع ذلك الغبار عليه بعد ما جف، ولا بد أن تكون طهارته مقطوعاً بها حتى لو تيمم بأرض قد أصابتها نجاسة فجفت وذهب أثرها لم يجز في ظاهر الرواية. والفرق بين التيمم منها وجواز الصلاة عليها أن الجفاف مقلل لا مستأصل وقليلها مانع في التيمم دون الصلاة، ويجوز أن يعتبر القليل مانعاً في شيء كقليلها في الماء مانع دون الثوب. كذا في البدائع وسيأتي تمامه في الأنجاس إن شاء الله تعالى. وظاهر كلامهم أن الأرض التي جفت نجسة في حق التيمم طاهرة في حق الصلاة والحق أنها طاهرة في حق الكل. وإنما منع التيمم منها لفقد الطهورية كالماء المستعمل طاهر غير طهور وكان ينبغي للمصنف أن يقول بمطهر ليخرج ما ذكرنا كما عبر به في منظومة ابن وهبان وللحديث الوارد من قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم جعلت لي الأرض مسجداً وطهوراً (۱) بناء على أن الطهور بمعنى المطهر وقد تقدم الكلام فيه . وفي المحيط والبدائع : ولو تيمم اثنان مكان واحد جاز لأنه لم يصر مستعملاً لأن التيمم إنما يتأدى بما التزق بيده لا بما فضل كالماء الفاضل في الإناء بعد وضوء الأول ا هـ . وهو يفيد تصور استعماله وقصره على صورة واحدة وهي أن يمسح الذراعين بالضربة التي مسح بها وجهه ليس غير .
And in al-Muhit: A junub passed by a mosque containing water; he performs tayammum for entry and it is not permitted for him except with tayammum. And if there is a small well and he cannot scoop from it, he does not bathe in it but performs tayammum because bathing in it would spoil it and he would not come out pure, so it is not beneficial. And if he falls into janaba inside the mosque, it is said: he is not permitted to exit without tayammum, by analogy with entry; and it is said: he is permitted because exiting purifies the mosque from impurity while entering pollutes it. End. And the full discussion on hayd will come, God willing. His words: (with pure) is attached to 'he performs tayammum', meaning that for the validity of tayammum, the purity of the earth is a condition, due to His saying: 'so perform tayammum with good earth' [4:43]. And there is no goodness with impurity. So if one performs tayammum with the dust of an impure garment, it is not valid unless that dust falls on him after it has dried. And its purity must be certain, so that if one performs tayammum on earth that had been struck by impurity and then dried and its trace disappeared, it is not valid in the apparent narration. The difference between performing tayammum on it and the permissibility of praying on it is that drying reduces but does not eliminate; a small amount of impurity prevents in tayammum but not in prayer, and it is permissible to consider a small amount as preventing in one thing, like a small amount of impurity in water prevents but not in clothes. So in al-Bada'i', and its full discussion will come in the chapter on impurities, God willing. The apparent meaning of their words is that the earth that dried is impure in respect to tayammum but pure in respect to prayer; but the truth is that it is pure in all respects, and tayammum is prevented from it due to the loss of purifying property (tahuriyyah), like used water which is pure but not purifying. The author should have said 'purifying' (mutahhir) to exclude what we mentioned, as expressed in the versification of Ibn Wahban, and due to the hadith 'The earth has been made for me a place of prayer and purification', based on 'tahur' meaning 'mutahhir'. And in al-Muhit and al-Bada'i': If two persons perform tayammum from one spot, it is valid because it does not become used; the tayammum is only performed by what sticks to his hand, not by what remains, like the excess water in the vessel after the first ablution. End. And this indicates the concept of its usage and restricts it to one image: that he wipes his arms with the same strike with which he wiped his face, and nothing else.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings. First, it discusses a junub who passes by a mosque with water: he must perform tayammum to enter; if there is a small well, he cannot bathe in it because it would spoil the water and he wouldn't become pure. If he becomes junub inside the mosque, there is a difference of opinion on whether he must perform tayammum before leaving. The author then focuses on the condition that the earth (sa'id) used for tayammum must be pure (tahir). The Quranic verse (4:43) requires 'good earth', and impurity negates goodness. Even if earth becomes dry after impurity, it is not valid for tayammum in the apparent narration, though praying on it is allowed. This is because drying reduces the impurity but does not remove it completely; a small amount still prevents in tayammum but not in prayer. The truth is that such earth is pure in itself, but it loses the property of being a purifier (tahuriyyah) due to the impurity having been there, similar to used water which is pure but not purifying. The author wishes the matn had said 'mutahhir' (purifying) instead of 'tahir' (pure). Finally, two people may perform tayammum from the same spot because the earth is not 'used up'; each only takes what sticks to his hand, not the remainder.

Key Terms
صعيد (sa'id): The surface of the earth; used as the medium for tayammum.
طهور (tahur): That which is pure and purifying; a substance that can remove legal impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the reason that tayammum on earth that was impure and then dried is invalid?
A) The earth remains impure.
B) The earth is pure but not purifying.
C) The earth is neither pure nor purifying.
D) The earth is impure but still purifying.

Key Takeaway
For tayammum, the earth must be both pure (tahir) and purifying (tahur); once impurity affects it, it loses the latter quality even if dried.

Taharah — Purification

Multiple Persons Using the Same Earth for Tayammum
Ruling on multiple persons using the same earth for tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that two or more persons can validly perform tayammum from the same spot of earth and explain the reasoning based on the nature of tayammum and analogy to water.

Core Idea
The earth for tayammum is not consumed; only what adheres to the hand is used, so the same spot remains purifying for others.

This lesson addresses a practical question in congregational settings: if one person performs tayammum on a patch of earth, can another use the same spot? The passage from al-Muhit and al-Bada'i' answers yes, drawing a clear analogy to the water remaining after wudu. Understanding this ruling prevents unnecessary repetition and reinforces the concept of 'use' in taharah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Two persons performing tayammum from the same spot – the ruling is that it is valid (ja'iz).
2
Understand the rationale
Tayammum is only performed by what sticks to the hand, not by the remainder. The earth is not 'used up' like water.
This contrasts with water, which becomes musta'mal (used) after touching a limb.
3
Reference the analogy
The excess water left in the vessel after the first wudu is still purifying (tahur). Similarly, the earth left after the first tayammum retains its purifying property.
The analogy is explicit in the text: 'ka al-ma' al-fadil fi al-inba' ba'd wudu' al-awwal'.
4
Note the limitation
The ruling is restricted to the case where the second person wipes his arms with the same strike used for the face – i.e., a single strike suffices for both face and arms.
This is the interpretation of the phrase 'wa qasrihi 'ala suratin wahidah'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If he becomes junub inside the mosque, there is a difference of opinion on whether he must perform tayammum before leaving. The author then focuses on the condition that the earth (sa'id) used for tayammum must be pure (tahir). The Quranic verse (4:43) requires 'good earth', and impurity negates goodness. Even if earth becomes dry after impurity, it is not valid for tayammum in the apparent narration, though praying on it is allowed. This is because drying reduces the impurity but does not remove it completely; a small amount still prevents in tayammum but not in prayer. The truth is that such earth is pure in itself, but it loses the property of being a purifier (tahuriyyah) due to the impurity having been there, similar to used water which is pure but not purifying. The author wishes the matn had said 'mutahhir' (purifying) instead of 'tahir' (pure). Finally, two people may perform tayammum from the same spot because the earth is not 'used up'; each only takes what sticks to his hand, not the remainder.

Key Terms
مستعمل (musta'mal): Used; refers to water or earth that has been employed for purification and thus loses its purifying property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it permissible for two persons to perform tayammum from the same spot of earth according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the first person's tayammum cleans the earth.
B) Because tayammum is only performed by what sticks to the hand, not by the remainder of the earth.
C) Because the earth is infinite and never depletes.
D) Because the second person can strike a different part of the same spot.

Key Takeaway
Multiple persons can use the same earth for tayammum because the earth is not 'used up'; only the dust that adheres to the hand is consumed, analogous to leftover water after wudu.

Definition of Earthly Substances Permissible for Tayammum
Defining what counts as 'from the earth' for valid tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which substances are permissible for tayammum based on the Hanafi definition of 'min jins al-ard' and explain the exclusion criteria.

Core Idea
Tayammum is valid only with substances naturally from the earth, not burned or melted.

This lesson unpacks a key condition for tayammum: the substance used must be 'from the kind of earth' (min jins al-ard). The author of al-Mustasfa provides a clear criterion: anything that burns to ash or melts under fire is excluded. We will walk through the logic, apply it to the extensive list given, and note differences with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the defining criterion
The condition 'min jins al-ard' is narrowed by two negative examples: substances that burn to ash (like wood) or that melt (like iron) are not from the earth. Everything else is considered from the earth.
This is a general rule; exceptions exist for minerals in their natural state.
2
Classify the listed substances
From the passage, separate the permissible items (stone, dust, sand, gypsum, etc.) from the impermissible items (wood, glass, frozen water, metals, pearl, flour, ash). Apply the 'burn or melt' test to each.
Pay special attention to tricky cases like glass (made from sand but melted) and pearl (animal origin).
3
Understand the mineral exception
Minerals (e.g., iron, copper) in their natural place (mine) are not themselves usable, but the dust upon them may be used for tayammum. This shows the focus is on the earthy component, not the mineral per se.
This nuance avoids contradiction: minerals are not 'min jins al-ard' as substances, but the dust covering them is.
4
Connect to worship validity
Using a correct substance makes tayammum valid (sahih); using an incorrect one invalidates tayammum and requires repeating with proper earth. This has direct impact on prayer acceptance.
If in doubt, one should find a clearly permissible substance.
5
Contrast with other schools
The Shafi'i school restricts permissible earth to pure soil (turāb), excluding stones and minerals. The Hanafi school, based on a broader interpretation of 'min jins al-ard', includes many mineral items.
The practical difference is especially relevant in regions with rocky or mineral-rich terrain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (من جنس الأرض) يعني يتيمم بما كان من جنس الأرض. قال المصنف في المستصفى : كل ما يحترق بالنار فيصير رماداً كالشجر أو ينطبع ويلين كالحديد فليس من جنس الأرض وما عدا ذلك فهو من جنس الأرض ا.هـ. فلا يجوز التيمم بالأشجار والزجاج المتخذ من الرمل وغيره والماء المنجمد والمعادن إلا أن تكون في محالها، فيجوز للتراب الذي عليها لا بها نفسها، واللؤلؤ وإن كان مسحوقاً لأنه متولد من حيوان في البحر، والدقيق والرماد، ويجوز بالحجر والتراب والرمل والمسبخة المنعقدة من الأرض دون الماء، والجص والنورة والكحل والزرنيخ والمغرة والكبيرت والفيروزج والعقيق والبلخش والزمرد والزبرجد. وفي
His words: (from the kind of earth) means that one performs tayammum with what is from the kind of earth. The author said in al-Mustasfa: Everything that burns by fire and becomes ash, like wood, or that melts and softens, like iron, is not from the kind of earth; everything other than that is from the kind of earth. End. So it is not permissible to perform tayammum with trees, glass made from sand and other things, frozen water, and minerals unless they are in their places; then it is permissible for the dust that is on them, not for the minerals themselves. And pearl, even if powdered, because it is generated from a sea animal, and flour, and ash. And it is permissible with stone, dust, sand, and salt-encrusted earth (sabbakha) that originates from land without water, and gypsum, lime, kohl, arsenic, ochre, sulphur, turquoise, agate, balakhsh, emerald, and peridot. And in

Commentary
This passage defines the condition 'min jins al-ard' (from the kind of earth) for tayammum. The author in al-Mustasfa sets criteria: anything that burns to ash (like wood) or melts (like iron) is not from the earth; all else is. Thus, tayammum is invalid with wood, glass (even if made from sand), frozen water, and metals. However, if minerals are in their natural state (in mines), the dust on them can be used. Pearls, even powdered, are excluded because they come from sea animals. Flour and ash are also excluded. Permissible substances include stone, dust, sand, salt-encrusted earth (sabbakha) from land, gypsum, lime, kohl, arsenic, ochre, sulphur, turquoise, agate, balakhsh, emerald, and peridot. This list is extensive; the key is that the substance must be naturally occurring from the earth and not transformed by fire or melting. The text ends with 'and in', likely continuing with more substances on the next page.

Key Terms
من جنس الأرض (min jins al-ard): Substances that originate from the earth and are not transformed by fire or melting; includes dust, stone, and certain minerals.
المستصفى (al-Mustasfa): A work by the author (maybe al-Kashghari) cited for the definition of 'min jins al-ard'.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is valid only with substances that are naturally from the earth and not altered by fire or melting.

Taharah — Purification

Purity Requirement for Earth in Tayammum
Ruling with proof on purity for tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for tayammum on earth that was impure and dried, explain the distinction between purity for tayammum and for prayer, and identify the dalil and its wajh al-dalalah.

Core Idea
Earth must be both pure and purifying (tahur) for tayammum; drying does not restore purifying quality.

This passage tackles a subtle issue in tayammum: what if the earth was contaminated by impurity, then dried so that no trace remains? Is tayammum valid? The author clarifies that such earth is pure (tahir) for prayer but not purifying (tahur) for tayammum, drawing an analogy to used water. The ruling is established through the hadith 'The earth was made for me a mosque and a purifier,' where 'tahur' is understood as 'mutahir' (purifier).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Find the exact ruling: tayammum on earth that was impure and dried is invalid according to Zahir al-Riwayah. Note the condition: purity must be certain.
The ruling is not that the earth is impure, but that it lacks purifying capacity.
2
Distinguish tayammum from prayer
Understand the difference: prayer is permissible on such dried earth because drying reduces impurity but does not eradicate it; a small residue is prohibitive in tayammum but not in prayer.
The author uses an analogy to water: a small impurity in water prevents purification but not wearing clothes.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith 'jucilat li al-ardu masjidan wa tahuran' is cited. 'Tahur' is interpreted as 'mutahir' (purifier). This implies that earth must be capable of purifying, which requires it to be pure itself.
The Hanafi understanding: tahur means mutahir, not just tahir.
4
Apply the analogy to used water
The author compares dried impurity earth to used water (al-mā' al-musta'mal): both are pure (tahir) but not purifying (tahur). Thus, tayammum is invalid due to loss of tahuriyyah.
This is a key Hanafi concept: the distinction between tahir and tahur.
5
Address the secondary issue: multiple tayammum
Two people can perform tayammum at the same spot because tayammum is performed by what adheres to the hand, not the remaining earth, unlike leftover water after wudu.
This restricts the 'usage' of earth to what clings to the hand.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يجوز إلا إذا وقع ذلك الغبار عليه بعد ما جف، ولا بد أن تكون طهارته مقطوعاً بها حتى لو تيمم بأرض قد أصابتها نجاسة فجفت وذهب أثرها لم يجز في ظاهر الرواية. والفرق بين التيمم منها وجواز الصلاة عليها أن الجفاف مقلل لا مستأصل وقليلها مانع في التيمم دون الصلاة، ويجوز أن يعتبر القليل مانعاً في شيء كقليلها في الماء مانع دون الثوب. كذا في البدائع وسيأتي تمامه في الأنجاس إن شاء الله تعالى. وظاهر كلامهم أن الأرض التي جفت نجسة في حق التيمم طاهرة في حق الصلاة والحق أنها طاهرة في حق الكل. وإنما منع التيمم منها لفقد الطهورية كالماء المستعمل طاهر غير طهور وكان ينبغي للمصنف أن يقول بمطهر ليخرج ما ذكرنا كما عبر به في منظومة ابن وهبان وللحديث الوارد من قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم جعلت لي الأرض مسجداً وطهوراً بناء على أن الطهور بمعنى المطهر وقد تقدم الكلام فيه . وفي المحيط والبدائع : ولو تيمم اثنان مكان واحد جاز لأنه . من مستعملاً لأن لم يصر التيمم إنما يتأدى بما التزق بيده لا بما فضل كالماء الفاضل في الإناء بعد وضوء الأول ا هـ . وهو يفيد تصور استعماله وقصره على صورة واحدة وهي أن يمسح الذراعين بالضربة التي مسح بها وجهه ليس غير .
It is not permissible except if that dust falls on it after it has dried, and it is necessary that its purity be certain, such that if one performs tayammum on earth that was affected by impurity, then dried and its trace disappeared, it is not permissible in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah). The difference between performing tayammum from it and the permissibility of praying upon it is that drying reduces but does not eradicate, and a small amount of it is prohibitive in tayammum but not in prayer, and it is permissible to consider a small amount prohibitive in one thing like a small amount of it in water being prohibitive but not on a garment. Thus in al-Bada'i', and its completion will come in al-Anjas if Allah wills. The apparent meaning of their statement is that earth that has dried is impure with respect to tayammum and pure with respect to prayer, but the truth is that it is pure in all respects. Rather, tayammum is prevented from it due to lack of purifying quality (tahuriyyah), like used water which is pure but not purifying, and the author should have said 'purifier' (mutahir) to exclude what we mentioned, as was expressed in the versification of Ibn Wahban, and due to the hadith from his saying, peace be upon him: 'The earth was made for me a mosque and a purifier (tahur),' based on tahur meaning purifier (mutahir), and discussion of it has preceded. In al-Muhit and al-Bada'i': If two people perform tayammum at the same spot, it is permissible because the tayammum is not used [water]; tayammum is only performed by what clings to the hand, not by what remains, like the leftover water in the vessel after the first person's ablution. And this implies understanding its use and restricting it to one form: that he wipes his forearms with the same strike with which he wiped his face, nothing more.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof addressing the purity requirement for earth used in tayammum. The author (Zayla'i) clarifies that the earth must be certainly pure; if it was affected by impurity and then dried so that no trace remains, tayammum with it is invalid according to Zahir al-Riwayah. He distinguishes this from prayer, which is permissible on such dried earth because drying reduces impurity but does not remove it completely, and a small amount is prohibitive in tayammum but not for prayer. He analogizes to water: a small amount of impurity in water prevents its use for purification but not for wearing clothes. He notes that the apparent view that dried earth is impure for tayammum and pure for prayer is corrected: it is pure in all respects, but tayammum is prevented due to loss of tahuriyyah (purifying quality), like used water which is pure but not purifying. The author should have used the word 'mutahir' (purifier) to exclude such cases. The proof is the hadith: 'The earth was made for me a mosque and a purifier (tahur),' with tahur meaning mutahir. The passage also discusses two people performing tayammum at the same spot: it is permissible because tayammum is performed only by what adheres to the hand, not by the remaining earth, unlike the leftover water after wudu. This restricts the usage to wiping the forearms with the same strike used for the face.

Key Terms
الطهورية (al-ṭahūriyyah): The property of being purifying (mutahir), i.e., capable of removing ritual impurity.
الماء المستعمل (al-mā' al-musta'mal): Water that has been used for a ritual purification (wudu/ghusl) and is no longer purifying but remains pure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because it has lost its purifying quality (tahuriyyah), like used water.
C) Because the hadith restricts tayammum to pure earth only.
D) Because the Prophet forbade using such earth.

Key Takeaway
Earth must be both pure and purifying for tayammum; drying after impurity removal does not restore its purifying capacity.

Definition of the Genus of Earth (Jins al-Ard) for Tayammum
Defining jins al-ard and listing permissible/impermissible substances with mixture rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion for the genus of earth to determine whether a given substance is permissible for tayammum, including cases of mixtures.

Core Idea
Tayammum is valid only with substances from the genus of earth—anything that burns to ash or melts is excluded; mixtures are judged by preponderance.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a ruling statement that defines the genus of earth (jins al-ard) for tayammum. It establishes a clear criterion from al-Mustasfa: substances that burn to ash or melt and soften are not from the genus; all else is. The passage then enumerates numerous permissible and impermissible substances, including discussions on mixtures, the principle of ghalabah (preponderance), and intra-Hanafi disagreements on specific items like coral and mountain salt. Understanding this passage is crucial for correctly applying tayammum in non-standard situations.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the Definition from al-Mustasfa
Identify the criterion: anything that burns to ash (like wood) or melts/softens (like metals) is not from the genus of earth. Everything else is from the genus of earth.
This is the foundational rule that determines permissibility.
2
Apply to Simple Cases
Classify the listed substances: stone, earth, sand, gypsum, lime, etc. are permissible; trees, glass, frozen water, pearl, flour, ash are impermissible.
Pearl is impermissible because it is animal product, not earth.
3
Understand the Ghalabah Principle for Mixtures
When earth is mixed with a non-earth substance, if earth is prevalent (ghalabah), tayammum is valid. This applies to burnt earth mixed with ash, gold/silver dust, and mud.
Fatawa Qadikhan establishes this principle.
4
Analyze Specific Disputes
Note the disagreements: coral (some prohibit, but mufta bihi permits), mountain salt (two narrations, fatwa permits), and mud (permissible only if time is about to expire).
These are intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf resolved by later scholars.
5
Identify the Operative Ruling (Mufta Bihi)
The relied-upon positions: coral permissible, mountain salt permissible, baked brick permissible, mud allowed only when fear of time passing, gold/silver dust permissible if earth is prevalent.
Always check for preponderance in mixtures.

يجوز التيمم بالأشجار والزجاج المتخذ من الرمل وغيره والماء المنجمد والمعادن إلا أن تكون في محالها، فيجوز للتراب الذي عليها لا بها نفسها، واللؤلؤ وإن كان مسحوقاً لأنه متولد من حيوان في البحر، والدقيق يفصل، والظاهر التفصيل . وفي المحيط : ولو تيمم بالذهب والفضة إن كان مسبوكاً لا يجوز، وإن لم يكن مسبوكاً وكان مختلطاً بالتراب والغلبة للتراب جاز ا هـ. فعلم بهذا أن ما أطلقه في فتح القدير محمول على هذا His statement: (of the genus of earth) means he performs tayammum with what is of the genus of earth. The author said in al-Mustasfa: Everything that burns with fire and becomes ash like wood, or melts and softens like iron, is not of the genus of earth, and what is besides that is of the genus of earth. Thus tayammum is not permissible with trees, glass made from sand and other things, frozen water, and minerals unless they are in their places, then it is permissible due to the dust on them not due to themselves; pearl even if powdered because it is generated from a sea animal; flour and ash; and it is permissible with stone, earth, sand, salty soil formed from earth without water, gypsum, lime, kohl, arsenic, ochre, sulfur, turquoise, agate, balakhsh, emerald, and peridot. In Fath al-Qadir: lack of permissibility with coral, and in Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Tawshih, al-Inayah, al-Muhit, Mi'raj al-Dirayah, and al-Tabyin: permissibility with it, so the first was a slip. As for salt, if it is sea salt, it is not permissible by agreement; if it is mountain salt, there are two narrations, each corrected, mentioned in al-Khulasah, but the fatwa is on its permissibility. In al-Tanjis: And it is permissible with baked brick, which is correct because it is petrified clay; similarly with pure pottery unless it is mixed with something not of the genus of earth or has a dye not of the genus of earth. Thus it is stated absolutely in al-Tanjis, al-Muhit, and others, while what is written in Fatawa Qadikhan: If earth is mixed with something not of the parts of earth, consideration is given to prevalence (ghalabah). This requires differentiating the mixture for raw [brick] unlike baked due to burning what is in it of earth's parts. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: If earth is burned by fire and mixed with ash, consideration is given to the prevalent; if earth is prevalent, tayammum with it is permissible; otherwise not. In Fath al-Qadir: Tayammum with burnt earth is permissible in the more correct view without detail, and the apparent is detail. In al-Muhit: If one performs tayammum with gold and silver, if it is smelted, it is not permissible; if not smelted and mixed with earth with earth being prevalent, it is permissible. Thus it is known that what Fath al-Qadir stated absolutely is to be understood with this detail. And if he finds nothing but mud, he smears it on his garment, then when it dries he performs tayammum with it, and it is said according to Abu Hanifah he performs tayammum with mud, and that is correct because the obligation according to him is placing the hand on the earth, not using a part of it, and mud is of the genus of earth unless it is overwhelmed by water, then tayammum with it is not permissible. Thus in al-Muhit. And al-Walwalaji in his fatwas, the author of al-Mubtagha, restricted permissibility with mud to when he fears the time will pass; before that, not, so that his face does not become soiled, becoming like disfigurement without necessity, and this is a good restriction worth memorizing. And al-Asbijabi mentioned: If wheat or something with which tayammum is not permissible has dust on it, and he strikes his hand on it and performs tayammum, consideration is given: if its trace becomes apparent by extending it, it is permissible; if not apparent, not permissible, and upon this everything with which tayammum is not permissible [if dust covers it] is good to memorize.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement defining the genus of earth (jins al-ard) for tayammum, with extensive enumeration of permissible and impermissible substances. The author cites al-Mustasfa: anything that burns to ash (like wood) or melts/softens (like iron) is not of the earth genus; all else is. Thus trees, glass, frozen water, and metals are impermissible unless there is dust on them. Even powdered pearl is impermissible because it is animal product. Flour, ash, stone, earth, sand, salty soil, gypsum, lime, kohl, arsenic, ochre, sulfur, and various gems are permissible. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on coral: some works prohibit, others permit, and the prohibition is deemed a slip. For salt, sea salt is prohibited by consensus, but mountain salt has two narrations; the fatwa permits it. Baked brick (آجر مشوي) is permissible because it is petrified clay, as is pure pottery unless mixed with non-earth substances. When earth is mixed with non-earth, the principle of ghalabah (preponderance) applies: if the mixture has more earth, it is permissible; otherwise not. This applies to burnt earth mixed with ash, and to gold/silver dust mixed with earth. For mud: Abu Hanifah permits tayammum with mud itself because the obligation is to place the hand on earth, not to use a part; but if mud is overwhelmed by water (too runny), it is not permissible. A restriction is added: if only mud is available, one may use it only if he fears the prayer time will pass; otherwise not, to avoid soiling the face unnecessarily. Finally, if a substance like wheat has dust on it, one can strike the hand on it and perform tayammum only if the dust's trace becomes apparent by extending the hand; otherwise not.

Key Terms
جنس الأرض (jins al-ard): The genus of earth: everything that is not combustible to ash nor meltable, including stones, minerals, etc.
الغلبة (al-ghalabah): Preponderance: when earth is mixed with something else, if the earth component is greater, tayammum is valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT permissible for tayammum?
A) Stone
B) Gypsum
C) Coral
D) Pearl

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is valid only with substances from the genus of earth, defined by not burning to ash or melting, with mixtures judged by preponderance of earth.

Permissible Earth-like Substances for Tayammum
Listing rulings on permissible earth-like substances

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on tayammum with various earth-like substances (coral, salt, baked brick, pottery, burnt earth, and gold/silver powders) and apply the principle of ghulba (majority) to mixed substances.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school permits tayammum on any substance of the earth's genus; mixtures are judged by the dominant component.

This lesson covers the extensive list of substances on which tayammum is permissible according to the Hanafi school. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq resolves internal disputes and establishes the operative fatwa, including the critical principle of ghulba (majority) for mixtures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the substances
List the substances mentioned: coral, salt (water-salt and rock-salt), baked brick, pottery, burnt earth, gold and silver. For each, note the ruling.
The text also discusses mixtures with non-earth elements.
2
Analyze internal disputes
For coral, note the disagreement: Fath al-Qadir says impermissible, others say permissible. For rock-salt, there are two narrations but the fatwa is permissibility.
The author declares the first view on coral a mistake.
3
Apply the principle of ghulba
When earth is mixed with non-earth, the majority determines the ruling. If the earth is predominant (ghalib), tayammum is valid; otherwise not.
This applies to burnt earth with ash, gold/silver dust, and pottery with non-earth dyes.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
For each contested item, identify which position is relied upon for fatwa. For coral, the mufta bihi is permissibility; for rock-salt, permissibility.
The fatwa on baked brick and pure pottery is permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم في كذا فتح القدير : عدم الجواز بالمرجان وفي غاية البيان والتوشيح والعناية والمحيط ومعراج الدراية والتبيين الجواز به فكان الأول سهواً. وأما الملح فإن كان مائياً فلا يجوز به اتفاقاً، وإن كان جبلياً ففيه روايتان وصحح كل منهما ذكره في الخلاصة لكن الفتوى على الجواز به . في التنجيس. ويجوز بالآجر المشوي وهو الصحيح لأنه طين مستحجر، وكذا بالخزف الخالص إلا إذا كان مخلوطاً بما ليس من جنس الأرض أو كان عليه صبغ ليس من جنس الأرض. كذا أطلق في التنجيس والمحيط وغيرهما مع أن المسطور في فتاوى قاضيخان : التراب إذا خالطه شيء ما ليس من أجزاء الأرض يعتبر فيه الغلبة، وهذا يقتضي أن يفصل المخالط للنيء بخلاف المشوي لاحتراق ما فيه من أجزاء الأرض كذا في فتح القدير .. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : وإذا احترقت الأرض بالنار إن اختلطت بالرماد يعتبر فيه الغالب إن كانت الغلبة للتراب جاز به التيمم وإلا فلا. وفي فتح القدير : يجوز التيمم بالأرض المحترقة في الأصح ولم يفصل، والظاهر التفصيل . وفي المحيط : ولو تيمم بالذهب والفضة إن كان مسبوكاً لا يجوز، وإن لم يكن مسبوكاً وكان مختلطاً بالتراب والغلبة للتراب جاز ا هـ. فعلم بهذا أن ما أطلقه في فتح القدير محمول على هذا التفصيل، وإذا لم يجد إلا الطين يلطخه بثوبه فإذا جف تيمم به، وقيل عند أبي حنيفة يتيمم بالطين وهو الصحيح لأن الواجب عنده وضع اليد على الأرض لا استعمال جزء منه والطين من جنس الأرض إلا إذا صار مغلوباً بالماء فلا يجوز التيمم به. كذا في المحيط . وقيد الجواز بالطين الولوالجي في فتاواه صاحب المبتغى بأن يخاف خروج الوقت، أما قبله فلا كيلا يتلطخ وجهه فيصير بمعنى المثلة من غير ضرورة وهو قيد حسن ينبغي حفظه.
From Fath al-Qadir: Tayammum is not permissible with coral, but in Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Tawshih, al-'Inayah, al-Muhit, Ma'arij al-Dirayah, and al-Tabyin it is permissible, so the first is a mistake. As for salt: if it is water-salt, then it is not permissible by agreement; if it is rock-salt, there are two narrations, and each has been authenticated. It is mentioned in al-Khulasa but the fatwa is on permissibility with it. In al-Tanjis: Tayammum is permissible with baked brick, and that is the correct view because it is petrified clay. Likewise with pure pottery, unless it is mixed with something not of the earth's genus or it has a dye not of the earth's genus. Thus it is stated absolutely in al-Tanjis, al-Muhit, and others, although the written text in Fatawa Qadikhan: Earth mixed with something not of the earth's parts, consideration is given to the majority. This requires distinguishing the mixture from the raw, contrary to the baked because of the burning of what is in it from the earth's parts. Similarly in Fath al-Qadir. In Fatawa Qadikhan: If earth is burnt by fire, if mixed with ash, consideration is given to the majority; if the majority is earth, tayammum is permissible, otherwise not. In Fath al-Qadir: Tayammum with burnt earth is permissible in the most correct view, without distinguishing, but the apparent is distinguishing. In al-Muhit: If one makes tayammum with gold or silver, if it is minted, it is not permissible; if it is not minted and mixed with earth, the majority being earth, it is permissible. From this it is known that what Fath al-Qadir stated absolutely is interpreted with this distinction. If one finds nothing but clay, he smears his garment with it, and when it dries, he makes tayammum with it. It is said according to Abu Hanifa that he makes tayammum with wet clay, and that is the correct view because the obligatory act with him is placing the hand on the earth, not using a part of it, and clay is of the earth's genus, unless it is overwhelmed by water, then tayammum is not permissible. Similarly in al-Muhit. Al-Walwalji in his Fatawa, the author of al-Mubtagha, restricted permissibility to fear of time leaving; before that, no, lest his face become smeared, leading to distortion without necessity. That is a good restriction that should be memorized.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, listing various substances and their permissibility for tayammum. The author begins with a dispute over coral (marjan): Fath al-Qadir says impermissible, while other sources say permissible; the first view is deemed a mistake. For salt, water-salt is impermissible by consensus, but rock-salt has two narrations; the fatwa favors permissibility. Baked brick (آجر مشوي) is permissible as it is petrified clay. Pure pottery is permissible unless mixed with non-earth substances or has non-earth dye. The text then introduces the principle of ghulba (majority) for mixtures: if earth is mixed with non-earth, the majority determines the ruling; burnt earth is treated similarly. Gold and silver in dust form are permissible if the earth is dominant. The passage then addresses wet clay (طين): at Abu Hanifa, tayammum with wet clay is valid because the obligation is placing the hand on earth, not using a part; however, if overwhelmed by water, it is invalid. Al-Walwalji adds a condition: tayammum with wet clay is only allowed when there is fear of time leaving, to avoid smearing the face without necessity. This condition is praised and recommended for memorization.

Key Terms
صعيد (sa'id): Face of the earth, including soil, sand, stones, etc.
مرجان (marjan): Coral, a marine substance considered by many Hanafi sources as permissible for tayammum.
غالبية (ghalibiyyah): Predominance; the principle that the majority component determines the ruling for mixed substances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for tayammum with baked brick (آجر مشوي)?
A) Impermissible because it is not earth
B) Permissible because it is petrified clay
C) Permissible only if mixed with sand
D) Impermissible unless fired in a specific manner

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits tayammum on a wide range of earth-like substances, with mixtures judged by the dominant component.

Wet Clay (Teen) and the Condition of Fear of Time
Ruling on wet clay with condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum with wet clay, the condition of fear of time leaving, and explain why the condition is necessary.

Core Idea
Wet clay is valid for tayammum only when time is about to expire, to avoid unnecessary soiling of the face.

This lesson focuses on the special case of wet clay (teen). According to Abu Hanifa, tayammum with wet clay is fundamentally valid because the obligation is to place the hand on earth, not to use a dry particle. However, later scholars added a condition of necessity to prevent a man from soiling his face without cause.

Guided Path
1
Understand Abu Hanifa's reasoning
The wajib in tayammum is wad' al-yad (placing the hand on earth), not isti'mal (using a part of earth). Therefore, wet clay qualifies as 'earth'.
This is a key difference from other schools that require dry soil.
2
Note the condition from al-Walwalji
Al-Walwalji added that permissibility is conditional upon fear of time leaving (khawf khuruj al-waqt). Before that, it is not allowed.
The reason is to avoid mithla (distortion of appearance) without necessity.
3
Recognize the limit of validity
Even with fear of time, if the clay is overwhelmed by water (maghlub bi'l-ma'), it is not valid.
The overwhelming water negates the earth-like quality.
4
Determine the operative ruling
The mufta bihi incorporates the condition: wet clay is valid only when one fears the prayer time will end.
This is a good restriction (qayd hasan) recommended for memorization.

Tayammum on Dusty Surfaces: The Dispute on Sa'id
Explaining tayammum on dusty surfaces and the inter-madhhab dispute on what constitutes sa'id

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the definition of sa'id for tayammum and evaluate the counter-argument of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Sa'id includes all earth; dust on objects suffices when apparent.

The Hanafi school permits tayammum on any part of the earth's surface, including dusty objects, provided dust is visible on the hand. This expansive view is contested by Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i, who restrict tayammum to pure soil or sand. The dispute hinges on the interpretation of 'sa'id' in the Quran and the precise wording of the hadith. This lesson unpacks the proofs, the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and condition
State the Hanafi ruling that tayammum is valid with any earth, including a dusty cloak, provided the dust leaves a trace on the hand. This condition is derived from al-Isbijabi's statement.
This condition (istibanah al-athar) is key for objects that are not pure earth.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold the expansive view. Abu Yusuf restricts tayammum to pure earth (turab) or sand. Note the opposing school aligns with Abu Yusuf.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf that also parallels the Shafi'i position.
3
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad cite Quran 4:43 (sa'id) as general, and the hadith 'the earth was made a place of prostration and a purifier' with the lam for genus. The opponent cites the hadith 'and its dust was made a purifier' to specify turab.
The Hanafi response argues that turab is a subset of sa'id and does not exclude other earth.
4
Determine the practical effect (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, one may perform tayammum on a dusty garment if dust is apparent. According to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, only pure earth or sand is valid, so such tayammum would be invalid.
This directly affects daily practice, especially when water is unavailable.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
Later authorities like al-Ramli affirm that the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two shaykhs) is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, despite that al-Hawi al-Qudsi chose Abu Yusuf's view.
The matn authors consistently relied on the two shaykhs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر الاسبيجابي ولو أن الحنطة أو الشيء الذي لا يجوز عليه التيمم إذا كان عليه التراب فضرب يده عليه وتيمم ينظر إن كان يستبين أثره بمده عليه جاز، وإن كان لا يستبين لا يجوز ا.هـ. وبهذا يعلم حكم التيمم على جوخة أو بساط عليه غبار، فالظاهر عدم الجواز لقلة وجود هذا الشرط في نحو الجوخة فليتنبه له والله سبحانه الموفق. وهذا كله عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف : لا يجوز إلا بالتراب وهو قول الشافعي لما أخرجه مسلم عن حذيفة عن النبي الله قال وجعلت لي الأرض مسجداً وجعل تربتها لنا أحمد والبيهقي وجعل لي التراب طهوراً ولأبي حنيفة ومحمد قوله تعالى فتيمموا صعيداً طيباً ﴾ [النساء : ٤٣] والصعيد اسم لوجه الأرض تراباً كان أو غيره. قال الزجاج : لا أعلم اختلافاً . بين أهل اللغة في ذلك، وإذا كان هذا مفهومه وجب تعميمه طهوراً» روی وتعين حمل تفسير ابن عباس الصعيد بالتراب على الأغلب، ويدل عليه قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في الصحيحين وجعلت لي الأرض مسجداً وطهوراً لأن اللام فيها للجنس فلا يخرج شيء منها لأن الأرض كلها جعلت مسجداً، وما جعل مسجداً هو الذي جعل طهوراً. وما في فيه غبار لطخ ثوبه من الطين حتى إذا جف تيمم لأن هذا تحصيل التراب فيجب عليه ذلك كما يجب عليه تحصيل الماء لو قدر عليه. وإن ذهب الوقت قبل أن يجف لا يتيمم بالطين ما لم يجف لكن مشايخنا قالوا: هذا قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله فإن عنده لا يجوز التيمم إلا بالتراب أو بالرمل، فأما عند أبي حنيفة فإن خاف ذهاب الوقت تيمم بالطين لأن التيمم بالطين عنده جائز لأنه . من أجزاء الأرض إلا أنه لا يتيمم قبل خوف ذهاب الوقت كيلا يتلطخ بوجهه فيصير بمعنى المثلة. هذا إذا لم يقدر على الصعيد، أما إذا قدر عليه مع هذا كما لو نفض ثوبه وتيمم بغباره جاز في قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد رحمهما الله . وقال : أبو يوسف رحمه الله : لا يجوز لأن الجواز عنده متعلق بالتراب أو بالرمل ولم يوجد. اهـ. كلامه. فقوله لأن التيمم عنده بالطين جائز الخ صريح في عدم اشتراط خروج الوقت لكن لما كان في معنى المثلة وجب تأخير فعله إلى ذلك الوقت لئلا يباشر ما هو معنى المثلة لغير ضرورة لا أنه لو فعله لم يجز، وهذا مستفاد من إطلاق المتون جوازه من جنس الأرض. وبما سبق ظهر لك صحة ما بحثته في التيمم على الجوخة وأنه على التفصيل بحصول الغبار وعدمه تأمل . ثم إني رأيت الشيخ عمر بن نجيم رحمه الله في النهر ذكر عين ما ذكرته حيث قال : ثم إني راجعت الفتاوى الولوالجية فإذا الذي فيها ونقل عبارته المتقدمة ثم قال : فتوهم رحمه الله أن معناه لا يصح التيمم وليس كذلك، بل معناه لا ينبغي له فعل ذلك بلا ضرورة ولو فعل جاز لأنه تيمم بما هو من أجزاء الأرض ولا جائز أن يكون من أجزائها في حال دون حال قوله : فالظاهر عدم الجواز) قال الرملي : بل الظاهر التفصيل إن استبان أثره جاز وإلا لا لوجود الشرط خصوصاً في ثياب ذري الأشغال تأمل قوله : وقال أبو يوسف لا يجوز الخ) قال الرملي قال في الحاوي القدسي والمختار قول أبي يوسف. وقال في شرح المنظومة المسمى بالحقائق، والصحيح قول الشيخين .اهـ وأقول قول الشيخين هو الذي اعتمده أصحاب المتون فلا يخفى أن ما في الحاوي غريب والله تعالى أعلم. قوله: (وجعل تربتها لنا طهوراً) ما سيأتي من قوله وأما رواية وترابها طهوراً الخ يقتضي أن يكون المذكور هنا ترابها لا تربتها
Al-Isbijabiy mentioned: If there is grain or something upon which tayammum is not permissible, but there is dust on it, and he strikes his hand on it and makes tayammum, consider: if its trace becomes apparent by his hand, it is permissible; if not, it is not permissible. From this is known the ruling of tayammum on a cloak or a rug that has dust: the apparent is impermissibility because this condition rarely exists in such items, so be mindful. And all this according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: it is not permissible except with earth, and that is the saying of al-Shafi'i, because of what Muslim narrated from Hudhayfa from the Prophet (ﷺ): 'The earth was made for me a place of prostration and its dust was made for us a purifier.' (Ahmad and Bayhaqi: 'And dust was made for me a purifier.') For Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the verse 'so make tayammum with clean sa'id' (4:43), and sa'id is a name for the face of the earth, whether soil or otherwise. Al-Zajjaj said: I know of no disagreement among the linguists about that. And if this is its meaning, it is obligatory to generalize it. And it is determined to interpret Ibn Abbas's explanation of sa'id as soil predominantly, and evidence for it is his (ﷺ) saying in the two Sahihs: 'The earth was made for me a place of prostration and a purifier.' Because the lam is for the genus, so nothing is excluded from it. And what is made a place of prostration is what is made a purifier. And what is in it: he smears his garment with wet clay until it dries and makes tayammum, because this is obtaining earth, so it is obligatory upon him just as it is obligatory upon him to obtain water if he could. But if time leaves before it dries, he does not make tayammum with the clay until it dries. Our mashayikh said: This is the saying of Abu Yusuf, for according to him tayammum is only permissible with earth or sand. As for according to Abu Hanifa, if he fears the time leaving, he makes tayammum with wet clay because tayammum with clay is permissible according to him since it is from the parts of the earth. However, he does not make tayammum before fear of time leaving so as not to smear his face, becoming a form of disfigurement. This is when he cannot find sa'id. But if he can find it, such as by shaking his garment and making tayammum with its dust, it is permissible in the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: it is not permissible because permissibility according to him is connected to earth or sand, and that was not found. So his statement: because tayammum with clay is permissible for him etc. is explicit in not requiring the time to leave, but since it resembles disfigurement, its action must be delayed to that time for him not to commit what is like disfigurement without necessity, not that if he does it it is invalid. And this is derived from the absolute allowance of the texts that it is from the genus of earth. From what preceded, the correctness of your investigation on tayammum on a cloak is clear, and that it is according to the distinction: obtaining dust or not. Then I saw Shaykh Umar ibn Nujaym in al-Nahr mention exactly what I mentioned, saying: I reviewed the Fatawa al-Walwaljiyya and found what is in it, and he quoted the previous expression. Then he said: He (meaning al-Ramli) misunderstood that its meaning is that tayammum is not valid, but it is not like that; rather, its meaning is that he should not do so without necessity, and if he does, it is valid because he made tayammum with what is from the parts of the earth, and it cannot be that it is from its parts in one case and not another. He said: 'so the apparent is impermissibility' – al-Ramli said: rather the apparent is distinction: if its trace becomes apparent it is permissible, otherwise not, due to the existence of the condition, especially in clothes of busy people. He said: 'and Abu Yusuf said it is not permissible etc.' – al-Ramli said: al-Hawi al-Qudsi said the chosen view is that of Abu Yusuf. And in Sharh al-Manzuma called al-Haqa'iq, the correct view is that of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). I say: the view of the two shaykhs is what the authors of the matn relied upon, so it is not hidden that what is in al-Hawi is strange. His saying: 'and He made its dust for us a purifier' – what will come later from his saying: 'and the narration: and its dust a purifier' indicates that what is mentioned here is 'turabiha' (its dust) not 'turbaitha' (its dust).
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the definition of sa'id for tayammum. It begins with a ruling from al-Isbijabi: tayammum on a dusty object (like grain) is valid only if dust is apparent on the hand. The author applies this to cloaks and rugs, concluding that such tayammum is usually invalid due to lack of apparent dust. This ruling holds according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf holds a stricter view: tayammum is only valid with pure earth (turab) or sand. The passage then presents the proofs: Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i rely on hadith specifying 'dust' (turab), while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rely on the Quranic verse commanding tayammum with 'sa'id', which linguistically includes all earth. Al-Zajjaj confirms no linguistic disagreement. The text argues that the hadith 'the earth was made a place of prostration and a purifier' supports the general view because the lam in 'al-ard' is for genus. A subsequent discussion clarifies that tayammum with wet clay is valid at Abu Hanifa even without fear of time, but it is recommended to delay to avoid disfigurement. The passage then references later scholars: al-Ramli and Ibn Nujaym affirm the distinction based on apparent dust. al-Ramli notes that al-Hawi al-Qudsi chose Abu Yusuf's view, but the relied-upon position (mu'tamad) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Finally, a textual note: the hadith mentions 'turabiha' (its dust) not 'turbaitha'.

Key Terms
صعيد (sa'id): Face of the earth, including all types of terrain like soil, sand, gravel.
تراب (turab): Dust or fine soil, specifically mentioned in hadith.
التربة (turba): Dust or soil; variant reading in hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), which of the following is valid for tayammum?
A) A dusty woolen cloak with visible dust on the hand
B) Pure sand only
C) Only soil from a specific region
D) Any surface as long as it is dry

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, defines sa'id as all earth, so tayammum on a dusty object is valid if dust is apparent, contrary to the stricter view of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i.

Taharah — Purification

Tayammum Valid Without Dust: Hanafi Position on Sa'id
Dispute over whether dust is required for tayammum; Hanafi position that any earthy surface suffices

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the necessity of dust for tayammum and apply the proofs from the hadith of Ammar and the interpretation of Quranic 'min'.

Core Idea
Tayammum is valid on any part of the earth, dust not required.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the commentator defends the Hanafi view that tayammum is valid even on earth without dust. The dispute involves both inter-madhhab differences with the Shafi'i school and intra-Hanafi differences with Imam Muhammad. We will examine the key proofs and the usul principles that underpin the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the matn: tayammum is valid on earth even if there is no dust (nqa').
The matn says: (الأرض وإن لم يكن عليه نقع)
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The opponent (Shafi'i school and Muhammad al-Shaybani) requires dust (turab) for tayammum.
Muhammad's view: لا يجوز لظاهر قوله تعالى فامسحوا...
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent argues from the Quranic 'minhu' (partitive) and the concept of mafhum al-laqab, implying that only 'turab' suffices.
They cite: فامسحوا بوجوهكم وأيديكم منه and the mention of 'turab' in some hadith.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis interpret 'min' as ibtida' al-ghayah (beginning of place), not partitive. Mafhum al-laqab is rejected in Hanafi usul. Mention of 'turab' is due to usual practice, not exclusivity.
Example: توضأت من النهر means 'I began wudu from the river'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: A person can perform tayammum on a clean rock without dust in the Hanafi school, but not in the Shafi'i school.
Also, Abu Yusuf allows it only when unable to find dust; the mufta bihi is the broad permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(الأرض وإن لم يكن عليه نقع وبه بلا عجز ناوياً فلغاً تيمم كافر لا وضوءه ولا تنقضه) ... لنا : لا تعارض فالعمل بهما واجب. فإن قيل المفهوم مخصص عند قائليه فذكرها يخرج غيرها قلنا أما على أصلنا فظاهر ومن أجاز المفهوم فبغير اللقب ا هـ. وكذا ذكر ابن الحاجب في أصوله وبهذا اندفع ما ذكره النووي في شرح مسلم أنه من قبيل حمل المطلق على المقيد قال القرطبي في تفسيره: وقولهم هذا من باب المطلق والمقيد فليس كذلك وإنما هو من باب النص على بعض أشخاص العموم كقوله تعالى فيهما فاكهة ونخل ورمان [الرحمن: ١٤٦٨ هـ. وعلى تسليم أنهما منه وقولهم أن مفهوم اللقب حجة إذا اقترن بقرينة وهي هنا موجودة لأنه لولا أن الحكم متعلق بالمذكور لم يكن لذكره فائدة قلنا: إنه إنما ذكره جرياً على الغالب وإشارة إلى أنه الأصل. قوله : ( وإن لم يكن عليه نقع أي وإن لم يكن على جنس الأرض غبار حتى لو وضع يده على حجر لا غبار عليه يجوز. وقال محمد لا يجوز لظاهر قوله تعالى فامسحوا بوجوهكم وأيديكم منه ﴾ [النساء : ٤٣] قلنا : «من» للابتداء في المكان إذ لا . يصح فيها ضابط التبعيضية وهو وضع بعض موضعها والباقي بحاله إذ لو قيل فامسحوا بوجوهكم وأيديكم بعضها أفاد أن المطلوب جعل الصعيد ممسوحاً والعضوين آلته وهو منتف اتفاقاً، ولا يصح فيها ضابط البيانية وهو وضع الذي موضعها مع جزء ليتم صلة الموصول كما في اجتنبوا الرجس من الأوثان) [الحج : ۳۰] أي الذي هو الأوثان. كذا في فتح ومثله «توضأت من النهر أي ابتداء الأخذ للوضوء من النهر. وفي الكشاف : فإن قلت قولهم إنها لابتداء الغاية قول متعسف ولا يفهم أحد من العرب من قول القائل مسحت . برأسي من الدهن ومن الماء ومن التراب إلا معنى التبعيض قلت : هو كما تقول والإدعان للحق أحق من المراء» ذكره في تفسير آية النساء واختار ابن أمير حاج تلميذ المحقق ابن الهمام أنها لتبيين جنس ما تماسه الآلة التي بها يمسح العضوين على أن في الآية شيئاً مقدراً طوى ذكره لدلالة الكلام عليه كما هو دأب إيجاز الحذف الذي هو باب من البلاغة. التقدير والله أعلم : امسحوا بوجوهكم وأيديكم مما مسه شيء من الصعيد وهذا لا . استعمال يوجب جزء من الصعيد في العضوين قطعاً ا هـ . وقوله «وبه بلا عجز» أي بالنقع يجوز التيمم بلا عجز عن التراب وعند أبي يوسف لا يجوز إلا عند العجز . تنبيهات : الأول : أن الصعيد المذكور في الآية ظرف مكان عندنا وعند الشافعي ومن يشترط التراب مفعول به بتقدير حذف الباء أي بصعيد ذكره القرطبي. الثاني: أن التيمم على التيمم ليس بقربة كذا في القنية وظاهره أنه ليس بمكروه وينبغي كراهته لكونه عبثاً. الثالث : ذكر في الغاية أن ههنا لطيفة وهي أن الله تعالى خلق درة ونظر إليها فصارت ماء ثم تكاثف منه وصار تراباً وتلطف منه فصار هواء وتلطف منه فصار ناراً فكان الماء أصلاً. ذكره المفسرون وهو منقول عن التوراة وإنما لم يجز التيمم بالمعدن كالحديد لأنه ليس بتبع للماء وحده حتى يقوم مقامه ولا للتراب كذلك وإنما هو مركب من العناصر الأربعة فليس له اختصاص بشيء منها حتى يقوم مقامه .
The earth even if there is no dust on it, and with it (dust) without inability, intending, then the tayammum of a disbeliever is void; his ablution is not broken... For us: there is no contradiction, acting upon both is obligatory. If it is said: the concept (mafhum) specifies according to its proponents, so mentioning them excludes others, we say: according to our principle it is apparent, and whoever permits the concept (mafhum) then not by the title (al-laqab)... And it is mentioned by Ibn al-Hajib in his Usul, and by this is repelled what al-Nawawi mentioned in Sharh Muslim that it is of the type of carrying the absolute to the restricted. Al-Qurtubi said in his Tafsir: Their saying that this is from the chapter of absolute and restricted is not so, rather it is from the chapter of specifying some individuals of the general, like His statement: 'In them are fruit, and date-palms, and pomegranates'... And if it is conceded that they are from it, and their saying that the concept of the title is evidence when accompanied by an indication, which exists here because if the ruling were not attached to the mentioned, there would be no benefit in mentioning it, we say: He only mentioned it following the usual and indicating that it is the origin. His statement: (even if there is no dust on it) meaning even if there is no dust on the type of earth, such that if one places his hand on a stone without dust it is permissible. Muhammad said it is not permissible due to the apparent meaning of His statement: 'so wipe your faces and hands from it' (Quran 4:43). We say: 'min' is for beginning in place, since the meaning of partitive does not hold in it... His statement: (and with it without inability) meaning with dust, tayammum is permissible even without inability to obtain dust. According to Abu Yusuf, it is not permissible except when unable. First point: The 'sa'id' mentioned in the verse is an adverb of place according to us, whereas according to al-Shafi'i and those who require dust, it is an object with a deleted preposition, i.e., with sa'id, as mentioned by al-Qurtubi. Second: Tayammum on tayammum is not an act of worship. Third: It is mentioned in al-Ghayah that there is a subtlety here: Allah created a pearl, looked at it, and it became water, then it became thick and became dust, then it became subtle and became air, then it became subtle and became fire, so water was the origin. Tayammum is not permissible on minerals like iron because it is not subsidiary to water alone to take its place, nor to dust similarly; rather it is composed of the four elements, so it has no specificity with any of them to take its place.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that tayammum is valid even on earth without dust (nqa'). The commentary expands with proofs. The Hanafi position holds that صعيد (sa'id) refers to the entire surface of the earth, not just soil with dust. This is supported by the hadith of Ammar where the Prophet said 'enough for you is to strike your hands on the earth' without specifying dust. Also, the hadith of tayammum on a wall (in Bukhari) shows that dust is not necessary. The opponents (including Shafi'is) argue that dust is required based on the word 'turab' in some narrations and the concept of 'mafhum al-laqab' which would specify only dusty earth. The Hanafi rebuttal: such a concept is not accepted in Hanafi usul, and the mention of 'turab' in some narrations is due to the usual case, not exclusivity. The verse 'faimsahu biwujuhikum waaydikum minhu' uses 'min' which Hanafis interpret as 'ibda' al-ghayah' (beginning of place), not 'tab'id' (partitive), thus requiring wiping from the earth, not with a part of it. This is supported by the phrase 'tawadd'tu min al-nahr' (I took ablution from the river) meaning beginning, not taking a part. The commentary also notes that Muhammad ibn al-Hasan required dust (nqa'), but the relied-upon position is that tayammum is valid without dust. Abu Yusuf only permits without dust if unable to find dust. The passage also discusses that tayammum on tayammum is not meritorious and clarifies that minerals are not valid for tayammum because they are composite, not purely from one element.

Key Terms
صعيد (sa'id): The surface of the earth, encompassing soil, sand, rock, and all things attached to it.
نقع (naq'): Dust or fine particles that arise from the earth when struck.
مفهوم اللقب (mafhum al-laqab): The implication of a title: that mentioning a specific term implies exclusivity (only that term's referent is valid).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is tayammum valid on a large rock that has no dust at all on it?
A) Yes, because any part of the earth (sa'id) suffices.
B) No, because dust (nqa') is required.
C) Only if there is no water available.
D) Only according to Muhammad; Abu Hanifa requires dust.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that tayammum is valid on any part of the earth, including surfaces without dust, making purification accessible in diverse environments.

Meaning of Sa'id and Tayammum with Dust without Inability
Clarifies the meaning of صعيد and disputes tayammum with dust without inability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi interpretation of الصعيد in the tayammum verse and state the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding tayammum with dust without inability.

Core Idea
الصعيد means the entire earth surface, so tayammum is valid on any natural ground even without inability.

The Quranic verse on tayammum uses the word صعيد. Does it mean only pure soil or any part of the earth's surface? This distinction leads to a practical difference in validity of tayammum. Additionally, within the Hanafi school, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf differ on whether inability to use soil is a condition for performing tayammum with dust. This lesson unpacks both issues from the text of al-Bahr al-Raiq.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on الصعيد
Identify that the Hanafi school interprets الصعيد as the entire surface of the earth, not restricted to soil. This is based on linguistic analysis and the verse's context.
The verse: 'فَتيمَّموا صعيداً طيباً' (4:43, 5:6).
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i and others hold that الصعيد specifically means pure soil, so tayammum is only valid on soil.
3
Analyse the Hanafi proof from the verse
The Hanafis argue that الصعيد is an adverb of place (zarf) and refers to the entire earth. The verse implies wiping the face and hands with dust that comes from any part of the earth.
The author cites an interpretation that the verse has an omitted element: 'wipe your faces and hands with something that has been touched by part of the earth.'
4
Consider the intra-Hanafi dispute on inability
Abu Hanifa permits tayammum with dust (using a specific method) without inability to use soil. Abu Yusuf restricts it to cases of inability.
The phrase 'وبه بلا عجز' is interpreted differently.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to the Hanafi school, tayammum can be performed on rock, grass, or any natural surface if dust is present. Shafi'is require actual soil. Within Hanafis, the mufta bihi view follows Abu Hanifa, allowing tayammum with dust even when soil is accessible but not used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم برأسي من الدهن ومن الماء ومن التراب إلا معنى التبعيض قلت : هو كما تقول والإدعان للحق أحق من المراء» ذكره في تفسير آية النساء واختار ابن أمير حاج تلميذ المحقق ابن الهمام أنها لتبيين جنس ما تماسه الآلة التي بها يمسح العضوين على أن في الآية شيئاً مقدراً طوى ذكره لدلالة الكلام عليه كما هو دأب إيجاز الحذف الذي هو باب من البلاغة. التقدير والله أعلم : امسحوا بوجوهكم وأيديكم مما مسه شيء من الصعيد وهذا لا . استعمال يوجب جزء من الصعيد في العضوين قطعاً ا هـ . وقوله «وبه بلا عجز» أي بالنقع يجوز التيمم بلا عجز عن التراب وعند أبي يوسف لا يجوز إلا عند العجز .
Book of Purification – Chapter of Tayammum. ... He said: 'And by it without inability' meaning with dust, tayammum is permitted without inability to use soil, but according to Abu Yusuf it is not permitted except when unable.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the meaning of الصعيد in the tayammum verse. The Hanafi school holds that الصعيد means the entire surface of the earth, not just soil. Therefore, tayammum is valid even without inability to use water, as per Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf disagrees and restricts tayammum to cases of inability. The author presents the Hanafi view supported by interpretation of the verse.

Key Terms
صعيد (ṣaʿīd): In this context, the entire surface of the earth, including soil, rock, grass, etc.
تميم (tayammum): Ritual purification with clean earth when water is unavailable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what does the word 'الصعيد' in the tayammum verse refer to?
A) Only pure soil
B) The entire surface of the earth
C) Dust only
D) Stone only

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines الصعيد as the entire earth's surface, making tayammum valid on any natural ground, and within the school, Abu Hanifa's view allowing tayammum with dust without inability is mufta bihi.

Three Beneficial Notes on Tayammum
Three additional notes on tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of صعيد, explain the ruling on tayammum on tayammum, and identify which surfaces are invalid for tayammum.

Core Idea
Tayammum on tayammum is futile; صعيد is a place, not soil; minerals are not valid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents three independent but important notes on tayammum. The first clarifies the linguistic and legal meaning of صعيد in the Qur'anic verse of tayammum. The second addresses the ruling on repeating tayammum without a new excuse. The third provides a cosmological background and explains why minerals like iron are not valid for tayammum.

Guided Path
1
List the three notes
Read the passage and identify the three distinct topics discussed.
2
Analyze the first note: definition of صعيد
According to the Hanafis, الصعيد in the verse is an adverb of place, not an object meaning 'soil'. Understand the linguistic difference and its effect on the permissibility of tayammum on any earth surface.
Contrast with Shafi'i view: صعيد as object meaning soil.
3
Analyze the second note: tayammum on tayammum
The text states that performing tayammum on an existing tayammum is not a meritorious act (qurba) and should be disliked as futile (عبث). Determine the ruling: makruh tanzih.
4
Analyze the third note: origin of elements and ruling on minerals
The passage mentions a subtlety about the creation of water, soil, air, and fire. Then it concludes that minerals like iron are composed of all four elements and have no exclusive relation to water or soil, so they are not valid for tayammum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيهات : الأول : أن الصعيد المذكور في الآية ظرف مكان عندنا وعند الشافعي ومن يشترط التراب مفعول به بتقدير حذف الباء أي بصعيد ذكره القرطبي. الثاني: أن التيمم على التيمم ليس بقربة كذا في القنية وظاهره أنه ليس بمكروه وينبغي كراهته لكونه عبثاً. الثالث : ذكر في الغاية أن ههنا لطيفة وهي أن الله تعالى خلق درة ونظر إليها فصارت ماء ثم تكاثف منه وصار تراباً وتلطف منه فصار هواء وتلطف منه فصار ناراً فكان الماء أصلاً. ذكره المفسرون وهو منقول عن التوراة وإنما لم يجز التيمم بالمعدن كالحديد لأنه ليس بتبع للماء وحده حتى يقوم مقامه ولا للتراب كذلك وإنما هو مركب من العناصر الأربعة فليس له اختصاص بشيء منها حتى يقوم مقامه .
Warnings: First: that الصعيد mentioned in the verse is an adverb of place according to us (Hanafis), and according to al-Shafi'i and those who require soil, it is an object with the preposition omitted, i.e. 'with soil' as al-Qurtubi mentioned. Second: that performing tayammum on top of tayammum is not a meritorious act, as stated in al-Qunyah, and apparently it is not disliked but should be disliked because it is futile. Third: It was mentioned in al-Ghayah that there is a subtlety here: that Allah created a pearl and looked at it, so it became water, then it thickened from it and became soil, and refined from it so it became air, and refined from it so it became fire, so water was the origin. The exegetes mentioned it and it is transmitted from the Torah. And tayammum with minerals like iron is not permitted because it is not derived from water alone to take its place, nor from soil likewise, but it is composed of the four elements, so it has no special connection with any of them to take its place.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage contains three independent notes. The first note reaffirms the Hanafi position that الصعيد is an adverb of place in the verse, contrasting with the Shafi'i view that it is an object with a preposition. The second note rules that performing tayammum on an existing tayammum (i.e., repeating tayammum without a new excuse) is not a meritorious act and is in fact disliked as futile. The third note provides a mystical origin story and concludes that minerals like iron are not valid for tayammum because they have no exclusive relation to either water or soil.

Key Terms
قربة (qurba): An act of worship that brings one closer to Allah.
عبث (ʿabath): Futility; an act without benefit or purpose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on performing tayammum on top of a previous tayammum without a new excuse?
A) Sunnah
B) Makruh
C) Mubah
D) Mustahab

Key Takeaway
Three key points: صعيد means the earth surface, not just soil; repeating tayammum unnecessarily is makruh; minerals are not valid for tayammum.

Taharah — Purification
