10 min
Condition of Intention (Niyyah) in Tayammum
Detailed expansion of the intention condition in tayammum with case-by-case application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for intention in tayammum and distinguish between valid and invalid intentions based on the concept of qurba maqsuda.

Core Idea
Intention in tayammum must be for a qurba maqsuda — an act of worship that requires purification and is intended for its own sake.

This lesson unpacks a key condition of tayammum: intention (niyyah). While any good deed may seem sufficient, the Hanafi school requires the intention to target an act of worship that is invalid without purification. We will explore the definition of niyyah, the scope of valid intentions, and several applications including the intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum for embracing Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling and its source
Recognize that the matn (Kanz al-Daqaiq) states 'intending' as a condition; the sharh expands this by defining intention and its requirements.
The base text is minimal; the commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq provides the detailed expansion.
2
Understand the definition of niyyah and its condition
Examine the definition: intention is a 'recently occurring will' (al-irada al-haditha). The condition is that the intended act must be a qurba maqsuda — an act of worship intended for its own sake that requires purification.
Contrast with acts that are not qurba maqsuda, such as entering the mosque or reading Quran.
3
Apply the condition to examples from the text
Work through the cases: tayammum for janazah prayer or sujood al-tilawah permits other prayers because they are qurba maqsuda. Tayammum for reading Quran or entering the mosque does not permit prayer because those acts are not qurba maqsuda.
Note the exception for a junub person who tayammum for reading Quran: some allow it because reading is part of a qurba (prayer) and requires purification.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Identify that Abu Yusuf holds tayammum for embracing Islam (al-Islam) valid, while the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that it is not sufficient for prayer because Islam does not require purification to be valid.
The difference stems from whether the act (Islam) is considered a qurba maqsuda that requires taharah.
5
Synthesize the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon ruling: the intention must be for a qurba maqsuda or a part thereof that is not halal without purification. Thus, tayammum for prayer or sujood is valid; for ancillary acts like touching the mushaf or entering the mosque, it is not.
This synthesis comes from the detailed tafsil (differentiation) provided by the author.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ناوياً) أي يتيمم ناوياً وهي من شروطه والنية والقصد الإرادة الحادثة ولهذا لا يقال الله تعالى ناو ولا قاصد. كذا في المستصفى وشرطها أن يكون المنوي عبادة مقصودة لا تصح إلا بالطهارة أو الطهارة أو استباحة الصلاة أو رفع الحدث أو الجنابة، وما وقع في التنجيس من أن النية المشروطة في التيمم هي نية التطهير وهو الصحيح فلا ينافيه لتضمنها نية التطهير. وإنما اكتفى بنية التطهير لأن الطهارة شرعت للصلاة وشرطت لإباحتهما فكانت نيتها نية إباحة الصلاة حتى لو تيمم لتعليم الغير لا تجوز به الصلاة في الأصح. كذا في معراج الدراية. فلو تيمم لصلاة الجنازة أو سجدة التلاوة جاز له أن يصلي سائر الصلوات لأن كلاً منهما قربة مقصودة، والمراد بالقربة المقصودة أن لا تجب في ضمن شيء آخر بطريق التبعية، ولا ينافي هذا ما ذكر في الأصول من أن سجدة التلاوة ليست بقربة مقصودة حتى لو تلاها في وقت مكروه جاز أن يؤديها في وقت مكروه آخر بخلاف الصلاة المفروضة إذا وجبت في وقت ناقص لا تؤدّي في ناقص آخر لأن النفي والإثبات ليس من جهة واحدة بل من جهتين. والمراد مما ذكر هنا أنها شرعت ابتداء تقرباً إلى الله تعالى من غير أن تكون تبعاً لغيرها بخلاف دخول المسجد ومس المصحف والمراد بما في الأصول أن هيئة السجود ليست بمقصودة لذاتها عند التلاوة بل لاشتمالها على التواضع المحقق لموافقة أهل الإسلام ومخالفة أهل الطغيان فلهذا قلنا : لا يختص إقامة الواجب بهذه الهيئة بل ينوب الركوع في الصلاة على الفور منابها . كذا في معراج الدراية تبعاً للخبازية. وصرحوا بأنه لو تيمم لدخول المسجد أو القراءة ولو من المصحف أو مسه أو زيارة القبور أو دفن الميت أو الآذان أو الإقامة أو السلام أو ردّه أو الإسلام لا تجوز الصلاة بذلك التيمم عند عامة المشايخ لأن بعضها ليست بعبادة مقصودة، والإسلام وإن كان عبادة مقصودة لكن يصح بدون الطهارة. هكذا أطلقوا في قراءة القرآن المنع ، وفي المحيط : أطلق الجواز وسوى بين صلاة الجنازة وسجدة التلاوة وقراءة القرآن. وفي السراج الوهاج : الأصح أنه لا يجوز له أن يصلي إذا تيمم لقراءة القرآن والحق التفصيل فيها فإن تيمم لها وهو جنب جاز له أن يصلي به سائر الصلوات . كذا في البدائع وغاية البيان. ولم يفصلا في دخول المسجد بين أن يكون جنباً أو محدثاً مع أن كلاً منهما تبع لغيره وهو الصلاة فالأولى أن يقال : الشرط كون المنوي عبادة مقصودة أو جزأها وهو لا يحل إلا بالطهارة، فالقراءة جزء من العبادة المقصودة إلا أنه كان جنباً وجد الشرط الأخير وهو عدم حل الفعل إلا بالطهارة فكمل الشرط فجازت الصلاة به، وإن كان عدم الشرط الأخير ولم تجز الصلاة به وخرج التيمم لدخول المسجد مطلقاً، أما إن كان للحدث فظاهر لفوات الشرطين، وأما للجناية فهو وإن وجد الشرط الأخير وهو عدم الحل إلا أنه عدم الشرط الأول وهو كونه عبادة مقصودة أو جزأها. وخرج التيمم لمس المصحف (أو الإسلام) قال في النهر : لا ينبغي عد الإسلام هنا كما وقع في فتح القدير وغيره لأنه يوهم معه يصح ، لكن لا يصلي به كغيره وليس مراد العدم أهليته للنية .اهـ. أقول: سيأتي أنه يصح عند أبي يوسف وإن لم تصح الصلاة به فعده هنا مبني على قوله قوله : (أو خراها) قال في النهر : محدثا أنه
His statement: 'Intending' – meaning he performs tayammum with intention. It is among its conditions...
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage discusses the intention (niyyah) required in tayammum. It states that the intention must be for an act of worship that is not valid without purification (a qurba maqsuda). Various cases are examined: tayammum for janazah prayer or sujood al-tilawah allows performing other prayers because these are qurba maqsuda. Tayammum for entering mosque, reading Quran, touching mushaf, etc., does not permit other prayers because those acts are not qurba maqsuda in the same way. There is a dispute with Abu Yusuf regarding tayammum for embracing Islam. The relied-upon position is that the intention must be for a qurba maqsuda or a part of it that is not halal without purification.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention, which is a condition for tayammum; must be for a qurba maqsuda.
عبادة مقصودة (ʿibādah maqṣūdah): An act of worship that is intended for its own sake and requires purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, which of the following intentions for tayammum would permit the performance of obligatory prayers?
A) Intention to enter the mosque
B) Intention to read the Quran while in a state of minor impurity
C) Intention to perform the funeral prayer
D) Intention to teach someone how to pray

Key Takeaway
Intention in tayammum must be for a qurba maqsuda or a part thereof that is not lawful without purification; this condition determines which acts permit subsequent prayer.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Intention of Purification and Permissibility of Prayer
Introducing the intention rule and qurbah maqsudah concept

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the intention of purification in tayammum suffices for prayer, and identify which acts qualify as qurbah maqsudah.

Core Idea
Tayammum's intention of purification implies permission for prayer only if the intended act is an intentional worship (qurbah maqsudah).

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author clarifies the critical role of intention in tayammum. While the required intention is simply purification, the permissibility of subsequent prayers depends on what that intention was for. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying tayammum in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the required intention
The text states that the intention in tayammum is simply the intention of purification. This suffices because purification is legislated for prayer, so intending purification implicitly intends permission for prayer.
2
Understand qurbah maqsudah
An intentional act of worship (qurbah maqsudah) is an act independently legislated to draw near to Allah, not a subsidiary of another act. Examples: funeral prayer, prostration of recitation.
3
Apply to examples
Tayammum performed for funeral prayer or prostration of recitation permits all prayers because these are qurbah maqsudah.
4
Contrast non-worship acts
Acts like entering the mosque or touching the mushaf are not qurbah maqsudah; tayammum for them does not permit prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التنجيس من أن النية المشروطة في التيمم هي نية التطهير وهو الصحيح فلا ينافيه لتضمنها نية التطهير. وإنما اكتفى بنية التطهير لأن الطهارة شرعت للصلاة وشرطت لإباحتهما فكانت نيتها نية إباحة الصلاة حتى لو تيمم لتعليم الغير لا تجوز به الصلاة في الأصح. كذا في معراج الدراية. فلو تيمم لصلاة الجنازة أو سجدة التلاوة جاز له أن يصلي سائر الصلوات لأن كلاً منهما قربة مقصودة، والمراد بالقربة المقصودة أن لا تجب في ضمن شيء آخر بطريق التبعية، ولا ينافي هذا ما ذكر في الأصول من أن سجدة التلاوة ليست بقربة مقصودة حتى لو تلاها في وقت مكروه جاز أن يؤديها في وقت مكروه آخر بخلاف الصلاة المفروضة إذا وجبت في وقت ناقص لا تؤدّي في ناقص آخر لأن النفي والإثبات ليس من جهة واحدة بل من جهتين. والمراد مما ذكر هنا أنها شرعت ابتداء تقرباً إلى الله تعالى من غير أن تكون تبعاً لغيرها بخلاف دخول المسجد ومس المصحف والمراد بما في الأصول أن هيئة السجود ليست بمقصودة لذاتها عند التلاوة بل لاشتمالها على التواضع المحقق لموافقة أهل الإسلام ومخالفة أهل الطغيان فلهذا قلنا : لا يختص إقامة الواجب بهذه الهيئة بل ينوب الركوع في الصلاة على الفور منابها . كذا في معراج الدراية تبعاً للخبازية. وصرحوا بأنه لو تيمم لدخول المسجد أو القراءة ولو من المصحف أو مسه أو زيارة القبور أو دفن الميت أو الآذان أو الإقامة أو السلام أو ردّه أو الإسلام لا تجوز الصلاة بذلك التيمم عند عامة المشايخ لأن بعضها ليست بعبادة مقصودة، والإسلام وإن كان عبادة مقصودة لكن يصح بدون الطهارة. هكذا أطلقوا في قراءة القرآن المنع ، وفي المحيط : أطلق الجواز وسوى بين صلاة الجنازة وسجدة التلاوة وقراءة القرآن. وفي السراج الوهاج : الأصح أنه لا يجوز له أن يصلي إذا تيمم لقراءة القرآن والحق التفصيل فيها فإن تيمم لها وهو جنب جاز له أن يصلي به سائر الصلوات . كذا في البدائع وغاية البيان. ولم يفصلا في دخول المسجد بين أن يكون جنباً أو محدثاً مع أن كلاً منهما تبع لغيره وهو الصلاة فالأولى أن يقال : الشرط كون المنوي عبادة مقصودة أو جزأها وهو لا يحل إلا بالطهارة، فالقراءة جزء من العبادة المقصودة إلا أنه كان جنباً وجد الشرط الأخير وهو عدم حل الفعل إلا بالطهارة فكمل الشرط فجازت الصلاة به، وإن كان عدم الشرط الأخير ولم تجز الصلاة به وخرج التيمم لدخول المسجد مطلقاً، أما إن كان للحدث فظاهر لفوات الشرطين، وأما للجناية فهو وإن وجد الشرط الأخير وهو عدم الحل إلا أنه عدم الشرط الأول وهو كونه عبادة مقصودة أو جزأها. وخرج التيمم لمس المصحف (أو الإسلام) قال في النهر : لا ينبغي عد الإسلام هنا كما وقع في فتح القدير وغيره لأنه يوهم معه يصح ، لكن لا يصلي به كغيره وليس مراد العدم أهليته للنية .اهـ. أقول: سيأتي أنه يصح عند أبي يوسف وإن لم تصح الصلاة به فعده هنا مبني على قوله قوله : (أو خراها) قال في النهر : محدثاً أن هم. . زعمه لأن مطلقاً فإنه وإن كان لا يحل إلا بها إلا أنه ليس بعبادة مقصودة، ولا يقال إن دخول المسجد عبادة وإن لم يكن للصلاة بل للاعتكاف لأنا نقول : العبادة الاعتكاف ودخول المسجد تبع له فكانت عبادة غير مقصودة. ولو تيمم لسجدة الشكر لا يصلي به المكتوبة، وعند محمد يصليها بناء على بناء على أنها قربة عنده وعندهما ليست بقربة كذا في التوشيح. وفي فتح القدير : فإن قلت ذكرت أن نية التيمم لرد السلام لا تصححه على ظاهر المذهب مع أنه عليه السلام تيمم لرد السلام على ما أسلفته في الأوّل. فالجواب أن قصد رد السلام بالتيمم يستلزم أن يكون نوى عند فعل التيمم التيمم له بل يجوز كونه نوى ما يصح معه التيمم ثم يرد السلام إذا صار طاهراً ! ولقائل أن يمنع عدم صحة التيمم للسلام كما المذهب أن التيمم للسلام ،صحيح، وإنما الكلام في جواز الصلاة به ولهذا قال قاضيخان في فتاواه : ولو تيمم للسلام أو لرده لا يجوز له أداء الصلاة بذلك التيمم ولم يقل لا يجوز تيممه، فعلم أن جواز الصلاة به حكم آخر لا تعلق له بما فعله عليه السلام فإنه تيمم للسلام عند فقد الماء، ولا شك في صحته. قال النووي في شرح مسلم : وهذا الحديث محمول على أنه كان عادماً للماء حال التيمم فإن التيمم مع وجود الماء لا يجوز للقادر على استعماله وعلى أصولنا لا حاجة إلى هذا الحمل فإن عندنا ما يفوت لا إلى خلف يجوز التيمم له مع وجود الماء كصلاة الجنازة ولا شك أن ردّ السلام منه بناء على أنه عليه السلام لا يذكر الله تعالى إلا على طهارة، بل عندنا ما هو أعم من ذلك وهو أن ما ليست الطهارة فعله شرطاً في وحله فإنه يجوز التيمم له مع وجود الماء كدخول المسجد للمحدث، ولهذا قال في المبتغى بالغين المعجمة : ويجوز التيمم لدخول مسجد عند وجود الماء وكذا للنوم فيه ا هـ . اهـ . مع زاده في الضابط لإدخال القراءة ولا حاجة إليه إذ وقوع القراءة جزءاً عبادة من وجه لا ينافي وقوعها عبارة مقصودة من وجه آخر ألا ترى أنهم ادخلوا سجود التلاوة في قولهم عبادة مقصودة أن السجود جزء من العبادة التي هي الصلاة. قوله : ( ولقائل أن يمنع الخ) قال في النهر : هذا ساقط جداً وإني يتخيل ما ذكر مع قوله ذكرت الخ) والذي ذكره أنه لو تيمم للسلام لا تجوز الصلاة به عند عامة المشايخ وحينئذ فيتعين أن يكون لا تصححه أي الصلاة بدليل قوله في ظاهر المذهب لأنه الذي مثلاً فإنه يحل بدون طهارة ويفوت لا إلى خلف و انفراد الأولى في مثل صلاة الجنازة فإنها تفوت لا إلى خلف ولا تحل بدون طهارة، وانفراد الثانية في مثل دخول المسجد للمحدث فإنه يحل بدون طهارة من الحدث الأصغر ولا يصدق عليه أنه يفوت لا إلى خلف قوله : (ولهذا قال في المبتغى (الخ قال في النهر : أنت خبير بأن ما في المبتغى
The impurity from that the intention required in tayammum is the intention of purification, and this is the correct view, so it does not negate it because it includes the intention of purification. They sufficed with the intention of purification because purification was legislated for prayer and was made a condition for permitting them, so its intention is the intention of permitting prayer, such that if he performed tayammum to teach others, prayer is not permissible with it according to the most sound view. Likewise in Mi'raj al-Dirayah. If he performed tayammum for the funeral prayer or the prostration of recitation, it is permissible for him to pray all other prayers because each of them is an intentional act of worship (qurbah maqsudah), and what is meant by intentional act of worship is that it is not obligated within something else by way of being a subsidiary. This does not contradict what is mentioned in the principles that the prostration of recitation is not an intentional act of worship, such that if he recited it in a disliked time, it is permissible to perform it in another disliked time, unlike the obligatory prayer if it becomes due in an imperfect time—it is not performed in another imperfect time, because the negation and affirmation are not from one aspect but from two aspects. What is meant here is that it was legislated as an initial act drawing near to Allah, not being subsidiary to something else, unlike entering the mosque and touching the mushaf. What is meant in the principles is that the form of prostration is not intended for its own sake at the time of recitation, but rather because it includes humility that achieves agreement with the people of Islam and opposition to the people of transgression. For this reason we said: the performance of the obligation is not restricted to this form, rather the bowing in prayer immediately substitutes for it. Likewise in Mi'raj al-Dirayah following al-Khabbaziyyah. They explicitly stated that if he performed tayammum for entering the mosque, or recitation even from the mushaf, or touching it, or visiting graves, or burying the dead, or the call to prayer, or the iqamah, or giving salaam, or returning it, or entering Islam, prayer is not permissible with that tayammum according to the majority of the mashayikh, because some of them are not intentional acts of worship, and although entering Islam is an intentional act of worship, it is valid without purification. Thus they universally prohibited in reading Quran. And in al-Muhit: he universally permitted and made equal between funeral prayer, prostration of recitation, and reading Quran. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: the most correct is that it is not permissible for him to pray if he performed tayammum for recitation of Quran, and the truth requires detail: if he performed tayammum for it while he was junub, it is permissible for him to pray all other prayers with it. Likewise in al-Bada'i' and Ghayat al-Bayan. They did not distinguish in entering the mosque between being junub or having minor impurity, despite each being subsidiary to something else, namely prayer. Better to say: The condition is that the intended act be an intentional act of worship or a part of it, and it is not permissible except with purification. So recitation is a part of the intentional act of worship, but if he was junub, the last condition is met—that the act is not permissible except with purification—so the condition is complete and prayer with it is permissible. If the last condition is not met, prayer with it is not permissible. Tayammum for entering the mosque falls under this absolutely. As for minor impurity, it is obvious due to the absence of both conditions. As for major impurity, although the last condition (impermissibility without purification) is found, the first condition (being an intentional act of worship or part of it) is absent. Tayammum for touching the mushaf (or entering Islam) is excluded. He said in al-Nahr: It is not appropriate to count Islam here as occurred in Fath al-Qadir and others because it gives the impression that it is valid, but he does not pray with it like others, and the meaning is not that he lacks capacity for intention. I say: It will come that it is valid according to Abu Yusuf even if prayer with it is not valid, so its inclusion here is based on his statement. His statement: (or its remnants) He said in al-Nahr: as a person with minor ritual impurity that it is... his claim because absolutely, although it is not permissible except with it, it is not an intentional act of worship. It cannot be said that entering the mosque is worship even if not for prayer but for i'tikaf, because we say: The worship is i'tikaf, and entering the mosque is subsidiary to it, so it is a non-intentional act of worship. If he performed tayammum for the prostration of thankfulness, he does not pray the obligatory prayer with it. According to Muhammad, he prays it based on it being an act of drawing near (qurbah) according to him, whereas according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's position in this context?) it is not a qurbah. Likewise in al-Tawshih. And in Fath al-Qadir: If you say: You mentioned that the intention of tayammum for returning salaam does not render it valid according to the apparent madhhab, despite the fact that he (peace be upon him) performed tayammum for returning salaam as I mentioned earlier. The answer is that intending to return salaam with tayammum necessarily implies that he intended at the time of performing tayammum the tayammum for it, but it is possible that he intended what makes tayammum valid, then returns salaam when he has become pure! And one may object by denying the incorrectness of tayammum for salaam, as the madhhab is that tayammum for salaam is valid, but the discussion is about the permissibility of prayer with it. For this reason, Qadi Khan said in his Fatawa: If he performed tayammum for salaam or returning it, he is not permitted to perform prayer with that tayammum—he did not say his tayammum is not valid. Thus it is known that the permissibility of prayer with it is a separate ruling unrelated to what he (peace be upon him) did, for he performed tayammum for salaam when water was absent, and there is no doubt about its validity. Al-Nawawi said in his commentary on Muslim: This hadith is interpreted as meaning that he was without water at the time of tayammum, because tayammum with the presence of water is not permissible for one able to use it. According to our principles, there is no need for this interpretation because according to us, for something that is missed without a substitute, tayammum is permissible even with the presence of water, like the funeral prayer. There is no doubt that returning salaam from him is based on the fact that he (peace be upon him) does not mention Allah except in a state of purity. Rather, according to us, there is a more general principle: for something for which purification is not a condition for its permissibility, it is permissible to perform tayammum for it even with the presence of water, like entering the mosque for one with minor impurity. For this reason, al-Mubtagha (?) said: It is permissible to perform tayammum for entering the mosque when water is present, and likewise for sleeping in it. End quote. End quote. With his addition in the parameter for including recitation, though it is unnecessary, because the occurrence of recitation as part of worship from one aspect does not negate its occurrence as an intended phrase from another aspect. Do you not see that they included the prostration of recitation in their statement 'intentional act of worship', though the prostration is part of the worship which is prayer. His statement: (And one may object) He said in al-Nahr: This is extremely weak, and how can one imagine what he mentioned with his statement 'you mentioned' and what he mentioned is that if he performed tayammum for salaam, prayer with it is not permissible according to the majority of mashayikh. In that case, it must be that it does not make it valid, i.e., prayer, as evidenced by his statement 'according to the apparent madhhab' because it is the subject of disagreement. I say: The remoteness of this is not hidden, and it is not appropriate for the answer he mentioned in al-Fath after the question. Reflect on his statement: (Rather, according to us, what is more general than that) i.e., more general in one respect, as mentioned by some virtuous scholars, because in the case of returning salaam, both principles come together: it is permissible without purification and it is missed without a substitute. The first principle (intentional worship) applies individually to things like funeral prayer, which is missed without a substitute and is not permissible without purification. The second principle (permissible without purification) applies individually to things like entering the mosque for one with minor impurity, which is permissible without purification from minor ritual impurity and is not described as missed without a substitute. His statement: (And for this reason, al-Mubtagha said) He said in al-Nahr: You are aware that what is in al-Mubtagha
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the intention in tayammum. The author begins by clarifying that the required intention in tayammum is the intention of purification, which is considered sufficient because purification was legislated for prayer. The core issue is whether a tayammum performed for one purpose permits performing other acts of worship, particularly prayers. The ruling: if one performs tayammum with an intention for an act that is an 'intentional act of worship' (qurbah maqsudah), such as funeral prayer or prostration of recitation, then that tayammum permits all prayers. This is because these acts are independently legislated as acts of drawing near to Allah, not as subsidiaries of something else. The passage then lists acts for which tayammum does NOT permit prayer: entering the mosque, reciting Quran (even from mushaf), touching the mushaf, visiting graves, burying the dead, adhan, iqamah, giving or returning salaam, entering Islam. The reasoning is that these are either not intentional acts of worship (like entering mosque) or are valid without purification (like entering Islam). However, there are nuances: for recitation, if the person is in a state of major impurity (junub), the tayammum does permit prayer because recitation is a part of worship and is not permissible without purification for a junub. The author then addresses a potential objection concerning the hadith of the Prophet performing tayammum to return salaam. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the validity of the tayammum itself and the permissibility of prayer with it. The Prophet's tayammum for salaam was valid because it was for an act that is permissible without purification and is missed without substitute, but that does not mean prayer with that tayammum is permissible. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that tayammum for such non-worship acts does not permit prayer. This discussion demonstrates the Hanafi method of ta'lil (identifying the effective cause) and the importance of categorizing acts as 'intentional worship' or not.

Key Terms
نية التطهير (niyyat al-tathir): The intention of purification, which is sufficient in tayammum and implies the intention to permit prayer.
قربة مقصودة (qurbah maqsudah): An act of worship that is intended for its own sake, not as a subsidiary of another act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if a person performs tayammum with the intention of entering the mosque, can he then pray the obligatory prayer with that tayammum?
A) Yes, because entering the mosque is a good deed.
B) No, because entering the mosque is not an intentional act of worship (qurbah maqsudah).
C) Yes, if he is in a state of major impurity (junub).
D) No, because tayammum is only valid for prayer.

Key Takeaway
The intention of purification in tayammum permits prayer only if the intended act is an intentional act of worship (qurbah maqsudah) or part thereof.
